Condition for Valid Delivery in Pledge: Vacating the Property
Ruling on delivery condition in pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid delivery (taslim) of a pledged house and explain why the pledgor's presence invalidates the initial declaration.

Core Idea
Delivery of a pledge requires actual vacating; mere verbal declaration while occupying the property is void.

In the Hanafi school, transfer of possession (qabd) is essential for a pledge to be binding. This lesson examines a key condition: the pledgor must physically vacate the pledged house and then explicitly re-declare delivery. Occupancy, whether by the pledgor or his goods, prevents valid possession, and a fresh delivery is required after removal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the delivery (taslim) of a pledged house. The source states that delivery is valid only if the pledgor (and his goods) are not inside.
This is a condition for validity, not a pillar.
2
Locate the rationale (ta'lil)
The reason given: occupancy (shughl) prevents the pledgee from taking actual possession, so the initial delivery is batil (void).
The Arabic phrase 'لشغلها به' explicitly states the cause.
3
Trace the analogy (qiyas)
The passage analogizes the pledgor's presence to the presence of his goods: both render the initial delivery void, requiring renewal after removal.
This shows the principle applies to any occupancy that impedes the pledgee's control.
4
Apply the consequence
If the pledgor initially declares delivery while inside, it is ineffective. He must leave, then explicitly say 'I have delivered it to you' for valid delivery.
The renewal is a separate act, not a continuation.
5
Note the practical effect
The ruling ensures that the pledgee genuinely obtains exclusive possession (qabd), which is the essence of a binding pledge.
Without this condition, the pledge is incomplete (naqis) and not enforceable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويمنع التسليم كون الراهن أو متاعه في الدار المرهونة حتى إذا رهن داراً وهو فيها وقال سلمتها إليه لا يتم الرهن حتى يقول بعدما خرج من الدار سلمتها إليك لأن التسليم الأول وهو فيها وقع باطلاً لشغلها به، ولا بد من تجديد التسليم بعد الخروج منها كما إذا سلمها ومتاعه فيها
Delivery is prevented by the presence of the pledgor or his goods in the pledged house. So if he pledges a house while he is in it and says 'I have delivered it to him,' the pledge is not complete until after he leaves the house and says 'I have delivered it to you.' Because the first delivery while he is in it was void due to his occupancy. It is necessary to renew delivery after leaving, just as if he delivered it while his goods were in it.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage establishes a condition for valid delivery (تسليم) in a house pledge. The presence of the pledgor or his movable property inside the house prevents actual or constructive possession by the pledgee. If the pledgor says 'I have delivered it' while still inside, it is legally ineffective (باطل) because the house is occupied by the pledgor. Valid delivery requires the pledgor to vacate the premises and then explicitly state that he is delivering possession. The analogy given: if the pledgor's goods are still inside, delivery is similarly defective until the goods are removed and re-delivery occurs. This ruling highlights that the essence of delivery is the transfer of possession (قبض) by emptying the property so that the pledgee can take exclusive control. The Hanafi school emphasizes that mere verbal declaration without actual vacating does not suffice.

Key Terms
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery of possession of the pledged item to the pledgee, which is a condition for the pledge to be binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because he verbally declared delivery
B) No, because he is still inside; he must leave and re-declare delivery
C) It is valid if he intends to deliver
D) It depends on whether the pledgee accepts

Key Takeaway
Valid delivery of a pledged house requires the pledgor to physically vacate and then explicitly re-declare delivery; occupancy invalidates the initial attempt.

Pledge of a Pregnant Animal or Animal with Saddle
Ruling on delivery of a mare with foal or an animal with saddle/bridle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between internal occupants and external dependencies in a pledge and state the Hanafi rule for valid delivery in each case.

Core Idea
The foal blocks delivery; the saddle auto-includes — internal occupants vs. external dependencies in pledge.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq addresses two important cases in the law of pledge (rahn): a pregnant animal and an animal with a saddle. It illustrates how the Hanafi school distinguishes between an internal attachment that occupies the pledged object and an external dependency that is considered a mere appurtenance, each with different consequences for delivery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Identify the two scenarios: (1) a pregnant mare is pledged while carrying a foal; (2) an animal is pledged with a saddle or bridle attached.
The foal is an internal occupant; the saddle is an external dependency.
2
Analyze the ruling for the foal
The foal prevents delivery of the mare because it occupies the animal. Delivery is not valid until the foal is unloaded.
Analogous to goods inside a house: the house must be delivered empty.
3
Contrast the saddle/bridle
If the saddle is not separately pledged, it is automatically included as a dependency (tābiʿ) and delivery of the animal suffices. If the saddle itself is pledged, it must be removed and physically handed over.
Dependencies are like fruits on a tree – they follow the main object.
4
Understand the analogies
The foal case is likened to pledging goods in a container or house: the container/house must be handed over empty. The saddle case is likened to fruit on a palm tree: the fruit is a dependency of the tree.
These analogies clarify the underlying cause (ʿilla).
5
Apply the principle
For any pledge, determine whether an attachment is an internal occupant (requiring removal) or an external dependency (automatically included).
Custom (ʿurf) determines what counts as a dependency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويمنع تسليم الدابة المرهونة الحمل الذي عليها فلا يتم حتى يلقى الحمل بخلاف ما إذا رهن الحمل دونها حتى يكون رهناً إذا دفع الدابة إليه لأن الدار مشغولة فصار كما إذا متاعاً رهن في دار أو في وعاء دون الدار والوعاء بخلاف ما إذا رهن سرجاً على دابة أو الجماماً في رأسها ودفع الدابة مع السرج واللجام حيث لا يكون رهناً حتى ينزعه منها ثم يسلمه إليه لأنه من توابع الدابة بمنزلة الثمرة أحمد للنخل حتى قالوا يدخل في رهن الدابة من غير ذكر
Delivery of the pledged riding animal is prevented by the foal that is on it, so it is not complete until the foal is unloaded. Contrary to when he pledges the foal without the mother, so that it becomes a pledge when he hands over the animal to him, because the house is occupied, so it becomes as if he pledged goods in a house or in a container without the house and the container. Contrary to when he pledges a saddle on an animal or a bridle on its head and hands over the animal with the saddle and bridle, where it is not a pledge until he removes it from it and then hands it over to him, because it is a dependent of the animal, like the fruit for the palm tree, until they said: it enters in the pledge of the animal without mention.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage discusses the impact of attachments on the delivery of a pledged animal. First, the foal (حمل) of a pregnant animal: if the animal is pledged while carrying a foal, delivery is not valid until the foal is unloaded (i.e., removed from the mother). The reason is that the foal occupies the animal and prevents exclusive possession by the pledgee. However, if the foal itself is pledged separately (without the mother), then handing over the animal suffices for delivery of the foal, because the foal is inside the animal like goods inside a container. This is analogous to pledging goods stored in a house—delivery of the house gives possession of the goods. Second, the saddle (سرج) and bridle (لجام): if these are pledged separately while on the animal, delivery is not valid until they are removed from the animal and physically handed over. Why? Because they are considered dependencies (توابع) of the animal—like fruits on a palm tree—so they are automatically included in a pledge of the animal if not mentioned. But if pledged separately, they require separate delivery. The key principle: items that are naturally attached as dependencies do not need separate delivery when the main object is pledged, but if they are the subject of the pledge themselves, they must be physically detached and delivered.

Key Terms
حمل (ḥaml): The foal carried by a pregnant animal; here, it acts as an obstacle to delivery unless removed or separately pledged.
توابع (tawābiʿ): Dependencies or appurtenances of the main object that automatically enter into its pledge without explicit mention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, because the saddle must be removed and separately delivered
B) Yes, because the saddle is a dependency and enters the pledge automatically
C) It is valid only if the price of the saddle is less than that of the horse
D) It is valid only if the saddle is specifically mentioned

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the delivery of a pledged animal is not valid if it carries a foal unless the foal is unloaded, but a saddle is automatically included as a dependency without mention.

Pledge of a Building on Government Land
Fatwa ruling on pledge of building on public land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on pledging a building on government land and identify the condition that makes it invalid.

Core Idea
A pledge requires full ownership and transferable possession; a building on state land fails both.

This fatwa from al-Tatimma addresses a common practical scenario: a person builds a shop or similar structure on land owned by the ruler (state). When the builder pledges that building to a creditor and hands over the keys so the creditor can collect rent, is the pledge valid? The answer is a clear 'no.' Understanding why reveals a fundamental condition of valid pledge contracts in Hanafi fiqh: the pledgor must have complete ownership of the asset and the ability to deliver exclusive possession. The building, not being on owned land, lacks these conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is pledging a building that was built on government (sultan's) land. The fatwa rules that the pledge is invalid (la yasihh) and the rent collected by the pledgee is not permissible (la yatibu).
The ruling is clear: the pledge is batil (void).
2
Extract the implied condition for a valid pledge
A valid pledge (rahn) in Hanafi fiqh requires that the pledgor have full ownership (milk) of the pledged item and the ability to deliver possession (qabd). Since the land belongs to the sultan, the builder only owns the structure, but the structure is physically attached to land he does not own.
Ownership of the building alone does not grant full control over its use or delivery.
3
Apply the condition to the scenario
The builder cannot transfer exclusive possession of the building because the land is not his; the creditor's right to collect rent interferes with the state's interest in the land. Moreover, collecting rent would give the pledgee a return on a loan, resembling riba.
Thus, the contract is invalid from the outset.
4
Conclude the ruling
The pledge is batil; the pledgee must not take the rent. Any rent already taken must be returned or considered unlawful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التتمة سئل علي بن رجل عمر عمارة على أرض السلطان كحانوت أو غيره ورهنه وسلم للمرتهن أخذ الأجرة قال : لا يصح ولا يطيب للمرتهن .
And in al-Tatimma: Ali was asked about a man who built a structure on the sultan's land, like a shop or other, and pledged it, and handed over to the pledgee to take the rent. He said: It is not valid, and it is not permissible (halal) for the pledgee.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This fatwa from Ali (likely Ali b. Ahmad, a Hanafi jurist) addresses the pledge of a building erected on government (sultan's) land. The question: can such a building be pledged and delivered to the creditor to collect rent? The answer is no: the pledge is invalid (لا يصح) and any rent collected by the pledgee would not be permissible (لا يطيب). The reasoning is implied: the builder does not own the land, only the building itself, and the building is not permanently affixed to owned land. Pledge requires the pledgor to own both the property and the right of possession. Since the land is owned by the state, the builder cannot transfer full possession to the pledgee. Moreover, the pledgee taking rent would be akin to usury or unjust enrichment because the pledgee's right is merely a security interest, not ownership. This ruling protects against riba and invalid contracts.

Key Terms
أرض السلطان (arḍ al-sulṭān): Land owned by the ruler (state) that is not privately owned; often used for public or leasehold structures.
رهن (rahn): A pledge or mortgage: a contract where a valuable asset is given as security for a debt.
لا يصح (lā yaṣiḥḥ): It is not valid; the contract is void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The pledge is valid and the creditor may keep the rent
B) The pledge is valid but the creditor must return the rent
C) The pledge is invalid and the creditor cannot collect rent
D) The pledge is valid only if the land is also pledged

Key Takeaway
A pledge on a building constructed on government land is void because the pledgor lacks full ownership and cannot deliver exclusive possession.

Sarf Sale with Pawn Price: Effect of Separation and Destruction
Ruling on a sarf case with a pawned price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of constructive possession in sarf to determine the validity of a currency exchange when the price is pawned and the pawn perishes before or after separation.

Core Idea
In sarf, pawning the price does not transfer possession; only destruction of the pawn within the session constitutes possession, validating the exchange.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq examines a currency exchange (sarf) where the buyer, after taking the dirhams, gives the dinars as a pawn. The ruling hinges on two possible sequences: separation before the pawn is destroyed, or destruction of the pawn before separation. Understanding this case clarifies the Hanafi doctrine that constructive possession can salvage a sarf contract, but only if destruction occurs within the same session.

Guided Path
1
Identify the essential condition of sarf
Recall that a valid currency exchange (sarf) requires hand-to-hand possession (qabd) of both countervalues in the same session. Without this, the contract is fasid (invalid).
This condition is based on the hadith 'al-dhahab bil-dhahab... yadan bi yadin'.
2
Analyze the first scenario: separation before pawn destruction
The buyer took the dirhams and pawned the dinars, then they separated. The pawn is still in the buyer's possession as a security. Since the dinars were not actually possessed, the sale is fasid. The dirhams are held under a defective contract.
The pawn is both a trust (for dinars) and a guarantee (for dirhams).
3
Analyze the second scenario: pawn destruction before separation
If the pawn perishes in the session before separation, it is treated as constructive possession of the dinars. The buyer is deemed to have received the dinars through the pawn's value, so the condition of hand-to-hand possession is fulfilled, making the exchange valid.
This is qabd hukmi (constructive possession).
4
Trace the dual nature of the pawn
The pawn is simultaneously a security for the dinar debt and a guarantee for the dirham substitute. Its destruction triggers different consequences depending on timing. After separation, destruction does not create constructive possession because the session has ended.
If the pawn perishes after separation, the owner claims the dinar value, and the mortgagee claims the dirhams, but the exchange remains invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر مسألة في الصرف : إنسان اشترى ألف درهم بمائة دينار وقبض الألف فأعطاه بالمائة الدينار رهناً يساويها ثم تفرقا فسد البيع لأن الافتراق قبل قبض الدنانير فصارت الدراهم مقبوضة في يد مشتريها بحكم صرف فاسد وليس له أخذ الرهن حتى يرد الألف، فإن هلك الرهن عنده رجع صاحبه عليه بمائة دينار والمرتهن بالألف لأن الدارهم بدل عن الدنانير والرهن بالشيء يكون رهناً به وببدله فيكون محبوساً بالدنانير مضموناً بالدراهم، فإذا هلك الرهن صار مستوفياً للدنانير في صرف فاسد فكان على المرتهن رد الدنانير على الراهن الدارهم فإن لم يتفرقا حتى ضاع الرهن فهو بالمائة الدنانير لأنه صار مستوفياً للدنانير في المجلس حكماً بهلاك الرهن فيصير كما لو استوفى حقيقة فكان الصرف جائزاً.
And he mentioned a question in currency exchange: A person bought one thousand dirhams with one hundred dinars and took possession of the thousand, then gave him as a pawn the one hundred dinars equal to it, then they separated. The sale is invalid because the separation was before taking possession of the dinars, so the dirhams came into the possession of their buyer by virtue of a defective exchange, and he may not take the pawn until he returns the thousand. If the pawn perishes in his possession, his owner claims from him one hundred dinars, and the mortgagee claims the thousand because the dirhams are substitute for the dinars, and the pawn on a thing is a pawn on it and on its substitute, so it is detained for the dinars and guaranteed by the dirhams. So when the pawn perishes, he becomes acquitted of the dinars in a defective exchange, so the mortgagee is obliged to return the dinars to the pledgor, and [the pledgor?] the dirhams. If they did not separate until the pawn was lost, then he is [liable for] the one hundred dinars because he became acquitted of the dinars in the session constructively by the destruction of the pawn, so it is as if he actually acquitted, thus the exchange is valid.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on a specific sarf (currency exchange) scenario. A buyer purchases 1000 dirhams for 100 dinars, takes the dirhams, but instead of paying the dinars, gives them as a pawn. If they separate before the dinars are actually possessed, the sale is invalid because in sarf, possession of both countervalues must occur in the session. The dirhams are now held under a defective contract. The pawn is concurrently detained for the dinars (the debt) and guaranteed by the dirhams (the substitute). If the pawn perishes after separation, the mortgagee is deemed to have received the dinars (through the pawn's value), so the exchange is still invalid, and the buyer must return the dirhams and the seller the dinars (as value of pawn). However, if the pawn perishes before separation, it is treated as constructive possession of the dinars, making the exchange valid.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): Currency exchange contract where both countervalues must be possessed in the session (hands on).
رهن (rahn): Pawn: a contract where an asset is detained as security for a debt.
بدل (badal): Substitute; here, dirhams are the substitute for dinars in the exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sarf case described, if the buyer pawns the price (dinars) and then the pawn perishes after the parties separate, what is the ruling on the exchange?
A) The exchange is valid because the debtor paid through the pawn.
B) The exchange is invalid because the pawn perished after separation, so the seller never actually possessed the price.
C) The exchange is valid because the pawn's destruction in the session counts as possession.
D) The exchange is invalid only if the pawn perishes before separation.

Key Takeaway
In sarf, pawning the price does not count as possession; constructive possession via destruction only validates the exchange if destruction occurs before separation.

Pawn on the Substitute in Sarf or Salam Capital: Constructive Possession Through Destruction
Ruling on pawn as substitute/capital: effect of destruction and separation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a pawn given as the substitute in sarf or the capital in salam: when destruction before separation perfects the contract and when separation before destruction invalidates it.

Core Idea
For sarf and salam capital, pawn destruction in the session is constructive possession perfecting the contract.

In Hanafi fiqh, certain contracts like sarf (currency exchange) and salam (forward sale) require possession of the price or capital in the contract session. This lesson examines a special case: when a pawn is given as that capital or substitute. The ruling hinges on whether the pawn perishes before the parties separate—if so, it counts as possession; otherwise, the contract fails. We will unpack the reasoning and compare with the rule for pawn on the subject matter of salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the pawned item
First, determine whether the pawn is given as the substitute (badal) in a sarf or as the capital (ra's al-mal) in a salam. The ruling applies specifically to these two cases.
2
Apply the session possession requirement
Recall that in sarf and salam, possession of the substitute/capital must occur in the contract session (majlis). The pawn's destruction in the session is treated as constructive possession (qabd hukmi), completing the requirement.
3
Distinguish the timing of destruction
If the pawn perishes before the parties separate, constructive possession is established, and the contract is valid (sahih). If they separate before the pawn perishes, actual possession never occurred, and the contract becomes invalid (batil).
4
Contrast with pawn on muslam fih
Note that when the pawn is the subject matter of salam (muslam fih) rather than the capital, separation does not invalidate the contract because possession of the muslam fih is not required in the session—only at delivery. This distinction highlights the unique treatment of the capital.
5
Confirm the outcome
If the pawn on substitute/capital perishes before separation, the seller is considered to have received the debt (the capital) and the contract is complete. If separated first, no payment is considered received, and the contract is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن هلك صار مستوفياً لوجود القبض واتحاد الجنس من حيث المالية وهو المضمون فيه هذا إذا هلك الرهن قبل الافتراق، وإن افترقا قبل الهلاك بطل الصرف والسلم لفوات القبض حقيقة وحكماً. هذا إذا كان رهناً ببدل الصرف أو برأس مال السلم، وإن كان رهناً بالمسلم فيه لا يبطل بالافتراق لأن قبضه لا يجب في المجلس، ثم إن هلك قبل الافتراق يصير مستوفياً لدينه حكماً فتم السلم كما إذا كان رهناً برأس المال أو بدل الصرف وهلك قبل الافتراق يصير مستوفياً لدينه فتم الصرف والسلم لو تفاسخا السلم وبالمسلم فيه رهن يكون ذلك رهناً برأس المال استحساناً حتى يحبسه به والقياس أن لا يحبسه به لأنه آخر وهو القبض والمسلم فيه وجب بالعقد فلا يكون الرهن بأحدهما رهناً بالآخر كما لو كان عليه دينان دراهم ودنانير وبأحدهما رهن فقضاه الذي به الرهن أو أبرأه منه ليس له حبسه بالدين الآخر وجه الاستحسان أنه ارتهن بحقه الواجب بسبب العقد الذي جرى بينهما وهو المسلم فيه عند عدم الفسخ ورأس المال عند الفسخ فيكون محبوساً به لأنه بدله فقام مقامه إذا الرهن بالشيء يكون رهناً ببدله كما إذا ارتهن بالمغصوب فهلك المغصوب صار رهناً بقيمته ولو هلك الرهن بعد التفاسخ يهلك بالمسلم فيه لأنه رهنه به وإن كان محبوساً بغيره كمن باع عبداً وسلم المبيع وأخذ بالثمن رهناً ثم تقايلا البيع له أن يحبسه لأخذ المبيع لأنه بدل الثمن، ولو هلك المرهون يهلك بالثمن لأنه مرهون به، وكذا لو اشترى عبداً شراء فاسداً وأدى قيمته كان للمشتري أن يحبس المبيع عند الفسخ ليستوفي الثمن، ثم إذا هلك المبيع يهلك بقيمته فكذا .هذا ثم إذا هلك الرهن بالمسلم فيه في مسألتنا يجب على رب السلم أن يدفع مثل المسلم فيه إلى المسلم إليه ويأخذ رأس المال لأن الرهن مضمون وقد بقي حكم الرهن إلى أن يهلك فصار رب المال بهلاك الرهن مستوفياً للمسلم فيه، ولو استوفاه حقيقة ثم تقايلا واستوفاء بعد الإقالة لزمه رد المستوفي واسترداد رأس المال فكذا هنا، وهذا لأن الإقالة في باب السلم لا تحتمل الفسخ بعد ثبوتها فبهلاك الرهن لا تبطل وقد تقدم.
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'So if it perishes, he becomes acquitted due to the existence of possession and unity of type in terms of monetary value, and that is what is guaranteed. This is when the pawn perishes before separation. If they separate before the destruction, the exchange and salam are invalidated because actual and constructive possession are missed. This is when the pawn is for the substitute of exchange or for the capital of salam. But if the pawn is for the thing sold in salam, it is not invalidated by separation because its possession is not required in the session. Then, if it perishes before separation, he becomes constructively acquitted of his debt, so the salam is perfected, just as if the pawn were for the capital or the substitute of exchange and perished before separation, he becomes acquitted of his debt, so the exchange or salam is perfected. If they rescind the salam and there is a pawn on the thing sold, that pawn becomes a pawn on the capital by istihsan, so that he may detain it by it. The qiyas is that he may not detain it by it because it is a different matter... and the wajh al-istihsan is that he pawned for his right owed due to the contract between them, which is the thing sold in case of no rescission and the capital in case of rescission, so it is detained by it because it is its substitute...'
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage expands on the previous ruling, distinguishing between pawns on the substitute (badal) in sarf or the capital in salam versus pawns on the subject matter (muslam fih) of salam. The key is that in sarf and salam capital, possession must occur in the session, so if the pawn perishes before separation, constructive possession perfects the contract. But for the muslam fih in salam, possession is not required in the session, so separation does not invalidate. The passage then discusses what happens if the parties rescind the salam: the pawn on the muslam fih becomes a pawn on the capital by istihsan, even though qiyas would not allow it. The istihsan reasoning is that the pawn is for the right arising from the contract, which is the muslam fih before rescission and the capital after rescission. If the pawn perishes after rescission, it is considered as perishing for the muslam fih, so the seller must deliver the muslam fih and take back the capital.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where capital is paid in advance for a deferred commodity (muslam fih).
قبض حكمي (qabd hukmi): Constructive possession, e.g., through destruction of pawn in the session.
بدل الصرف (badal al-sarf): The substitute in a currency exchange (sarf) contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a salam contract, if the capital is pawned and the pawn perishes after the parties separate, what is the ruling?
A) The salam is valid because the capital was secured by pawn.
B) The salam is invalid because constructive possession did not occur in the session.
C) The salam is valid only if the muslam fih is also pawned.
D) The salam becomes a loan.

Key Takeaway
For a pawn given as the substitute in sarf or capital in salam, its destruction in the session before separation constitutes constructive possession, perfecting the contract; separation before destruction invalidates it.

Pawn on the Subject Matter (Muslam Fih) of Salam: Effects of Rescission and Istihsan
Subsidiary ruling on pawn after rescission of salam: istihsan vs. qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that when a salam contract is rescinded, a pawn originally given on the muslam fih becomes a pawn on the capital by istihsan, and describe the consequences if it perishes after rescission.

Core Idea
After rescission, pawn on muslam fih becomes pawn on capital by istihsan, overriding qiyas.

This lesson continues from the previous one but focuses on a special scenario: when the parties rescind (tafakhus) a salam contract and there is a pawn on the subject matter (muslam fih). According to qiyas (analogy), the pawn should not be transferable to the capital, but Hanafi jurists apply istihsan (juristic preference) to treat it as a pawn on the capital, allowing the pawn to be detained for the capital. We will explore the reasoning and the consequences if the pawn perishes after rescission.

Guided Path
1
Understand the starting scenario
A salam contract exists with a pawn given on the muslam fih (the deferred commodity). The parties then rescind the contract. The question: does the pawn now serve as security for the capital (which must be returned)?
2
Identify the qiyas ruling
Qiyas says the pawn does not transfer to the capital because the capital was not the original debt; the muslam fih was. The pawn was specific to the muslam fih. After rescission, the right changes to the capital, but the pawn is a separate security and should not automatically attach to a different debt.
The text gives an analogy: if someone owes two debts and pawns for one, paying off that debt does not allow detaining the pawn for the other debt.
3
Apply the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan overrides qiyas because the pawn was given for the right arising from the contract. Before rescission, that right is the muslam fih; after rescission, it becomes the capital (the substitute). Since the pawn was for the contract right, it automatically transfers to the substitute (the capital). This is supported by the principle that a pawn on a thing is also a pawn on its substitute.
The text provides an example: if a stolen item is pawned, then the stolen item perishes, the pawn becomes on the value (substitute).
4
Determine the consequence of the pawn perishing after rescission
If the pawn perishes after rescission, it is considered to have been in security for the muslam fih (the original debt) until destruction, so the seller (the one who gave the pawn) must deliver the muslam fih and take back the capital. This mirrors the rule if they had actually received the muslam fih and then rescinded.
5
Note the overall outcome
The ruling shows how istihsan allows flexibility in contractual rights, ensuring that the pawn continues to secure the obligation even after a fundamental change in the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (فإن هلك صار مستوفياً لوجود القبض واتحاد الجنس من حيث المالية وهو المضمون فيه هذا إذا هلك الرهن قبل الافتراق، وإن افترقا قبل الهلاك بطل الصرف والسلم لفوات القبض حقيقة وحكماً. هذا إذا كان رهناً ببدل الصرف أو برأس مال السلم، وإن كان رهناً بالمسلم فيه لا يبطل بالافتراق لأن قبضه لا يجب في المجلس، ثم إن هلك قبل الافتراق يصير مستوفياً لدينه حكماً فتم السلم كما إذا كان رهناً برأس المال أو بدل الصرف وهلك قبل الافتراق يصير مستوفياً لدينه فتم الصرف والسلم لو تفاسخا السلم وبالمسلم فيه رهن يكون ذلك رهناً برأس المال استحساناً حتى يحبسه به والقياس أن لا يحبسه به لأنه آخر وهو القبض والمسلم فيه وجب بالعقد فلا يكون الرهن بأحدهما رهناً بالآخر كما لو كان عليه دينان دراهم ودنانير وبأحدهما رهن فقضاه الذي به الرهن أو أبرأه منه ليس له حبسه بالدين الآخر وجه الاستحسان أنه ارتهن بحقه الواجب بسبب العقد الذي جرى بينهما وهو المسلم فيه عند عدم الفسخ ورأس المال عند الفسخ فيكون محبوساً به لأنه بدله فقام مقامه إذا الرهن بالشيء يكون رهناً ببدله كما إذا ارتهن بالمغصوب فهلك المغصوب صار رهناً بقيمته ولو هلك الرهن بعد التفاسخ يهلك بالمسلم فيه لأنه رهنه به وإن كان محبوساً بغيره كمن باع عبداً وسلم المبيع وأخذ بالثمن رهناً ثم تقايلا البيع له أن يحبسه لأخذ المبيع لأنه بدل الثمن، ولو هلك المرهون يهلك بالثمن لأنه مرهون به، وكذا لو اشترى عبداً شراء فاسداً وأدى قيمته كان للمشتري أن يحبس المبيع عند الفسخ ليستوفي الثمن، ثم إذا هلك المبيع يهلك بقيمته فكذا .هذا ثم إذا هلك الرهن بالمسلم فيه في مسألتنا يجب على رب السلم أن يدفع مثل المسلم فيه إلى المسلم إليه ويأخذ رأس المال لأن الرهن مضمون وقد بقي حكم الرهن إلى أن يهلك فصار رب المال بهلاك الرهن مستوفياً للمسلم فيه، ولو استوفاه حقيقة ثم تقايلا واستوفاء بعد الإقالة لزمه رد المستوفي واسترداد رأس المال فكذا هنا، وهذا لأن الإقالة في باب السلم لا تحتمل الفسخ بعد ثبوتها فبهلاك الرهن لا تبطل وقد تقدم.
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'So if it perishes, he becomes acquitted due to the existence of possession and unity of type in terms of monetary value, and that is what is guaranteed. This is when the pawn perishes before separation. If they separate before the destruction, the exchange and salam are invalidated because actual and constructive possession are missed. This is when the pawn is for the substitute of exchange or for the capital of salam. But if the pawn is for the thing sold in salam, it is not invalidated by separation because its possession is not required in the session. Then, if it perishes before separation, he becomes constructively acquitted of his debt, so the salam is perfected, just as if the pawn were for the capital or the substitute of exchange and perished before separation, he becomes acquitted of his debt, so the exchange or salam is perfected. Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference overriding analogy for a more equitable outcome.
تفاسخ (tafākhus): Mutual rescission of a contract, also called iqala.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
When a salam contract is rescinded, a pawn on the muslam fih becomes a pawn on the capital by istihsan; if it perishes after rescission, the pawner must deliver the muslam fih and retrieve the capital.

Sale with Condition of Pledge: Buyer's Refusal and Seller's Options
Ruling on sale with pledge condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale conditioned on a specific pledge, explain the role of istihsan, and compare the majority view with Zufar's opinion.

Core Idea
A condition of pledge in a sale is valid but not enforceable; the seller may rescind if the buyer refuses.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary addresses a common scenario in sale contracts: can a seller require the buyer to pledge a specific item as security for the price? The default analogy would invalidate such a condition, but Hanafi jurists apply the principle of istihsan to permit it, with important limits on enforcement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling from the Matn
Read the first line: if a seller sells on condition that the buyer pledges a specific item, and the buyer refuses, the buyer is not compelled and the seller has the option to rescind, unless the buyer pays the price immediately or pledges the value.
The matn gives the practical outcome: no compulsion, but an option for the seller.
2
Understand Qiyas vs Istihsan
By strict qiyas, such a condition would invalidate the sale because it is a condition not required by the contract, benefits one party, and resembles two transactions in one. However, the author applies istihsan (juristic preference) to validate it based on compatibility.
The passage explicitly states: 'This is istihsan, and by qiyas this sale with this condition is not valid.'
3
Trace the Istihsan Reasoning
The istihsan argument: a pledge is for security, which is compatible with a sale contract (since both aim to secure payment). Similarly for suretyship. Thus the condition is considered compatible, and the sale is valid under istihsan.
The text says: 'the face of istihsan is that it is a condition compatible with the contract, because the pledge is for security.'
4
Analyze the Dispute with Zufar
Zufar argues that the buyer should be compelled to hand over the pledge because the condition creates a right (like agency). The commentator refutes this: a pledge is a gratuitous contract (tabarru'), and one cannot be forced to perform a voluntary act.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; the majority view (Abu Hanifa and the two companions) is that there is no compulsion.
5
Apply the Rule to Analogous Cases
The passage also covers suretyship: if a surety is present in the session and accepts, the sale is valid; if absent, the sale becomes corrupt unless the surety comes and accepts within the session. Similarly, if the pledge is unspecified, the sale becomes corrupt unless specified in the session.
The key condition: the pledge or surety must be specific and present during the contract session.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومن باع عبدا على أن يرهن المشتري بالثمن شيئاً بعينيه فامتنع لم يجبر وللبائع فسخ البيع إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالا أو قيمة الرهن رهنا) وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا يجوز هذا البيع بهذا الشرط وعلى هذا القياس والاستحسان إذا باعه شيئاً على أن يعطيه كفيلاً حاضراً في المجلس فقبل الكفيل لأنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد وفيه منفعة لأحدهما ومثله مفسد للبيع ولأنه صفقة في صفقتين وهو منهي عنه . وجه الاستحسان أنه شرط ملائم للعقد لأن الرهن للاستيثاق وكذا الكفالة والاستيثاق يلائم العقد، فإذا كان الكفيل حاضراً في المجلس وقبل اعتبر فيه المعنى وهو الملايمة فصح العقد وإذا لم يكن الرهن ولا الكفيل معيناً أو كان الكفيل غائباً حتى افترقا لم يبقى معنى للجهالة فكان الاعتبار لعينه فيفسد. ولو كان الكفيل غائباً فحضر في المجلس وقبل ج. وكذا صح . لو لم يكن الرهن معيناً فاتفقا على تعيين الرهن في المجلس أو نقد المشتري الثمن حالاً جاز البيع وبعد المجلس لا يجوز . قوله «فامتنع لم يجبر» أي امتنع المشتري عن تسليم الرهن لم يجبر على تسليمه. وقال زفر رحمه الله تعالى : يجبر لأنه صار بالشرط حقاً . من حقوقه كالوكالة المشروطة في عقد الرهن . قلت : عقد الرهن تبرع ولا جبر على المتبرع كالواهب غير أن للبائع الخيار إن شاء رضي بترك الرهن وإن شاء فسخ البيع لأنه وصف مرغوب فيه فواته يوجب الخيار كسلامة المبيع عن العيب في البيع إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالاً لحصول المقصود أو يدفع قيمة الرهن رهناً
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And whoever sells a slave on the condition that the buyer pledges a specific thing for the price, and he refuses, he is not compelled, and the seller has the option to rescind the sale, unless the buyer pays the price immediately or pledges the value of the pledge). This is istihsan, and by qiyas this sale with this condition is not valid. And upon this qiyas and istihsan, if he sells something to him on condition that he gives him a surety present in the session, and he accepts the surety, because it is a condition not required by the contract and it contains a benefit for one of them, and the like corrupts the sale, and because it is a transaction in two transactions, which is prohibited. The face of istihsan is that it is a condition that is compatible with the contract, because the pledge is for security, and similarly suretyship, and security is compatible with the contract. Thus, if the surety is present in the session and accepts, the meaning is considered, which is compatibility, so the contract is valid. If neither the pledge nor the surety is specific, or the surety is absent until they separate, there is no meaning to ignorance, so the consideration is for its essence, and it becomes corrupt. If the surety was absent and then came to the session and accepted, it is valid. Similarly, if the pledge was not specific and they agreed on specifying the pledge in the session, or the buyer paid the price immediately, the sale is valid; after the session, it is not valid. His statement: 'if he refuses, he is not compelled' means the buyer refuses to hand over the pledge, he is not compelled to hand it over. Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, said: He is compelled because it becomes a right by the condition, from his rights, like the conditional agency in the contract of pledge. I say: The contract of pledge is a gratuitous contract, and there is no compulsion on a gratuitous donor, like the donor, except that the seller has the option: if he wishes, he may accept leaving the pledge, and if he wishes, he may rescind the sale, because it is a desirable description, its loss gives an option, like the soundness of the sold item from defect in the sale, unless the buyer pays the price immediately to achieve the purpose, or pays the value of the pledge as a pledge.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, expanded by the commentator. It discusses a sale where the seller stipulates that the buyer pledges a specific item for the price. The default ruling (qiyas) would invalidate such a condition because it is not part of the original contract and resembles two transactions in one. However, the author applies istihsan (juristic preference) to validate it, reasoning that the condition of a pledge is compatible with the contract since both aim for security. The key practical outcome: if the buyer refuses to hand over the specified pledge, he is not forced to do so (because a pledge is a gratuitous contract and cannot be compelled). Instead, the seller gets an option to either accept the sale without the pledge or rescind the sale. An exception: if the buyer pays the price immediately or pledges an amount equal to the value of the specified item, the seller must accept. The passage also compares to the case of a surety (kafalah), where a similar rule applies: if the surety is present and accepts in the session, the contract is valid; otherwise it becomes corrupt. Imam Zufar disagrees on the compulsion issue, arguing the buyer must be compelled because the pledge condition creates a right. The commentator refutes this, noting that a pledge is a voluntary (tabarru') contract, and one cannot be forced to perform a voluntary act. This discussion highlights the Hanafi distinction between binding conditions and non-binding gratuitous acts.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more suitable result.
كفالة (kafālah): Suretyship; guaranteeing payment or presence of a person.
تبرع (tabarru'): Gratuitous act; voluntary without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a buyer refuses to hand over the specifically pledged item after agreeing to a sale conditioned on that pledge?
A) The buyer is compelled to hand it over
B) The seller may rescind the sale unless the buyer pays the price or pledges the value
C) The sale becomes void automatically
D) The seller must accept another item of equal value

Key Takeaway
A sale conditioned on a specific pledge is valid via istihsan, but the buyer cannot be compelled to pledge; the seller's recourse is to rescind unless the buyer pays or substitutes value.

Sale with Condition to Pawn: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Explaining the ruling of a sale conditioned on pawning and its istihsan basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale conditioned on pawning, explain the istihsan basis, and distinguish between the majority Hanafi position and Zufar's opinion.

Core Idea
A sale with a condition to pawn is valid by istihsan, but the buyer cannot be forced to pawn; the seller has the option to rescind.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a nuanced ruling in Hanafi sales law. While qiyas would invalidate a sale conditioned on pawning because it resembles a prohibited transaction within a transaction, the Hanafi school validates it through istihsan, arguing that the condition is suitable (mulaim) for the contract's purpose of security. The passage also clarifies that the buyer is not compelled to deliver the pawn, and the seller's remedy is an option to rescind unless the buyer provides immediate payment or an equivalent pawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is selling a slave on condition that the buyer pawns a specific thing for the price. The Hanafi ruling: the sale is valid by istihsan, but the buyer is not compelled to pawn.
2
Locate the two proofs: qiyas and istihsan
The author states that qiyas would invalidate the sale (due to condition not required, benefit to one party, resembling bay'atan fi bay'a), but istihsan validates it. Understand the reasoning behind each.
3
Trace the istihsan reasoning
The key term is mulaim (suitable). The condition of pawning or suretyship is suitable because both aim at security, which is consistent with a credit sale. This suitability overrides the strict qiyas.
Istihsan is a departure from qiyas for a stronger reason.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar
Zufar argued the buyer is compelled because the condition creates a right similar to a stated agency. The majority response: pawning is tabarru' (gratuitous), and no one is forced into a gratuitous contract. Instead, the seller has an option to rescind.
Zufar's view is a minority within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: under Zufar, the buyer is forced; under the majority, the seller simply has the option. The mufta bihi is the majority view: the buyer is not compelled, and the seller may rescind unless the buyer pays or provides an alternative pawn.

قال رحمه الله : (ومن باع عبدا على أن يرهن المشتري بالثمن شيئاً بعينيه فامتنع لم يجبر وللبائع فسخ البيع إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالا أو قيمة الرهن رهنا) وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا يجوز هذا البيع بهذا الشرط وعلى هذا القياس والاستحسان إذا باعه شيئاً على أن يعطيه كفيلاً حاضراً في المجلس فقبل الكفيل لأنه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد وفيه منفعة لأحدهما ومثله مفسد للبيع ولأنه صفقة في صفقتين وهو منهي عنه . وجه الاستحسان أنه شرط ملائم للعقد لأن الرهن للاستيثاق وكذا الكفالة والاستيثاق يلائم العقد، فإذا كان الكفيل حاضراً في المجلس وقبل اعتبر فيه المعنى وهو الملايمة فصح العقد وإذا لم يكن الرهن ولا الكفيل معيناً أو كان الكفيل غائباً حتى افترقا لم يبقى معنى للجهالة فكان الاعتبار لعينه فيفسد. ولو كان الكفيل غائباً فحضر في المجلس وقبل ج. وكذا صح . لو لم يكن الرهن معيناً فاتفقا على تعيين الرهن في المجلس أو نقد المشتري الثمن حالاً جاز البيع وبعد المجلس لا يجوز . قوله «فامتنع لم يجبر» أي امتنع المشتري عن تسليم الرهن لم يجبر على تسليمه. وقال زفر رحمه الله تعالى : يجبر لأنه صار بالشرط حقاً . من حقوقه كالوكالة المشروطة في عقد الرهن . قلت : عقد الرهن تبرع ولا جبر على المتبرع كالواهب غير أن للبائع الخيار إن شاء رضي بترك الرهن وإن شاء فسخ البيع لأنه وصف مرغوب فيه فواته يوجب الخيار كسلامة المبيع عن العيب في البيع إلا أن يدفع المشتري الثمن حالاً لحصول المقصود أو يدفع قيمة الرهن رهناً الكفالة والرهن
He (the author) said, may God have mercy on him: (And whoever sells a slave on the condition that the buyer pawns a specific thing for the price, and then the buyer refuses, he is not compelled, and the seller has the option to rescind the sale unless the buyer pays the price immediately or gives the value of the pawn as a pawn.) This is istihsan, and by qiyas this sale with this condition is not permissible. And according to this qiyas and istihsan, if someone sells something on the condition that the buyer gives a surety present in the session, and the surety accepts, it is because it is a condition not required by the contract and contains benefit for one of them, and such a thing invalidates the sale, and because it is a transaction within a transaction, which is prohibited. The basis of istihsan is that it is a condition suitable for the contract because pawning is for security, and similarly suretyship, and security suits the contract. So if the surety is present in the session and accepts, the meaning (suitability) is considered and the contract is valid. But if neither the pawn nor the surety is specified, or if the surety is absent until they separate, there remains no meaning to ignorance, so consideration is given to the wording and it is invalid. And if the surety is absent but then attends the session and accepts, it [؟] is valid. Similarly if the pawn is unspecified and they agree on its specification in the session, or if the buyer pays the price immediately, the sale is valid; after the session it is not valid. His statement: 'He is not compelled' means if the buyer refuses to hand over the pawn, he is not compelled to hand it over. Zufar, may God have mercy on him, said: He is compelled because it has become a right among his rights, like the agency stated in a pledge contract. I say: The pledge contract is a gratuitous contract, and one is not compelled in a gratuitous contract, like a donor. However, the seller has the option: if he wishes he may accept the abandonment of the pawn, and if he wishes he may rescind the sale, because it is a desired attribute, its loss gives an option, like the soundness of the sold item from defect in a sale, unless the buyer pays the price immediately to achieve the purpose, or gives the value of the pawn as a pawn. Suretyship and pawning.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a sale conditioned on pawning. The matn itself is quoted at the beginning in parentheses. The commentator begins by stating that the ruling of the matn is based on istihsan (juristic preference), whereas qiyas (analogy) would invalidate such a sale because the condition is not required by the contract and provides benefit to one party, which typically corrupts the sale. The istihsan justification is that the condition of pawning (or suretyship) is 'suitable' (mulaim) for the contract because the purpose of both pawning and suretyship is to secure the debt, and security is consistent with the nature of a sale on credit. The commentator then clarifies details: if the surety is present and accepts, the sale is valid; if the pawn or surety is unspecified or the surety is absent until the parties separate, the sale is invalid due to uncertainty. However, if the missing specification or presence is rectified in the same session, it is valid. After this, the commentator explains the matn's phrase 'he is not compelled': the buyer who agreed to pawn cannot be forced to do so. Zufar disagreed, analogizing to a stated agency in a pledge contract, where the agent is compelled. The commentator refutes this by noting that pawning is a gratuitous contract (tabarru'), akin to a gift, and no one can be forced to give a gift. Instead, the seller has the option to rescind the sale if the benefit of the pawn is lost, analogous to the option for a defect in the sold item. This option is negated if the buyer pays the price immediately or gives the value of the pawn as a pawn, fulfilling the purpose of security. The passage concludes with the heading 'الكفالة والرهن' (suretyship and pawning) which may introduce the next topic.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): The passage defines istihsan as the basis for validating the sale with a condition to pawn, overriding the qiyas that would invalidate it.
تبرع (tabarru'): The passage describes pawning (رهن) as a gratuitous contract (tabarru'), meaning it is a voluntary act without compulsion.
ملائم (mulaim): The condition of pawning or suretyship is described as 'suitable' (ملائم) for the sale contract because it serves the purpose of security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a buyer refuses to deliver the pawn as agreed in a sale?
A) The buyer is forced by the court to deliver the pawn.
B) The seller automatically wins the right to cancel the sale.
C) The seller has the option to rescind the sale unless the buyer pays the price or gives the value as pawn.
D) The sale becomes void immediately.

Key Takeaway
A sale with a condition to pawn is valid by istihsan, but the buyer cannot be forced to pawn; the seller's recourse is an option to rescind unless the purpose is fulfilled by other means.

Ruling on 'Hold This Cloth Until I Give You the Price' as a Pawn and Related Disputes
Explaining the Hanafi ruling and intra-madhhab dispute on ambiguous retention statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa classifies the ambiguous statement 'hold this until I pay' as a pawn rather than a deposit, and apply the principle that contracts are interpreted by their meanings to analogous scenarios.

Core Idea
Context over literal wording: an ambiguous 'hold' becomes a pawn when linked to securing a debt.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over a common transactional statement: when a buyer tells the seller 'hold this cloth until I give you the price,' is it a pawn (رهن) or a deposit (وديعة)? The answer determines whether the seller has a security interest in the cloth. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, explains the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar, then supports Abu Hanifa's view using the fundamental Hanafi principle that contracts are interpreted according to their intended meanings (العبرة في العقود للمعاني). We will dissect each argument and see how this principle applies to various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the Hanafi position
Identify the legal question: does an ambiguous statement 'hold this until I pay' create a pawn or a deposit? State Abu Hanifa's ruling that it is a valid pawn.
This is the mufta bihi position, as per the matn and later tarjih.
2
Identify the opponent's argument
Analyze the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Zufar: the word 'hold' (امسك) is ambiguous, and the default should be the lesser obligation (deposit) because it involves lower risk.
They rely on the principle of acting with certainty when ambiguity exists.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Examine Abu Hanifa's dalil: the context of retention until payment of the price clearly indicates the meaning of pawn. Contracts are interpreted by their purposes (العبرة في العقود للمعاني).
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the purpose of the statement, not its literal wording.
4
Determine the practical difference
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: if considered a pawn, the seller holds the item as security and can sell it upon default; if a deposit, the seller is merely a trustee with no special rights.
This difference has significant implications for liability and enforcement.
5
Apply to subsidiary scenarios
Work through the additional cases in the passage: before vs. after possession, perishable goods, explicit mention of 'pawn,' and pawning multiple items without specifying shares.
Each scenario tests the boundaries of the principle.

يكون رهناً، ومثله عن أبي يوسف لأن قوله «امسك ويحتمل الرهن ويحتمل الايداع والثاني أقلهما فيقضي بثبوته بخلاف ما إذا قال امسكه بدينك أو بمالك علي لأنه لما قابله بالدين فقد عين الرهن ولنا أنه أتى بما ينيء The cloth until I give you the price, then it is a pawn. And if he pawns two slaves for a thousand, he may not take one for his share because the purpose of the conditional pawn is achieved by its value. He (the author), may God have mercy on him, said: (And if he says to the seller: 'Hold this cloth until I give you the price,' then it is a pawn.) And Zufar said: It is not a pawn, and similar is reported from Abu Yusuf, because his saying 'hold' is ambiguous: it could mean a pawn or a deposit, and the second (deposit) is the lesser (burden) so it is established, unlike if he said 'hold it for your debt' or 'for what you have against me' because when he linked it to the debt, he specified the pawn. Our argument is that he expressed what indicates the meaning of pawn, which is retention until payment of the price, and consideration in contracts is for meanings, so much so that a suretyship with a condition of the original debtor's discharge becomes a transfer (hawala), and a transfer with a condition of the transferor's non-discharge becomes a suretyship. Do you not see that if he said 'I give you ownership of this for such-and-such,' it is a sale because he explicitly stated the effect of a sale, as if he said 'I sold it to you for such-and-such.' And he used the word 'this' unconditionally, which includes both the sold cloth and other, there being no difference whether that cloth is the purchased one or not, provided it is after possession, because the sold item after possession is suitable to be a pawn for its price, so the ruling of pawn is established in it, unlike before possession because it is held for the price and its guarantee is unlike the guarantee of pawn, so it is not subject to two different guarantees due to the impossibility of their combination. So if he said to him 'hold the sold item until I give you the price' before possession, and it perishes, the sale is rescinded. And if the sold item is something that spoils by being kept, like meat and ice, and the buyer delays and the seller fears its loss, it is permissible for the seller to sell it, and it is permissible for the buyer to buy it, and the seller gives charity for the excess if he sells it for more than the first price because there is a doubt in it. And in al-Muntaqa: A man had a right against another man, then he gave him a cloth and said: 'Hold this until I give you what you have against me.' Abu Hanifa, may God have mercy on him, said: It is a pawn because he came with the meaning of pawn, which is retention and detention for the purpose of paying the debt and giving it. And Abu Yusuf, may God have mercy on him, said: It is a deposit, not a pawn, because retention is ambiguous: it could be for pawn or for deposit, so it is interpreted as a deposit because it is the lesser (burden) and it is certain, while pawn is doubtful. So if he said 'hold this for your property' or 'hold this as a pawn until my property,' then it is a pawn by consensus. And if he said 'hold these thousand for your right and witness for me the taking of possession,' then this is a collection (iqtida') because taking and receiving for a debt is only for collection and recovery. And if he said 'hold them until I bring you your right,' then it is a pawn because he ordered retention for payment, which is only for pawn. And if the debtor paid him one hundred then said 'take it as a pawn for what was in it of counterfeit or defective coins,' then it is a pawn for the defective (satuq) not the counterfeit (zuyuf), because counterfeit are used for collection, while defective are not. A man pawned goods to another for a thousand dirhams, then the pledgee said to the pledgor: 'Give it to me,' and the pledgor said 'Pawn it to me for your property,' and he pawned it for nine hundred, the first pawn is dissolved and the second is concluded. So likewise this is as if he bought it for a thousand then sold it for seven hundred, the first is dissolved and the second concluded. He (the author), may God have mercy on him, said: (And if he pawns two slaves for a thousand, he may not take one for his share, like a sale. He restricted it with 'for a thousand' to indicate that he did not specify the share of each. So if he specified for each something of the debt for which he pawned them, the answer is the same in the original narration because the contract is single and is not divided by specification, like a sale.)
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on multiple matn statements from Kanz al-Daqa'iq concerning the classification of ambiguous statements as pawns (رهن) and related issues. The first matn states that if someone says to the seller 'Hold this cloth until I give you the price,' it constitutes a valid pawn. This ruling is disputed: Zufar and Abu Yusuf argue that the word 'hold' (امسك) is ambiguous between pawn and deposit (وديعة), and since deposit is the lesser obligation and more certain, the statement should be interpreted as a deposit. Abu Hanifa, however, holds that the context of retention until payment of price clearly indicates the meaning of pawn, as the purpose is to secure the debt. The commentator supports Abu Hanifa by citing the principle that contracts are interpreted by their meanings rather than literal words, giving examples of suretyship (كفالة) becoming transfer (حوالة) and vice versa when conditions change. The commentary then addresses various specific scenarios: if the item is sold and the request to hold is made before possession, it cannot be a pawn because the item is already held for the price with a different guarantee; if the item is perishable, the seller can sell it and give charity for excess profit due to doubt. Additional rulings from al-Muntaqa illustrate the same dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on whether 'Hold this until I give you your due' is a pawn or deposit. Consensus exists when the word 'pawn' is explicitly used. Other cases include collection (اقتضاء) and the effect of specifying or not specifying shares in a pawn of multiple items. The final matn discusses pawning two slaves for a single sum, where the pledgee cannot release one for part of the debt; even if shares are mentioned, the contract remains indivisible, like a sale.

Key Terms
امسك (imsak): In this context, 'hold' is an ambiguous term that could mean pawn or deposit. The dispute centers on its interpretation based on context.
وديعة (wadi'ah): A deposit (trust) where the holder is not responsible for loss unless negligent. Abu Yusuf and Zufar interpret the statement as a deposit rather than a pawn.
العبرة في العقود للمعاني (al-ibrah fi al-uqud lil-ma'ani): The principle that contracts are interpreted according to their intended meanings, not just literal wording, used by Abu Hanifa to justify the pawn interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, if a buyer says to the seller after taking possession, 'Hold this cloth until I give you the price,' what is the legal status?
A) It is a deposit (وديعة).
B) It is a pawn (رهن).
C) It is a sale (بيع).
D) It is a gift (هبة).

Key Takeaway
A statement of retention linked to debt payment is validly interpreted as a pawn, not a deposit, because contracts are judged by their intended meanings.

Ruling on Pawning One Item to Two Creditors
Ruling with comparative analysis against sale and gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pawning one item to two creditors and explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes pawn from sale and gift.

Core Idea
A pawned item can be held fully by two creditors because pawn creates detention, not ownership.

When a single item is pawned to two creditors, a natural question arises: must the item be split, or can each creditor hold the entire item? The Hanafi school rules that the entire item becomes a pledge for each creditor's full debt. This ruling is based on a careful distinction between pawn (rahn) and contracts of sale or gift, which transfer ownership. In this lesson, we will examine the Hanafi position, the opposing objection, and the reasoning that secures the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: if a person pawns an item to two creditors, the contract is valid and the entire item becomes a pledge for each creditor's full debt.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi.
2
Identify the opposing view and its analogy
Some scholars object by analogy: in sale or gift to two people, the item becomes shared (shayi') because ownership cannot be held completely by two. They argue the same should apply to pawn.
This analogy is based on the contract being attached to one item in a single transaction.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes pawn from sale/gift: pawn does not transfer ownership, only detention (ihtibas). Detention can be established completely for multiple parties simultaneously, unlike ownership.
Thus, the analogy fails and the pawn is not divided.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the Hanafi view, each creditor can hold the entire pawn until his debt is paid, and they may take turns in possession. Under the opposing view, each would hold a half or proportionate share.
This affects enforcement and priority in case of default.
5
Note the tarjih
The Hanafi view is preferred (al-asahh) and is the basis for fatwa, as stated by authorities like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
A condition is added: if debts are specified without total, the pawn is invalid.

ولو رهن عينا عند رجلين صح والمضمون على حصة دينه فإن قضى دين ... الزيادات له أن يقبض أحدهما إذا أدى ما سمى له لأن التفرق يثبت في الرهن بتسمية حصة كل واحد منهما لأن قبول العقد في أحدهما لا يكون شرطاً لصحة العقد في الآخر حتى إذا أحدهما قبل في صح فيه بخلاف البيع لأن العقد فيه يتعدد بتفصيل الثمن، ولهذا لو قبل البيع في أحدهما دون الآخر بطل البيع في الكل لأن البائع يتضرر بتفريق الصفقة عليه لما أن العادة قد جرت بضم الرديء إلى الجيد في البيع فيلحقه الضرر بالتفريق ولا كذلك الرهن لأن الراهن لا يتضرر بالتفريق ولهذا لا يبطل به وهذه الرواية هي الأصح. وقيد بالألف لأنه لو رهن عبدين أحدهما بكذا والآخر بكذا ولم يبين لم يجز ؛ هكذا في الفتاوى الغيائية قال الله : (ولو رهن عينا عند رجلين صح سواء كانا شريكين في الدين أو لم يكونا شريكين فيه ويكون جميع العين رهناً عند كل واحد منهما لأن الرهن أضيف إلى كل العين في صفقة واحدة ولا يكون شائعاً باعتبار تعدد المستحق لأن موجبه جعله محبوساً بدين كل واحد منهما إذا لا تضايق في استحقاق الحبس ولهذا لو رهن لا ينقسم على أجزاء الدين بل يكون كله محبوساً بكل الدين وبكل جزء من أجزائة فلا شيوخ قال صاحب العناية أخذاً من النهاية : قيل هو منقوض بما إذا باع من رجلين أو وهب من رجلين على قول أبي يوسف ومحمد فإن العقد فيهما أضيف إلى جميع الدين في صفقة واحدة وفيه الشيوع حتى كان المبيع والمرهون بينهما نصفين كما لو نص على المناصقة والجواب أن إضافة العقد إلى اثنين توجب الشيوع فيما يكون العقد مفيداً للملك كالهبة والبيع فإن العين الواحدة لا يمكن أن تكون مملوكة لشخصين على الكمال فتجعل شائعة فتنقسم عليهما للجواز والرهن غير مفيد للملك وإنما يفيد الاحتباس، ويجوز أن تكون العين الواحدة محتسبة لحقين على الكمال فيمتنع الشيوخ فيه تحرياً للجواز لكون القبض لا بد منه في الرهن والشيوخ يمنع عنه؛ إلى هنا كلامه
And if he pawns an item to two men, it is valid, and the pledge is for the share of his debt. If he pays the debt... the additions: he may take from one of them if he pays what was specified for him, because separation is established in the pledge by specifying the share of each one, because acceptance of the contract regarding one of them is not a condition for validity of the contract regarding the other, so if they accept regarding one, it is valid in it, unlike sale because the contract there is multiplied by detailing the price. Therefore, if he accepts sale for one without the other, the entire sale is invalid because the seller is harmed by splitting the bundle, as custom has attached the defective to the good in sale, so harm comes by splitting, unlike pledge because the pledgor is not harmed by splitting, so it is not voided by it, and this narration is the most correct. And it is restricted to 'thousand' because if he pawns two slaves, one for this and the other for that, and does not specify, it is not valid; thus in al-Fatawa al-Ghiyathiyya. He said: 'And if he pawns an item to two men, it is valid whether they are partners in the debt or not, and the entire item is a pledge for each one of them, because the pledge is attached to the entire item in one transaction and is not shared due to multiplicity of the entitled party, because its effect is to make it held for the debt of each one, since there is no constriction in the right of detention. Therefore, if he pawns, it is not divided over parts of the debt, but the whole is held for the whole debt and for every part of its parts.' So the shuyukh said... the author of al-'Inayah, taking from al-Nihayah, said: 'It is said this is refuted by the case of selling to two men or gifting to two men according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, for the contract there is attached to the entire item in one transaction and there is sharing, so the sold item and the pawned item are between them half and half, as if they specified sharing. The answer is that attaching the contract to two necessitates sharing in what the contract confers ownership like gift and sale, for a single item cannot be owned by two persons completely, so it is made shared and divided between them for validity. The pledge does not confer ownership, only detention, and it is permissible for a single item to be held for two rights completely, so the shuyukh prevent it.' Up to here is his speech.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that when a single item is pawned to two creditors, it becomes a full pledge for each creditor's entire debt, without division. The author distinguishes this from sale and gift, where ownership cannot be shared completely, so the item must be divided. The ruling is based on the principle that pawn (rahn) creates a right of detention (habas), which can be held fully by multiple parties simultaneously, unlike ownership (milk). The passage also addresses an objection from some shuyukh, who analogize to sale/gift where the item becomes shared (shayi'), and the answer clarifies that pawn does not transfer ownership, so the analogy fails. The relied-upon position (al-asahh) is that the pawn is valid and the entire item is held for each creditor. A condition is added: if the pawner specifies different amounts without indicating the total, it is invalid. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract by which property is detained as security for a debt.
شيوع (shuyū'): Undivided co-ownership or sharing in a property.
احتباس (ihtibās): Detention; the right to hold property as security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person pawns one item to two creditors, how is the item held?
A) Each creditor holds half of the item.
B) The entire item is held as a pledge for each creditor's full debt.
C) The item is divided proportionally to the debt amounts.
D) The pawn is invalid unless the creditors are partners in the debt.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a pawned item is held fully for each creditor because pawn creates detention, not ownership, and detention can be shared completely.

Joint Pawning: Two Pawners, One Creditor
Ruling on joint pawning by two pawners to one creditor, with contrast to gift and a dispute on divisible items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when two persons jointly pawn a single item to one creditor, and explain why the whole item is held for each debt rather than shared.

Core Idea
Joint pawning is valid: the entire pawn is held for each debt, because pawn is detention, not ownership.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: two debtors jointly pawn one item to a single creditor. The Hanafi school allows this, treating the entire item as security for each debtor's share of the debt. The ruling hinges on the nature of pawn (rahn) as mere detention (habs) rather than transfer of ownership, which permits multiple rights in the same item. We also examine a related dispute on guarantee when the item is divisible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The case: two pawners (rahin) jointly pawn one item to a single creditor (murtahin). The item may be divisible or indivisible.
The text first contrasts pawn with gift to highlight the difference.
2
Understand the key principle: pawn is detention, not ownership
In gift, the item must be divided because ownership cannot be shared in the same unit. In pawn, mere detention (habs) allows the whole to be held for each claim.
The whole item is 'mahbus' (detained) for each debt, not owned.
3
Apply the principle to joint pawning
Each pawner's debt attaches to the entire pawn. The creditor holds the whole until both debts are paid. Unity of transaction (صفقة) is required; if done in two transactions, it's invalid.
The text gives an analogy: if one pays all but one dirham, the whole remains pawn.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on divisible items
If the item is divisible, each pawner should hold half. If one hands over the whole to the other, the one who gives must guarantee (yadman) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but not according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

أقول : بخلاف الهبة من رجلين حيث لا يجوز عند الإمام لأن العين تنقسم عليهما لاستحالة ثبوت الملك لكل واحد منهما في الكل فيثبت الشيوع ضرورة وقد تقدم بيانه في كتاب الهبة، وكل واحد منهما في نوبته كالعدل في العبد رهناً بذلك الدرهم فكذا هذا ويعتبر اتحاد صفقة الرهن واختلافهما ولا يعتبر اختلاف الدينين واتفاقهما حتى لو رهن بدينه عيناً في صفقتين لم يجز لاختلاف صفقة الرهن فيمكن الشيوع في كل صفقة. ولو مات أحد الراهنين فورثه الآخر فالرهن على حالة لأن الوارث يقوم مقام المورث في حقوقه وأملاكه والرهن لا يبطل بموت الراهن ولا بموت المرتهن فيبقى الرهن على حاله. ومن رهن مالين بدين واحد وقيمة المالين سواء صار كل هذا والبعض من وموجبه صيرورته محبوساً بالدين وهذا مما يقابل الوصف بالتجزي فصار محبوساً لكل واحد منهما بكماله فيمسك هذا يوماً والآخر يوماً، وصار كل واحد منهما في اليوم الذي يمسك كالعدل في حق الآخر، فإذا بكماله والعين الواحدة تجوز أن تصير كلها محبوسة بحق هذا وعلى هذا لو اشترى رجلان شيئاً واحداً وأدى أحدهما حضته لم يكن له أن يقضيه شيئاً وللبائع أن يحبسه كله حتى يستوفي ما على الآخر، فإن هلك عنده بعد ما
