بدا للراهن أن يتركه فللمرتهن أن يرده لأن الرهن غير لازم في حق المرتهن رهن اثنان لم يكن لأحدهما أن يسترده بدون الآخر لأن أحدهما متى انفرد بالرد أبطل حق الآخر فإن حق الآخر بقي في النصف شائعاً والرهن في نصف شائع باطل، وإنما جعل الرهن منهما رهناً من كل واحد منهما على الكمال ضرورة تصحيح العقد تحرياً للجواز والضرورة في تصحيح العقد لا تصحيح الفسخ فيعتبر الفسخ متجزئاً فمتى انفرد أحدهما بالفسخ يبقى في حق الآخر الرهن في جزء شائع وكان في نقضه نقض الرهن في الكل فلا يملكه. ولو نقض أحد شريكي المفاوضة جاز لأن تصرف أحدهما كتصرفهما حتى يكون رهن أحدهما كرهنهما فكذا نقض أحدهما كنقضهما، ولا يملكه أحد شريكي العنان لأنه ليس تصرف أحدهما كنصرهما . يجعل رهن أحدهما كرهنهما، فإن نقضه وقبضه وهلك عنده ولم يباشر العقد بإذن شريكه كان حتى في لا
I say: Unlike gifting to two, which is not valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa because the item is divided between them due to the impossibility of establishing full ownership for each, so sharing is necessitated, as previously explained in the book of gift. And each one in his turn is like a trustee (adl) regarding the other. This is if the item is indivisible apparently. And if it is divisible, then each must hold half. If one of them hands over all to the other, then he must compensate (yadman) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). In al-Mabsut: a discussion in chapters: first on pawning of two men from one, second on taking pawn by two men from one, third on rescission. Chapter: Two men pawn jointly to a man: it is valid because the pledgee's possession is realized in the whole without sharing, and the separation of their properties causes sharing in the pawn. It is permissible for the property of another to be pawned for a debt of another, just as if he borrows something and pawns it, because they both pawned jointly and consented. The whole becomes a pledge for each one according to his debt, because they intended validity of the pawn and it cannot be valid except by making each a pledgor of the whole for his debt, to validate the pawn, because one tries to validate the contract as much as possible, and this is possible. Do you not see that if one pawns another's slave with his permission for a thousand, he becomes a pledgor of the whole for every dirham etc. Even if he pays all the debt except one dirham, the entire slave remains a pawn for that dirham. So here too. And the unity of the transaction is considered, not the difference or agreement of the debts, such that if he pawns an item for his debt in two transactions, it is not valid due to different transactions, so sharing may occur in each transaction. If one of the two pawners dies and the other inherits him, the pawn remains as is, because the heir stands in place of the deceased in his rights and properties, and pawn is not invalidated by death of pledgor or pledgee. So the pawn remains as is. If one pawns two properties for one debt and their values are equal, each becomes a pawn for half the debt. If two men take a pawn from one man and their debts are different, it is valid, and each has the amount of his debt between them, because the debt is attached to the entire slave and there is no sharing, as if he pawned for each, and he did not pawn some of this and some of that. Its effect is to make it held for the debt, and this accepts division by description, so it becomes held for each completely, so he holds it one day and the other the next day, and each in the day he holds becomes like a trustee for the other. If it perishes, each recovers to the extent of his share, because recovery accepts division by description. If the pledgor pays the debt of one, he may not take anything from the pawn, and the other may hold it all until he recovers his debt, because the item became held for each completely, and a single item may be fully held for the right of one and another. Analogously, if two men buy one item and one pays his share, he may not take anything, and the seller may hold the entire item until he recovers what is owed by the other. If it perishes with him after he has recovered his debt, he takes back what he gave, as we mentioned. If pledgor and pledgee rescind, as long as the pledgor has not taken possession, it remains a pawn held by the pledgee, because cancellation of pawn is not valid except by cancellation of possession, just as pawn is not valid except by possession, because cancellation is the opposite of the contract by ruling. If the pledgor decides to abandon it, the pledgee may return it, because pawn is not binding (lazim) for the pledgee. For two pawners, one may not take it back without the other, because if one alone returns, he nullifies the other's right, as the other's right remains in half as undivided, and pawn in an undivided half is invalid. The pawn from the two is made a full pawn from each only out of necessity to validate the contract, seeking validity. The necessity for validating the contract does not extend to validating rescission, so rescission is considered divisible. When one alone rescinds, the pawn for the other remains in a divided share, and in its cancellation is cancellation of the entire pawn, so he does not have that right. If one of the partners of mufawada rescinds, it is valid, because the action of one is like the action of both, so the pawn of one is like the pawn of both, and similarly rescission of one is like rescission of both. The partner of 'inan does not have that right, because his action is not like their action. The pawn of one is made like the pawn of both, so if he cancels and takes possession and it perishes with him without having contracted the pawn with the permission of his partner, it is...
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This long passage contains the author's commentary (بخلاف الهبة) and a series of distinct rulings from al-Mabsut. The author first contrasts pawn with gift: gifting one item to two donees is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa because ownership cannot be held completely by two, so division is forced. But in pawn, since it is detention not ownership, the entire item can be held for each creditor. For divisible items, each must hold half; if one hands over the whole, he must guarantee according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while the two companions disagree (they say no guarantee). Then the author mentions three types of cases: (1) two pawners pawning to one creditor, (2) two creditors (or two pawners?) taking a pawn from one, (3) rescission. The detailed rules follow: when two persons pawn jointly to one, the entire pawn is a pledge for each pawner's debt, and the creditor holds the whole. Various sub-rulings: if one pawner dies and the other inherits, the pawn continues; if two properties are pawned for one debt, each is half; if two creditors take a pawn from one debtor, each can hold in turns; if one debt is paid, the other creditor can hold the entire pawn until his debt is paid, etc. The rescission section explains that cancellation of pawn requires returning possession, and if two pawners jointly made the pawn, one alone cannot cancel because that would divide the pawn which is invalid. However, in a mufawada partnership, one partner can cancel, but in 'inan partnership, he cannot. The passage ends with a fragment about a partner who cancelled and took possession without permission.

Key Terms
تفاسخ (tafāṣukh): Mutual rescission of the pawn contract between pledgor and pledgee.
مفاوضة (mufāwaḍa): A type of partnership (sharika) where each partner acts as agent and surety for the other with full authority.
عنان (ʿinān): A limited partnership where each partner acts as agent but not surety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when two pawners jointly pawn a single item to one creditor?
A) It becomes shared equally between the two pawners as security for their debts.
B) The entire item is a pawn for each pawner's debt separately.
C) It is divided proportionally to each pawner's debt.
D) The pawn is invalid because a single item cannot serve two debts.

Key Takeaway
Joint pawning is valid: the entire pawn is held for each debt, because pawn is detention, not ownership.

Multiple Pledgees and Multiple Properties
Rulings on pawning multiple properties for one debt and multiple pledgees for one pawn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rulings when two persons take a pawn from one debtor and when one debtor pawns two properties for one debt.

Core Idea
When two creditors take a pawn, they hold in turns; when one pawns two properties, each secures half the debt.

This lesson covers two distinct scenarios: first, a single debtor pawning two properties for one debt; second, two creditors taking a single pawn from one debtor. The text provides detailed rules for each, including how the pawn is held and what happens upon payment. An analogy with sale clarifies the principle that a single item can be fully detained for multiple rights.

Guided Path
1
Scenario A: One debtor pawns two properties for one debt
If values are equal, each property becomes pawn for half the debt. If unequal, the text does not specify but implies proportionally.
This is a straightforward division based on value.
2
Scenario B: Two creditors take a single pawn from one debtor
The debts may be different. The pawn is held for each creditor completely, but they hold in turns (one day each) as trustees.
Each acts as 'adl' (trustee) for the other during their turn.
3
Apply the rules on payment and destruction
If the debtor pays one creditor, that creditor cannot take his share; the other may hold the whole until his debt is paid. If the pawn perishes, each recovers proportionally.
The rule mimics the sale analogy: two buyers of one item, the seller holds the whole until both pay.
4
Note the analogy with sale
The text explicitly analogizes: if two buy one item and one pays, the seller holds the whole for the unpaid balance.
This reinforces that detention can cover multiple claims.

العبد رهناً بذلك الدرهم فكذا هذا ويعتبر اتحاد صفقة الرهن واختلافهما ولا يعتبر اختلاف الدينين واتفاقهما حتى لو رهن بدينه عيناً في صفقتين لم يجز لاختلاف صفقة الرهن فيمكن الشيوع في كل صفقة. ولو مات أحد الراهنين فورثه الآخر فالرهن على حالة لأن الوارث يقوم مقام المورث في حقوقه وأملاكه والرهن لا يبطل بموت الراهن ولا بموت المرتهن فيبقى الرهن على حاله. ومن رهن مالين بدين واحد وقيمة المالين سواء صار كل واحد منهما رهناً بنصف الدين، فلو ارتهن رجلان من رجل رهناً والدينان مختلفان جاز ولكل واحد منهما قدر دينه فيما بينهما لأن الدين أضيف هذا إلى كل العبد ولا شيوع فيه كأنه رهن لكل منهما ولم برهن البعض من هذا والبعض من وموجبه صيرورته محبوساً بالدين وهذا مما يقابل الوصف بالتجزي فصار محبوساً لكل واحد منهما بكماله فيمسك هذا يوماً والآخر يوماً، وصار كل واحد منهما في اليوم الذي يمسك كالعدل في حق الآخر، فإذا هلك صار كل واحد منهما مستوفياً بقدر حصته لأن الاستيفاء مما يقبل الوصف بالتجزي، ولو قضى الراهن دين أحدهما ليس له أخذ شيء من الرهن وللآخر أن يمسكه كله حتى هذا يستوفي دينه لأن العين صارت محبوسة لكل واحد بكماله والعين الواحدة تجوز أن تصير كلها محبوسة بحق هذا وعلى هذا لو اشترى رجلان شيئاً واحداً وأدى أحدهما حضته لم يكن له أن يقضيه شيئاً وللبائع أن يحبسه كله حتى يستوفي ما على الآخر، فإن هلك عنده بعد ما قضى دينه يسترد ما أعطاه لما ذكرنا. ولو تفاسخ الراهن والمرتهن فما لم يقبضه الراهن فهو رهن يمسكه المرتهن لأن نقض الرهن لا يصح إلا بنقض القبض كالرهن لا يصح إلا بالقبض لأن نقض الشيء ضد العقد حكماً، ولو بدا للراهن أن يتركه فللمرتهن أن يرده لأن الرهن غير لازم في حق المرتهن رهن اثنان لم يكن لأحدهما أن يسترده بدون الآخر لأن أحدهما متى انفرد بالرد أبطل حق الآخر فإن حق الآخر بقي في النصف شائعاً والرهن في نصف شائع باطل، وإنما جعل الرهن منهما رهناً من كل واحد منهما على الكمال ضرورة تصحيح العقد تحرياً للجواز والضرورة في تصحيح العقد لا تصحيح الفسخ فيعتبر الفسخ متجزئاً فمتى انفرد أحدهما بالفسخ يبقى في حق الآخر الرهن في جزء شائع وكان في نقضه نقض الرهن في الكل فلا يملكه. ولو نقض أحد شريكي المفاوضة جاز لأن تصرف أحدهما كتصرفهما حتى يكون رهن أحدهما كرهنهما فكذا نقض أحدهما كنقضهما، ولا يملكه أحد شريكي العنان لأنه ليس تصرف أحدهما كنصرهما . يجعل رهن أحدهما كرهنهما، فإن نقضه وقبضه وهلك عنده ولم يباشر العقد بإذن شريكه كان حتى في لا
I say: Unlike gifting to two, which is not valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa because the item is divided between them due to the impossibility of establishing full ownership for each, so sharing is necessitated, as previously explained in the book of gift. And each one in his turn is like a trustee (adl) regarding the other. This is if the item is indivisible apparently. And if it is divisible, then each must hold half. If one of them hands over all to the other, then he must compensate (yadman) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). In al-Mabsut: a discussion in chapters: first on pawning of two men from one, second on taking pawn by two men from one, third on rescission. Chapter: Two men pawn jointly to a man: it is valid because the pledgee's possession is realized in the whole without sharing, and the separation of their properties causes sharing in the pawn. It is permissible for the property of another to be pawned for a debt of another, just as if he borrows something and pawns it, because they both pawned jointly and consented. The whole becomes a pledge for each one according to his debt, because they intended validity of the pawn and it cannot be valid except by making each a pledgor of the whole for his debt, to validate the pawn, because one tries to validate the contract as much as possible, and this is possible. Do you not see that if one pawns another's slave with his permission for a thousand, he becomes a pledgor of the whole for every dirham etc. Even if he pays all the debt except one dirham, the entire slave remains a pawn for that dirham. So here too. And the unity of the transaction is considered, not the difference or agreement of the debts, such that if he pawns an item for his debt in two transactions, it is not valid due to different transactions, so sharing may occur in each transaction. If one of the two pawners dies and the other inherits him, the pawn remains as is, because the heir stands in place of the deceased in his rights and properties, and pawn is not invalidated by death of pledgor or pledgee. So the pawn remains as is. If one pawns two properties for one debt and their values are equal, each becomes a pawn for half the debt. If two men take a pawn from one man and their debts are different, it is valid, and each has the amount of his debt between them, because the debt is attached to the entire slave and there is no sharing, as if he pawned for each, and he did not pawn some of this and some of that. Its effect is to make it held for the debt, and this accepts division by description, so it becomes held for each completely, so he holds it one day and the other the next day, and each in the day he holds becomes like a trustee for the other. If it perishes, each recovers to the extent of his share, because recovery accepts division by description. If the pledgor pays the debt of one, he may not take anything from the pawn, and the other may hold it all until he recovers his debt, because the item became held for each completely, and a single item may be fully held for the right of one and another. Analogously, if two men buy one item and one pays his share, he may not take anything, and the seller may hold the entire item until he recovers what is owed by the other. If it perishes with him after he has recovered his debt, he takes back what he gave, as we mentioned. If pledgor and pledgee rescind, as long as the pledgor has not taken possession, it remains a pawn held by the pledgee, because cancellation of pawn is not valid except by cancellation of possession, just as pawn is not valid except by possession, because cancellation is the opposite of the contract by ruling. If the pledgor decides to abandon it, the pledgee may return it, because pawn is not binding (lazim) for the pledgee. For two pawners, one may not take it back without the other, because if one alone returns, he nullifies the other's right, as the other's right remains in half as undivided, and pawn in an undivided half is invalid. The pawn from the two is made a full pawn from each only out of necessity to validate the contract, seeking validity. The necessity for validating the contract does not extend to validating rescission, so rescission is considered divisible. When one alone rescinds, the pawn for the other remains in a divided share, and in its cancellation is cancellation of the entire pawn, so he does not have that right. If one of the partners of mufawada rescinds, it is valid, because the action of one is like the action of both, so the pawn of one is like the pawn of both, and similarly rescission of one is like rescission of both. The partner of 'inan does not have that right, because his action is not like their action. The pawn of one is made like the pawn of both, so if he cancels and takes possession and it perishes with him without having contracted the pawn with the permission of his partner, it is...
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This long passage contains the author's commentary (بخلاف الهبة) and a series of distinct rulings from al-Mabsut. The author first contrasts pawn with gift: gifting one item to two donees is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa because ownership cannot be held completely by two, so division is forced. But in pawn, since it is detention not ownership, the entire item can be held for each creditor. For divisible items, each must hold half; if one hands over the whole, he must guarantee according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while the two companions disagree (they say no guarantee). Then the author mentions three types of cases: (1) two pawners pawning to one creditor, (2) two creditors (or two pawners?) taking a pawn from one, (3) rescission. The detailed rules follow: when two persons pawn jointly to one, the entire pawn is a pledge for each pawner's debt, and the creditor holds the whole. Various sub-rulings: if one pawner dies and the other inherits, the pawn continues; if two properties are pawned for one debt, each is half; if two creditors take a pawn from one debtor, each can hold in turns; if one debt is paid, the other creditor can hold the entire pawn until his debt is paid, etc. The rescission section explains that cancellation of pawn requires returning possession, and if two pawners jointly made the pawn, one alone cannot cancel because that would divide the pawn which is invalid. However, in a mufawada partnership, one partner can cancel, but in 'inan partnership, he cannot. The passage ends with a fragment about a partner who cancelled and took possession without permission.

Key Terms
تفاسخ (tafāṣukh): Mutual rescission of the pawn contract between pledgor and pledgee.
مفاوضة (mufāwaḍa): A type of partnership (sharika) where each partner acts as agent and surety for the other with full authority.
عنان (ʿinān): A limited partnership where each partner acts as agent but not surety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two creditors take a pawn from one debtor, and one creditor's debt is paid, what happens to the pawn?
A) The paid creditor takes his share.
B) The unpaid creditor may hold the entire pawn.
C) The pawn is returned to the debtor.
D) The pawn is divided equally between them.

Key Takeaway
A single pawn can be wholly detained for each of multiple claims; holders take turns as trustees.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
10 min
Rescission of Pawn and Partnership Effects
Rulings on rescission of pawn, joint rescission, and partnership effects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid rescission (tafāṣukh) of a pawn contract and explain the differences between mufāwaḍa and ʿinān partnerships regarding rescission by one partner.

Core Idea
Rescission requires returning possession; one joint pawner cannot rescind alone, but a mufāwaḍa partner can.

The final part of the passage discusses the rescission of pawn (tafāṣukh). It explains that rescission requires return of possession, just as the contract required possession initially. For joint pawners, one alone cannot rescind because that would divide the pawn, which is invalid. However, in a mufāwaḍa partnership (full partnership), one partner can rescind on behalf of both, but in ʿinān (limited partnership), he cannot. The text also mentions the scenario where the pledgor abandons the pawn and the pledgee may return it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the requirement for rescission
Rescission requires the pledgor to take back possession. If the pledgor has not taken possession, the pawn remains with the pledgee. Cancellation is the opposite of the contract.
The principle: نقض الشيء ضد العقد حكماً.
2
Joint pawners: one cannot rescind alone
If two pawners jointly pawned, one cannot rescind without the other, because that would leave the other's right in an undivided half, which is invalid.
The pawn was made whole for each out of necessity; that necessity does not extend to rescission.
3
Partnership types: mufāwaḍa vs ʿinān
In mufāwaḍa, each partner has full authority, so one can rescind the pawn of both. In ʿinān, partners are only agents, not sureties, so one cannot rescind alone.
The text uses the principle that the action of one in mufāwaḍa is like the action of both.
4
Special case: partner who cancels without permission
If a partner in ʿinān cancels and takes possession without his partner's permission, and the pawn perishes, the partner is liable.
The text is fragmented but indicates liability.

Commentary
This long passage contains the author's commentary (بخلاف الهبة) and a series of distinct rulings from al-Mabsut. The author first contrasts pawn with gift: gifting one item to two donees is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa because ownership cannot be held completely by two, so division is forced. But in pawn, since it is detention not ownership, the entire item can be held for each creditor. For divisible items, each must hold half; if one hands over the whole, he must guarantee according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while the two companions disagree (they say no guarantee). Then the author mentions three types of cases: (1) two pawners pawning to one creditor, (2) two creditors (or two pawners?) taking a pawn from one, (3) rescission. The detailed rules follow: when two persons pawn jointly to one, the entire pawn is a pledge for each pawner's debt, and the creditor holds the whole. Various sub-rulings: if one pawner dies and the other inherits, the pawn continues; if two properties are pawned for one debt, each is half; if two creditors take a pawn from one debtor, each can hold in turns; if one debt is paid, the other creditor can hold the entire pawn until his debt is paid, etc. The rescission section explains that cancellation of pawn requires returning possession, and if two pawners jointly made the pawn, one alone cannot cancel because that would divide the pawn which is invalid. However, in a mufawada partnership, one partner can cancel, but in 'inan partnership, he cannot. The passage ends with a fragment about a partner who cancelled and took possession without permission.

Key Terms
تفاسخ (tafāṣukh): Mutual rescission of the pawn contract between pledgor and pledgee.
مفاوضة (mufāwaḍa): A type of partnership (sharika) where each partner acts as agent and surety for the other with full authority.
عنان (ʿinān): A limited partnership where each partner acts as agent but not surety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid because both must agree.
B) It is valid because one partner's action represents both.
C) It is valid only if the other partner later approves.
D) It is invalid because pawn cannot be rescinded by one party.

Key Takeaway
Rescission requires return of possession; joint pawners cannot rescind alone, but mufāwaḍa partners can.

Two Pawners Pawning One Property to One Creditor
Ruling on joint pledging with analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on joint pledging (rahn) by two pawnors to one creditor and apply the qiyas (analogy) to determine validity and effects.

Core Idea
The whole property is pledged for each debt, using a legal fiction (hila) to validate the contract.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario: two individuals jointly pawn a single asset to one creditor for separate debts. The Hanafi school rules that this is valid and that the entire asset becomes a pledge for each debtor's full debt. This ruling is based on a qiyas (analogy) to the case of pawning another's property with permission, and it relies on the principle that contracts should be upheld as much as possible. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly structuring joint pledges in accordance with Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the passage and determine the legal act (two persons pawning one property to one creditor) and the ruling (sahih/valid). Note the key consequence: the entire property becomes a pledge for each debt.
2
Understand the legal fiction (hila)
Recognize that each pawnor is treated as pawning the whole property for his own debt, even though physically it is the same asset. This is a hila (legal fiction) to ensure the validity of the contract.
The text says: 'because they intended the validity of the pledge... it will only be valid by making each of them a pawner of the whole for his debt.'
3
Trace the qiyas dalil
Examine the analogy: if a person pawns another's slave with permission for a 1000 debt, the entire slave becomes a pledge for every dirham. Apply this analogy to the joint pawning scenario: each pawnor implicitly permits the other, so the whole property is pledged for each debt.
The key phrase: 'Do you not see that if a person pawns another slave with his permission...' This is a clear qiyas jaliy.
4
Note the condition: unity of transaction
The passage stipulates that the pledge transaction must be a single contract (ittihad al-safqah). If there are two separate transactions, the pledge is invalid because each transaction can only create a part share. The debts may differ, but that does not affect validity.
This condition is crucial: the contract must be one, not two separate contracts.
5
Apply the ruling to death/inheritance scenario
If one pawnor dies and the other inherits him, the pledge remains intact because the successor inherits rights and obligations. The pledge is not invalidated by the death of a pawnor or pledgee.
This shows the continuity of the pledge contract despite changes in ownership/status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكون كله رهناً لكل واحد منهما بدينه لأنهما قصدا صحة الرهن ولن يصح إلا بأن يجعل كل واحد منهما راهناً كله بدينه تصحيحاً للرهن لأنه يحتال لتصحيح العقد ما أمكن وهذا ممكن ألا ترى أن من رهن عبداً آخر بإذنه بألف صار راهناً كله بكل درهم مثلاً . حتى لو قضى كل الدين إلا درهماً بقي كل العبد رهناً بذلك الدرهم فكذا هذا ويعتبر اتحاد صفقة الرهن واختلافهما ولا يعتبر اختلاف الدينين واتفاقهما حتى لو رهن بدينه عيناً في صفقتين لم يجز لاختلاف صفقة الرهن فيمكن الشيوع في كل صفقة. ولو مات أحد الراهنين فورثه الآخر فالرهن على حالة لأن الوارث يقوم مقام المورث في حقوقه وأملاكه والرهن لا يبطل بموت الراهن ولا بموت المرتهن فيبقى الرهن على حاله.
It all becomes a pledge for each of them for his debt, because they intended the validity of the pledge, and it will only be valid by making each of them a pawner of the whole for his debt to correct the pledge, because one resorts to correcting the contract as much as possible, and this is possible. Do you not see that if a person pawns another slave with his permission for a thousand, he becomes a pawner of the whole for every dirham, for example. Even if he pays all the debt except one dirham, the entire slave remains a pledge for that dirham, so likewise this. And the unity of the pledge transaction is considered, and their difference, and the difference or agreement of the debts is not considered, such that if one pawns an asset for his debt in two transactions, it is not valid due to the difference of the pledge transaction, so partial ownership can occur in each transaction. And if one of the two pawners dies and the other inherits him, the pledge remains as it was, because the successor takes the place of the predecessor in his rights and properties, and the pledge does not become void by the death of the pawner nor by the death of the pledgee, so the pledge remains as it was.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling when two persons jointly pawn one property to a single creditor for their separate debts. The ruling is that the entire property becomes a pledge for each man's entire debt. The reason is that both parties intend a valid pledge contract, and validity can only be achieved by considering each pawner as a pawner of the entire property for his own debt. This is a legal fiction (hila) to uphold the contract. The author supports this by analogy: if someone pawns another's slave with the owner's permission for a debt of a thousand, the slave becomes a pledge for every dirham of that debt. Even if only one dirham remains unpaid, the entire slave remains pledged. Similarly here, the unity of the pledge transaction (i.e., one contract) is required; if there are two separate transactions, it is invalid because each transaction can only create a part share. The death of one pawner does not cancel the pledge; if the other inherits him, the pledge continues as the successor inherits both rights and obligations.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract by which property is held as security for a debt.
راهن (rahin): The person who gives the pledge (pawnor).
مرتهن (murtahin): The person who receives the pledge (creditor/pledgee).
صفقة الرهن (safqat al-rahn): The transaction or contract of pledge; unity of contract is required.
حيلة (hila): Legal fiction or stratagem to achieve a valid contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The debts must be equal.
B) The transaction must be a single contract.
C) The property must be divided proportionally.
D) Each pawnor must separately indicate his share.

Key Takeaway
Two pawnors can validly pledge one property to one creditor for separate debts, and the entire property is security for each debt, provided the contract is a single transaction.

Pawning Two Properties for One Debt: Equal Values
Ruling on equal-valued multiple pledges

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a debtor pawns two equal-valued properties for one debt and determine how much debt each property secures.

Core Idea
When two equal-valued properties are pawned for one debt, each secures half the debt.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the Hanafi law of mortgage (rahn): a single debtor pledges two distinct properties as security for one debt. The key question is: how is the debt allocated between the two properties? The source text provides a clear answer when the properties are of equal value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its conditions
The act is pawning two properties for one debt. The condition stated is that the values of the two properties are equal.
If the values are unequal, a different ruling applies (proportional allocation).
2
Understand the legal consequence
Each property becomes a pledge for exactly half the debt. The debt is split equally between them.
This means that if one property perishes, the creditor can recover half the debt from the other.
3
Consider the implications for partial payment or loss
If the debtor pays half the debt, one property is released. If one property is lost, the creditor still has claim to half the debt from the remaining property.
This ensures the creditor cannot recover more than the debt owed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن رهن مالين بدين واحد وقيمة المالين سواء صار كل واحد منهما رهناً بنصف الدين
And if a person pawns two properties for one debt and the value of the two properties is equal, each one of them becomes a pledge for half of the debt.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This brief ruling addresses a scenario where one debtor pawns two distinct properties as security for a single debt. If both properties are of equal value, each one is considered pledged for exactly half the debt. This is a straightforward distribution: the debt is split equally between the two properties because they are equal in value. The implication is that if one property perishes, the creditor can recover half the debt from the other; if the debtor pays half the debt, only one property is released.

Key Terms
مالين (malayn): Two properties or assets that are distinct and pledged separately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1000 dirhams
B) 500 dirhams
C) 2000 dirhams
D) 0 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When two equal-valued properties are pawned for one debt, each secures exactly half the debt.

Two Creditors with One Pawn and Different Debts
Ruling on two creditors taking one pledge from one debtor for different debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on two creditors holding a single pledge with different debts, including how possession is managed and how proceeds are distributed upon destruction.

Core Idea
Two creditors of one debtor with different debts hold the entire pledge alternately, each acting as trustee for the other.

When two people lend money to the same debtor and take a single item as pledge, they cannot both hold it at once. This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling: they alternate possession day by day, and if the property perishes, they recover proportionally. We'll also see how this principle applies when the debtor pays one creditor and how it compares to a partial payment in a sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the pledge
Note that there are two creditors, one debtor, a single pledged item, and two different debts. This is the specific scenario addressed.
The debts must be different amounts; otherwise the ruling may differ.
2
Determine the validity of the contract
The text explicitly states that the pledge contract is valid (jaza) despite the plurality of creditors.
This is the default Hanafi position.
3
Understand the possession arrangement
Since two creditors cannot physically hold the item simultaneously, they alternate possession day by day. On his day, each holds the entire item and acts as a trustee (adl) for the other.
The right to hold is for the whole, not a share.
4
Analyze the consequence of destruction
If the pledged property perishes, each creditor recovers proportionally to his debt (istifa' bi qadr hussatihi). Satisfaction is divided by description, not by physical parts.
This differs from equal division.
5
Apply the analogy to a similar scenario
The text analogizes to two buyers purchasing one item: if one pays his share, the seller retains the entire item until full payment. This reinforces the principle of detaining the whole for each right.
This helps internalize the underlying logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ارتهن رجلان من رجل رهناً والدينان مختلفان جاز ولكل واحد منهما قدر دينه فيما بينهما لأن الدين أضيف هذا إلى كل العبد ولا شيوع فيه كأنه رهن لكل منهما ولم برهن البعض من هذا والبعض من وموجبه صيرورته محبوساً بالدين وهذا مما يقابل الوصف بالتجزي فصار محبوساً لكل واحد منهما بكماله فيمسك هذا يوماً والآخر يوماً، وصار كل واحد منهما في اليوم الذي يمسك كالعدل في حق الآخر، فإذا هلك صار كل واحد منهما مستوفياً بقدر حصته لأن الاستيفاء مما يقبل الوصف بالتجزي، ولو قضى الراهن دين أحدهما ليس له أخذ شيء من الرهن وللآخر أن يمسكه كله حتى هذا يستوفي دينه لأن العين صارت محبوسة لكل واحد بكماله والعين الواحدة تجوز أن تصير كلها محبوسة بحق هذا وعلى هذا لو اشترى رجلان شيئاً واحداً وأدى أحدهما حضته لم يكن له أن يقضيه شيئاً وللبائع أن يحبسه كله حتى يستوفي ما على الآخر، فإن هلك عنده بعد ما قضى دينه يسترد ما أعطاه لما ذكرنا.
And if two men take a pledge from a man, and the two debts are different, it is valid, and each of them has the amount of his debt between them, because the debt is attributed to the entire slave, and there is no partial ownership in it, as if it is pledged to each of them, and he did not pledge some of this and some of that. And its requirement is its being detained for the debt, and this is something that accepts division by description, so it becomes detained for each of them in its entirety, so this one holds it one day and the other the next day. And each of them, on the day he holds it, is like a trustee (adl) regarding the other's right. So if it perishes, each of them becomes satisfied to the extent of his share, because satisfaction (istifa') accepts division by description. And if the debtor pays the debt of one of them, he cannot take anything from the pledge, and the other can hold all of it until he also collects his debt, because the property has become detained for each one in its entirety, and a single property can become entirely detained for the right of this one. And similarly, if two men buy one thing and one pays his share, he cannot take anything, and the seller can hold all of it until he collects what is owed by the other. If it perishes after the debtor paid his debt, the creditor takes back what he gave, for the reason we mentioned.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage rules on a scenario where two different creditors take a single pledge from one debtor, with the two debts being of different amounts. The contract is valid. For the purpose of possession, each creditor is considered to have the right to hold the entire pledge, because the pledge is detained for both debts. However, since two people cannot physically possess one item simultaneously, they alternate possession day by day. On his day of possession, the holder acts as a trustee for the other. If the pledged property perishes, each creditor recovers proportionally to his debt. If the debtor pays one creditor in full, that creditor cannot take physical possession, and the other creditor retains the right to hold the entire pledge until his debt is paid. The passage analogizes this to a buyer who pays half the price; the seller can retain the entire item until the full price is paid.

Key Terms
العدل (al-adl): A trustee or agent who holds property for the benefit of another, not as owner.
الاستيفاء (al-istifa'): Satisfaction or recovery of the debt from the pledged property upon its destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two creditors hold one pledge for different debts, how is possession managed?
A) They split the property physically.
B) They alternate possession day by day.
C) Only one holds it forever.
D) They both hold it simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
Two creditors of one debtor with different debts each have a right to hold the entire pledged property alternately, and upon destruction they recover proportionally.

Cancellation of Pawn and Retrieval by Two Pawners
Rulings on cancellation of pawn and retrieval by two pawners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on unilateral cancellation by one of two joint pawners and explain the legal reasoning based on the concept of indivisible pledge.

Core Idea
A joint pawn cannot be cancelled by one pawner alone because the pledge is considered as if each pawned the whole.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in pawn contracts: when two persons jointly pawn a property with a creditor. The Hanafi school clarifies that one pawner cannot unilaterally retrieve the pledge. We will explore the legal reasoning behind this rule, including the concept of the pledge being treated as a single indivisible contract, and how cancellation is treated differently than formation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key parties and actions
Recognize the pawner (rahin), pledgee (murtahin), mutual cancellation (tafasukh), and unilateral retrieval attempt.
In this passage, the pledgee can refuse to return the pledge if the pawner unilaterally abandons it.
2
Understand the basic rule of cancellation
Cancellation requires annulling possession; without repossession by the pawner, the pledge remains.
This mirrors the rule that a pledge is not valid without possession.
3
Focus on the joint pawner scenario
Two pawners jointly pledge a property; one wishes to cancel alone. The text states he cannot.
The reason relates to the legal fiction used to validate the original contract.
4
Grasp the legal fiction at formation
To validate a joint pledge, each pawner is considered to have pledged the whole property. This is a necessity (darura) for validity.
Without this fiction, the pledge would be void due to undivided shares.
5
Apply the distinction between formation and cancellation
The fiction applies only to formation, not cancellation. Cancellation is divisible; one pawner cancelling would leave the other's share as an undivided half, which is invalid. Thus, unilateral cancellation is prohibited.
The text emphasizes: 'necessity in validating the contract does not validate the cancellation.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تفاسخ الراهن والمرتهن فما لم يقبضه الراهن فهو رهن يمسكه المرتهن لأن نقض الرهن لا يصح إلا بنقض القبض كالرهن لا يصح إلا بالقبض لأن نقض الشيء ضد العقد حكماً، ولو بدا للراهن أن يتركه فللمرتهن أن يرده لأن الرهن غير لازم في حق المرتهن رهن اثنان لم يكن لأحدهما أن يسترده بدون الآخر لأن أحدهما متى انفرد بالرد أبطل حق الآخر فإن حق الآخر بقي في النصف شائعاً والرهن في نصف شائع باطل، وإنما جعل الرهن منهما رهناً من كل واحد منهما على الكمال ضرورة تصحيح العقد تحرياً للجواز والضرورة في تصحيح العقد لا تصحيح الفسخ فيعتبر الفسخ متجزئاً فمتى انفرد أحدهما بالفسخ يبقى في حق الآخر الرهن في جزء شائع وكان في نقضه نقض الرهن في الكل فلا يملكه.
And if the pawner and the pledgee mutually cancel the pledge, then what the pawner has not taken possession of remains a pledge held by the pledgee, because the annulment of the pledge is not valid except by annulling possession, just as the pledge is not valid except with possession, because annulment of a thing is the opposite of the contract by effect. And if the pawner decides to leave it, the pledgee has the right to return it, because the pledge is not binding with respect to the pledgee. If there are two pawners, one of them cannot retrieve it without the other, because when one alone returns it, he invalidates the right of the other. For the right of the other would remain in half as an undivided share, and a pledge in an undivided half is void. Rather, the pledge from the two of them was made a pledge from each of them in its entirety out of necessity to validate the contract, seeking permissibility, and necessity in validating the contract does not validate the cancellation, so the cancellation is considered divisible. So when one of them alone cancels, the right of the other remains in an undivided portion, and in his cancellation there is cancellation of the entire pledge, so he does not possess the right to do so.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage addresses cancellation (faskh) of a pledge contract. First, cancellation requires repossession by the pawner; without that, the pledgee still holds the property. If the pawner unilaterally decides to abandon the pledge, the pledgee can refuse and keep it, because the pledge is not binding on the pledgee (he can give it up if he wishes). However, if there are two joint pawners, one cannot unilaterally retrieve the pledge without the other. The reason is that the pledge was established as if each pawner had pledged the whole property (a legal fiction) to validate the contract. This fiction is limited to validation and does not extend to cancellation. Cancellation is considered divisible: if one pawner cancels, the other's right becomes a share in an undivided half, which is invalid for a pledge. Thus, one pawner alone cannot cancel; both must agree, or the pledge continues.

Key Terms
تفاسخ (tafasukh): Mutual cancellation of a contract by both parties.
شائع (sha'i'): Undivided share; a part of jointly owned property not physically separated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two persons jointly pawn a property, can one of them alone retrieve the pledge from the creditor?
A) Yes, his share.
B) Yes, but only if the other agrees.
C) No, not without the other.
D) No, because the pledge is void.

Key Takeaway
A joint pawn cannot be cancelled by one pawner alone; both must agree, as cancellation would create an invalid pledge of an undivided share.

Dispute on Acknowledgment of Void Debt (Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on joint pledge and acknowledgment of void debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether one joint creditor's acknowledgment of void debt voids the entire common pledge or only his share, and explain the reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
One joint creditor's acknowledgment voids his share only, not the whole pledge — the school's nuance on independent rights.

This passage from al-Faqih Abu al-Layth's al-Uyun presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a joint creditor's admission that the secured debt is void destroys the entire pledge or only his portion. The difference turns on whether the pledge is viewed as a single contract or as two independent rights. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply principles of partnership and pledge in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Read the passage and identify the parties: two creditors each owed 1000 dirhams by a debtor, who gave a common pledge (a piece of land) to secure both debts. One creditor later acknowledges the debt is void (a talji'a, fictitious transaction).
The acknowledgment is made while the pledge is still in their possession.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf (and Abu al-Layth) holds that the entire pledge becomes void. His reasoning: although the debts are different, the pledge contract is one and indivisible; acknowledging the invalidity of the debt (the basis of the pledge) nullifies the entire pledge.
The key point: unity of the pledge contract.
3
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's position and its basis
Muhammad holds that the pledge remains valid for the other creditor. His reasoning: the debts are separate, and the pledge is a right for each creditor independently. The acknowledgment only affects the acknowledging creditor's own right, not his partner's.
The key point: independence of rights.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf, the other creditor loses his security; under Muhammad, he retains it. The text does not give a tarjih, but later Hanafi works often prefer Muhammad's view as the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
Be aware that the passage itself does not resolve which view is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الفقيه أبو الليث في العيون رجلان لكل واحد منهما ألف درهم على رجل فارتهنا منه أرضاً بدينهما وقبضاها ثم قال أحدهما إن المال الذي لنا على فلان باطل والأرض في أيدينا تلجئة قال الفقيه أبو الليث وأبو يوسف رحمه الله : بطل الرهن لأن الدينين وإن اختلفا ولكن الرهن بهما واحد فإذا اعترف أحدهما ببطلان الدين والرهن بطل الرهن أصلاً. وقال محمد الله تعالى : لا يبطل الرهن ويبرأ من حصته من الدين والرهن بحاله لأن الدينين مختلفان والرهن حقاً لهما فإقراره يصح مبطلاً لحق نفسه دون حق شريكه فبطل حق المقر في الدين والرهن وبقي حق الآخر فيهما على حاله
And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned in al-Uyun: Two men, each having one thousand dirhams from a man, they took a land as a pledge from him for their debts and took possession of it. Then one of them said, 'The money that we have from so-and-so is void, and the land in our hands is a disguise (talji'a).' Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The pledge becomes void, because even though the two debts are different, the pledge is one for both, so if one acknowledges the invalidity of the debt and the pledge, the entire pledge becomes void. And Muhammad (may Allah Almighty have mercy on him) said: The pledge does not become void, and he is discharged from his share of the debt, and the pledge remains as it is, because the two debts are different, and the pledge is a right for both. So his acknowledgment is valid to nullify his own right but not the right of his partner. Thus the right of the acknowledging one is voided in the debt and pledge, and the right of the other remains in both as it was.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage presents a known intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the effect of one of two joint creditors acknowledging that the debt secured by a common pledge is void (or a 'talji'a' — a fictitious transaction). According to Abu Yusuf and Abu al-Layth, the entire pledge becomes void because the pledge contract is one and the debt is the basis; if one acknowledges the debt is void, the entire pledge is void. According to Muhammad, the pledge remains valid for the other creditor because the debts are separate and each creditor has an independent right; the acknowledgment only affects the acknowledging creditor's share. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is often that of Muhammad, but the text does not explicitly tarjih. The practical difference: if one creditor says the debt is fake, does the other lose his security? Muhammad says no.

Key Terms
تلجئة (talji'a): A disguised or fictitious transaction; here the creditor claims the debt was fake.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession, here of the invalidity of the debt.
رهن (rahn): Pledge, collateral given as security for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, if one of two joint creditors acknowledges that the common debt is void, what happens to the pledge?
A) The entire pledge becomes void.
B) The pledge remains for the other creditor.
C) The pledge is split between them.
D) The pledge becomes invalid only if the debtor agrees.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute on joint pledges, Muhammad al-Shaybani's view—that acknowledgment only voids the acknowledging creditor's share—is the relied-upon position, preserving the innocent creditor's security.

Death of the Agent Voids the Agency
Matn and sharh on agency termination with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that agency becomes void upon the agent's death and explain why it is not inherited, distinguishing it from mudaraba.

Core Idea
Agency is a personal trust that dies with the agent; it is not inherited like a right to profit.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: that agency (wakala) becomes void upon the death of the agent, with no succession by heirs or executors. The commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides the legal reasoning and addresses an opposing view from Abu Yusuf. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between rights in one's favor (inheritable) and rights upon one (not inheritable).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the matn statement: 'And it becomes invalid by the death of the agent, so that neither his heir nor his executor takes his place.' Note that the ruling is clear: the agency contract terminates instantly upon the agent's death.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentary gives two reasons: agency is a 'covenant of mercy' (rahmah) not subject to inheritance, and the principal consented specifically to the agent's judgment (ra'y), not to another's. Grasp that personal trust is non-transferable.
The term 'rahmah' indicates the contract is based on mercy and confidence, not a property right.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf analogizes to mudaraba: if a mudarib dies and the capital is merchandise, the executor may sell. He extends this to agency if the agent appointed an executor. Identify the opposing view and its basis.
The opposing school here is not another madhhab but a companion of Abu Hanifa.
4
Critique the analogy
The Hanafi response refutes the analogy: agency is a right upon the agent (obligation), not a right for him, so it is not inheritable. Mudaraba is a right for the mudarib (to profit), hence inheritable. Also, a mudarib can delegate during life, an agent cannot.
This highlights the principle of distinguishing based on the nature of the right (haqq 'alayh vs. haqq lahu).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred position (mufta bihi) is that agency ends with death; Abu Yusuf's view is not acted upon. Confirm that the practical consequence is clear: the agent's executor cannot sell the principal's property.
The strength of the majority view lies in the consistent application of inheritance rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وتبطل بموت الوكيل حتى لا يقوم وارثه ولا وصيه مقامه) لأن الوكالة رحمه لا يجري فيها الإرث ولأن الموكل رضي برأيه لا برأي غيره. وعن أبي يوسف أنه إن وصى الوكيل يملك بيعه لأن الوكالة لازمة فيملك الوصي كالمضارب إذا مات والمالية عروض المضارب بيعها لما أنه لازم بعد ما صار عروضاً . قلنا : الوكالة حق على الوكيل فلا تورث عنه لأن الإرث يجري في حق له لا في حق عليه فوجب القول ببطلانها لا بخلاف المضاربة لأنها حق المضارب فيورث عنه فتقوم الورثة مقامه فيه، ولأن المضارب له ولاية التوكيل في حياته فجاز أن يقوم وصيه مقامه بعد وفاته كالأب في مال الصغير والوكيل ليس له حق التوكيل في حياته فلا يقوم غيره مقامه بعد موته.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And it becomes invalid by the death of the agent, so that neither his heir nor his executor takes his place.' Because agency is a covenant of mercy, inheritance does not apply in it, and because the principal consented to his opinion, not to another's. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if the agent appoints an executor, he may sell because the agency is binding, so the executor may sell, like the mudarib when he dies and the capital is merchandise, the mudarib's executor sells it because it becomes binding after it becomes merchandise. We say: Agency is a right upon the agent, so it is not inherited from him, because inheritance applies to rights in his favor, not to obligations. So it is necessary to say it becomes invalid, unlike mudaraba, because it is a right of the mudarib, so it is inherited from him, and the heirs take his place in it. And because the mudarib has the authority to appoint an agent during his lifetime, so it is permissible that his executor takes his place after his death, like the father over the property of a minor. The agent does not have the right to appoint an agent during his lifetime, so no one else takes his place after his death.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute. The base text (matn) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that the agency becomes void with the death of the agent, so neither his heir nor his executor succeeds him. The commentator (sahib al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) explains the reasoning: agency is a contract based on personal trust (ra'y), which is not inheritable. Abu Yusuf reported a contrary opinion: if the agent appointed an executor, that executor can sell, analogizing to mudaraba where the executor can sell if the capital becomes merchandise. The Hanafi response rejects this analogy: agency is a right upon the agent (obligation), not a right in his favor, so it does not pass to heirs. Mudaraba is a right for the mudarib (to profit), so it is inheritable. Also, a mudarib can delegate during his life, so his executor can too; an agent cannot delegate, so his executor cannot act. Thus the ruling stands with the majority Hanafi position.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakala): A contract of agency where one person appoints another to act on his behalf.
مضاربة (mudaraba): A profit-sharing partnership where one provides capital and the other labor.
وصي (wasi): Executor or guardian appointed by will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school rule that agency ends with the agent's death without succession?
A) Because the principal can always sell the property himself.
B) Because agency is a right upon the agent, not a right for him, so it is not inheritable.
C) Because the agent's executor is not trustworthy.
D) Because the contract of agency is void from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
Agency terminates upon the agent's death because it is a personal trust and an obligation, not an inheritable right.

Rulings on the 'Adl's Sale and Disputes in Pawn
Multiple rulings on the 'adl's sale in pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the 'adl's authority to sell, resolve price disputes, determine the term, and handle defect returns in a pawn contract.

Core Idea
The 'adl's authority is personal and limited; his sale is governed by strict rules to protect the rahin and murtahin.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq collects key rulings on the actions of the 'adl (trustee) in a pawn contract. Understanding these rules is essential for anyone involved in pawn transactions governed by Hanafi fiqh. We will explore the boundaries of the 'adl's empowerment, disputes over price and term, and the consequences of defects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the 'adl's role
The 'adl is a trustee holding the pawn; his empowerment is personal and limited. Death or incurable insanity voids his authority. Travel with the pawn is restricted in dangerous conditions.
2
Analyze disputes over the sale price
When the 'adl, murtahin, and rahin disagree on the price, the murtahin's statement is taken with his oath. If evidence is produced, the rahin's evidence prevails because it contradicts the 'adl's claim.
The murtahin is the creditor, so his claim about what he received is accepted.
3
Determine the validity of credit sales
Credit sales are generally permissible, but unusual credit periods (e.g., ten years) are invalid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. If the rahin indicated a need for cash, credit is also invalid.
The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ from Abu Hanifa in some details.
4
Assess the 'adl's capacity and travel restrictions
If the 'adl becomes incurably insane, he is removed; if temporary, he remains. He cannot travel with the pawn on dangerous roads, and is tied to the city.
Safe travel does not permit removal of the pawn from the city.
5
Handle defects after sale
If the sold item is returned due to a defect, the 'adl recovers from the rahin, unless he admitted a defect that arose during his possession. If the rahin confirms the defect existed, the 'adl recovers from him.
If the 'adl chooses to recover from one and that person becomes insolvent, he cannot recover from the other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة: لو مات العدل بطل التسليط . وفي السراجية : العدل المسلط على البيع إذا باع البعض بطل الرهن في الباقي، وإذا باع العدل الرهن ووقع الاختلاف بين الراهن والمرتهن والعدل في مقدار الثمن فقال العدل بعت بمائة فأعطيتها المرتهن وقال المرتهن باعه بخمسين فالقول للمرتهن مع يمينه؛ كذا في الخانية، وإن أقام البينة فالبينة بينة الراهن، وإذا كان العدل مسلطاً على البيع إذا حل الأجل فقال المرتهن كان الأجل إلى شهر رمضان وقد دخل شهر رمضان وقال الراهن إلى شوال فالقول قول الراهن في وقت حلول الأجل القول قول المرتهن وإذا باع العدل بالنسيئة جاز البيع من غير تفصيل؛ كذا في الأصل. وفي غيره : إذا باع بنسيئة غير معهودة بأن باع إلى عشر سنين ينبغي أن لا تجوز عندهما. وقال القاضي أبو علي النسفي : إن تقدم من الراهن ما يدل على البيع بالنقد بأن قال المرتهن يطالبني بدينه ويؤذيني فبعه حتى أوفيه فباعه بالنسيئة لا يجوز بمنزلة ما لو قال بعه فإني محتاج إلى النفقة وفي الذخيرة: لو كان المرتهن هو فقال له الراهن بعه واستوف دينك من ثمنه فباعه بالنسيئة يجوز كيفما كان. وقال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : لو لحق العدل جنون يقع الإياس من إفاقته فينعزل، وإن كان يرجى إفاقته لا ينعزل حتى إذا عاد عقله إليه له أن يبيع وإن باع في حال جنونه والعدل في يصح، حق العين كالمودع فما جاز للمودع جاز للعدل ولا يملك أن يسافر بالرهن إذا كانت الطريق مخيفة، وإذا كان الطريق آمناً وقيد بالمصر لا يملك السفر، وفي الغياثية : إذا مات المرتهن يبيع العدل العين المرهونة بحضرة الورثة ولو باع العدل ثم رد عليه بعيب رجع به على الراهن إلا أن يكون الرد عليه بإقراره بعيب جاز إن يحدث في المدة ولو صدقه الراهن بالعيب في يده يرجع به عليه، ولو اختار العدل أحدهما فأفلس ليس له أن يرجع على الآخر.
In al-Dhakhira: If the 'adl dies, the empowerment is void. In al-Sirajiyya: The 'adl empowered to sell, if he sells part, the pawn becomes void in the remainder. If the 'adl sells the pawn and a dispute occurs between the rahin, murtahin, and 'adl regarding the amount of the price: the 'adl says 'I sold for one hundred and gave it to the murtahin', and the murtahin says 'he sold it for fifty', then the word is with the murtahin with his oath; as in al-Khaniyya. If he produces evidence, the evidence of the rahin is accepted. If the 'adl is empowered to sell when the term matures, and the murtahin says 'the term was until Ramadan and Ramadan has entered', and the rahin says 'until Shawwal', then the word is that of the rahin regarding the maturation of the term, the word is that of the murtahin. If the 'adl sells on credit, the sale is permissible without detail; as in al-Asl. In others: if he sells on an unusual credit, e.g., selling for ten years, it should not be permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi said: If there was prior indication from the rahin that he wanted cash, e.g., he said 'the murtahin is demanding his debt and bothering me, so sell it until I pay him', and he sold on credit, it is not permissible, like if he said 'sell it for I need maintenance'. In al-Dhakhira: If it is the murtahin himself, and the rahin said to him 'sell it and take your debt from its price', and he sold on credit, it is permissible regardless. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: If the 'adl is struck by insanity such that recovery is despaired of, he is removed; if recovery is hoped for, he is not removed, so when his reason returns he may sell. If he sells while insane, it is not valid. The 'adl is like a trustee (mudi') regarding the property; what is permissible for the mudi' is permissible for the 'adl. He may not travel with the pawn if the road is dangerous; if the road is safe and tied to the city, he may not travel. In al-Ghiyathiyya: If the murtahin dies, the 'adl sells the pawned property in the presence of the heirs. If the 'adl sells and then it is returned due to a defect, he recovers from the rahin, unless the return was due to his admission of a defect that occurred during the period. If the rahin confirms the defect in his possession, he recovers from him. If the 'adl chooses one of them and he becomes insolvent, he may not recover from the other.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage collects several rulings concerning the 'adl (trustee) in a pawn contract. The 'adl is like a depositary; his authority is personal. If he dies, the empowerment lapses. If he sells part of the pawn, the entire pawn contract is void? (Actually: 'batal al-rahin fi al-baqi' - the pawn becomes void in the remainder, meaning the remaining portion is no longer held as pawn, likely requiring the debt to be settled differently). In disputes about the sale price, the murtahin's statement is taken (with oath) because he is the creditor and his claim is about what he received. But if both parties produce evidence, the rahin's evidence is given priority because it contradicts the 'adl's claim? Actually, the text: 'أقام البينة فالبينة بينة الراهن' - if evidence is produced, the evidence of the rahin is accepted. This is because the rahin is the owner and his witness testifies against the 'adl's claim of sale at a high price. Regarding the term, if the murtahin claims it was Ramadan and the rahin says Shawwal, the rahin's word is taken (the debtor's claim is accepted) because the term is a condition favorable to the rahin. The 'adl's sale on credit is generally permissible, but if it is an unusual period (like 10 years), it is not allowed according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. However, if the rahin indicated a need for cash, selling on credit is invalid. If the murtahin himself sells (with permission), credit is permissible. The 'adl's capacity: if he becomes incurably insane, he is removed; if temporary, he remains. He cannot travel with the pawn if the road is dangerous. If the murtahin dies, the 'adl sells in the presence of the heirs. If the sold item is returned due to a defect, the 'adl recovers from the rahin, unless he admitted a defect that arose during his possession. If the rahin admits the defect existed, the 'adl recovers from him. If the 'adl chooses to recover from one of them and that person becomes insolvent, he cannot claim from the other.

Key Terms
عدل ('adl): A trustworthy third party appointed to hold the pawn and sell it if needed.
رهن (rahn): The pawned property itself, or the contract of pawn.
تسليط (taslit): Empowerment given to the 'adl to sell the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The rahin, because he is the owner.
C) The murtahin, with his oath.
D) All parties are equally believed.

Key Takeaway
The 'adl's authority is personal and limited; disputes over price and term are resolved in favor of the creditor or debtor based on specific rules, and defect returns are recoverable from the rahin.

The 'Adl's Authority: Selling on Credit and in Different Currency
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of the 'adl's sale authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the 'adl's sale on credit and for different currency, and evaluate which position is the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The 'Adl's empowerment is absolute per Abu Hanifa, but Sahibayn restrict it to fair price and standard currency to prevent harm.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses two interconnected issues: whether the 'adl (trustee) of a pawn can sell it on credit, and whether he can sell it for a currency different from the debt. While the base text in al-Asl gives broad permission, later sources record a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The practical difference matters because it determines the validity of many pawn sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers: (1) selling the pawn on credit (nasi'a), and (2) selling the pawn for a currency different from the debt's currency. Determine what each scenario involves.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the 'adl's empowerment is absolute (mutlaq). He may sell for any price (high or low) and in any currency. If sold for different currency, he must exchange the proceeds into the debt currency before paying the creditor.
The power is like a general agency; no inherent restrictions unless stated by the rahin.
3
State the Sahibayn's objections
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict the 'adl: (a) sale must be in dirhams and dinars (gold/silver), (b) price must be fair market value or slightly less (taghabun al-nas), and (c) credit sale with an unusually long term (e.g., ten years) is invalid. They aim to protect the rahin from harm (ghabn fahish).
Their view is recorded in other works like al-Dhakhira.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the sale is valid regardless of price and currency (with exchange obligation). Under the Sahibayn, the sale must be in standard currency at fair value; an unusual credit term invalidates the sale.
This affects both the 'adl's liability and the validity of the transaction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
According to later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Haskafi, Ibn Abidin), the cautious fatwa leans towards the Sahibayn's position because it better safeguards the rahin's interests, although the absolute view remains a valid opinion within the school.
The passage notes a contradiction with al-Asl, but the later consensus has shifted toward the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا باع العدل بالنسيئة جاز البيع من غير تفصيل؛ كذا في الأصل. وفي غيره : إذا باع بنسيئة غير معهودة بأن باع إلى عشر سنين ينبغي أن لا تجوز عندهما. وقال القاضي أبو علي النسفي : إن تقدم من الراهن ما يدل على البيع بالنقد بأن قال المرتهن يطالبني بدينه ويؤذيني فبعه حتى أوفيه فباعه بالنسيئة لا يجوز بمنزلة ما لو قال بعه فإني محتاج إلى النفقة وفي الذخيرة: لو كان المرتهن هو فقال له الراهن بعه واستوف دينك من ثمنه فباعه بالنسيئة يجوز كيفما كان. ... قال الحاكم أبو الفضل : هذا الجواب خلاف جواب الأصل شرح الطحاوي فإن سلط العدل على البيع وأداء الثمن منه جاز بيعه عند أبي حنيفة فيما عز وهان وبأي ثمن كان من قبيل المطلق بالبيع فإن باعه بجنس الدين فإنه يقضي دينه من الثمن، وإن باعه بخلاف جنس الدين فإنه يبيع الثمن بجنس الدين ويقضي دين المرتهن. وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى يبيعه بالدراهم والدنانير بمثل قيمته أو أقل بقدر ما يتغابن الناس فيه فإن باعه بجنس الدين قضى به الدين، وإن باعه بخلاف جنسه صرفه بجنس الدين وقضى الدين.
If the 'adl sells on credit, the sale is permissible without detail; as in al-Asl. In others: if he sells on an unusual credit, e.g., selling for ten years, it should not be permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi said: If there was prior indication from the rahin that he wanted cash, e.g., he said 'the murtahin is demanding his debt and bothering me, so sell it until I pay him', and he sold on credit, it is not permissible, like if he said 'sell it for I need maintenance'. In al-Dhakhira: If it is the murtahin himself, and the rahin said to him 'sell it and take your debt from its price', and he sold on credit, it is permissible regardless. ... Al-Hakim Abu al-Fadl said: This answer contradicts the answer in al-Asl and Sharh al-Tahawi. For if the 'adl is empowered to sell and pay from its price, his sale is permissible according to Abu Hanifa whether the price is high or low, and with any price, as a general authorization to sell. If he sells it for the same type as the debt, he pays the debt from the price. If he sells it for a different type, he exchanges that price for the same type as the debt and pays the murtahin's debt. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, he sells it for dirhams and dinars at its value or less by the amount people usually overlook in transactions. If he sells it for the same type as the debt, he pays the debt with it. If he sells it for a different type, he exchanges it for the same type and pays the debt.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage discusses two issues: selling the pawn on credit, and selling for a currency different from the debt. The base text (al-Asl) says selling on credit is generally permissible without detail. Other sources restrict this: if the credit term is unusually long (e.g., 10 years), it is not permissible according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Additionally, if the rahin indicated he needed cash (e.g., because the murtahin is pressuring him), selling on credit is invalid because it contradicts the rahin's intent. However, if the murtahin himself sells with the rahin's permission to take his debt from the price, credit is always permissible. On the second issue: if the 'adl is empowered to sell and pay the debt from the price, Abu Hanifa allows sale for any price (high or low) and for any currency. If the sale is for the same currency as the debt, he pays directly; if different, he must exchange the proceeds for the debt currency and then pay. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict the sale to dirhams and dinars (gold/silver) at market value or slightly less (by the amount people tolerate). They require the sale to be in the same currency as the debt if possible, otherwise exchange first. This shows a difference in the extent of the 'adl's discretion: Abu Hanifa gives broad authority, while the Sahibayn impose restrictions to protect the interests of both parties.

Key Terms
نسيئة (nasi'a): Credit sale, where payment is deferred.
جنس الدين (jins al-dayn): The type of currency in which the debt is denominated.
تغابن الناس (taghabun al-nas): The small difference in price that people normally overlook in transactions.
عدل ('adl): The trustee or agent who holds the pawn and is authorized to sell it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), what must the 'adl sell the pawn for?
A) Any currency the buyer offers.
B) Only what the debt is denominated in.
C) Dirhams and dinars (gold/silver coins).
D) Only the currency of the rahin's choice.

Key Takeaway
The 'adl's authority is debated: absolute per Abu Hanifa, restricted by Sahibayn to fair price and standard currency; the cautious fatwa follows the latter.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

8 min
The Ruling on Selling a Pawned Item: Valid but Suspended
States the ruling and its rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sale of a pawned item and explain why it is suspended (mawquf).

Core Idea
A pawned item may be sold, but the sale is suspended until the mortgagee permits or the debt is paid.

This lesson establishes the fundamental ruling for when a pledgor sells an item that is currently held as collateral. The sale is not immediately effective but is valid in itself – it is suspended (mawquf) on a condition. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the law of mortgage (rahn) in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling on a pledgor selling the pawned item? The passage states: 'The sale of a pawn is suspended on the permission of its mortgagee or the payment of his debt.'
2
Classify the ruling
This is a sahih mawquf – valid in essence but its effect is contingent. It is not batil (void) nor immediately nafidh (effective).
Hanafis use mawquf for contracts valid in formation but needing ratification.
3
Identify the reason for suspension
The suspension is due to the mortgagee's right of detention (haqq al-habs). The sale cannot override that right without the mortgagee's consent or the debt being discharged.
The impediment (mani') is the attached right of the mortgagee.
4
Note the consequence
If the mortgagee permits or the pledgor pays the debt, the sale becomes effective. If not, the buyer may litigate and the judge will revoke the sale.
The passage mentions: 'for the judge would revoke it if the matter is brought to him and the buyer demands delivery.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتوقف بيع الرهن على إجازة مرتهنه أو قضاء دينه. اختلفت عبارة محمد رحمه الله تعالى في هذه المسألة؛ قال في موضع بيع المرهون فاسد، وفي موضع جائز، والصحيح أنه جائز موقوف، وقوله فاسد محمول على إذا لم يجز المرتهن فإن القاضي يفسد إذا خوصم إليه وطلب المشتري تسليمه، وقوله جائز بمعنى محمول على ما إذا أجاز وسلمه. وفي الجامع: باع الراهن الرهن فالبيع باطل؛ قيل معناه سيبطل، وعن أبي يوسف ينفذ سواء علم المرتهن بالبيع أو لا، وإنما يتوقف لأنه تعلق به حق المرتهن وفي بقائه إبطال حقه فلا ينفذ إلا بإجازته أو بقضاء الراهن الدين لزوال المعنى وهو تعلق حق المرتهن.
The sale of a pawn is suspended on the permission of its mortgagee or the payment of his debt. The expressions of Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) differ on this issue: in one place he said the sale of a pawn is void, and in another it is valid. The correct view is that it is valid but suspended. His statement 'void' is interpreted as when the mortgagee does not permit, for the judge would revoke it if the matter is brought to him and the buyer demands delivery. His statement 'valid' is interpreted as when the mortgagee permits and delivers. In al-Jami': if the pledgor sells the pawn, the sale is invalid; it is said its meaning is that it will become invalid. According to Abu Yusuf, it is effective whether the mortgagee knows of the sale or not. It is suspended only because the right of the mortgagee is attached to it, and its continuation would nullify his right, so it is not effective except with his permission or the pledgor's payment of the debt, because the reason (the attachment of the mortgagee's right) ceases.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a pledgor selling the pawned item. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that Imam Muhammad's statements appear contradictory, but the correct position is that the sale is valid but suspended (ja'iz mawquf). The sale does not become immediately effective because the mortgagee has a right to detain the pawn (haqq al-habs). Once the mortgagee permits or the debt is repaid, the sale becomes effective. Abu Yusuf's view that the sale is effective regardless is less relied upon. The suspension is due to the impediment of the mortgagee's right; once that impediment is removed, the sale proceeds.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): A contract that is valid in itself but its effect is suspended on a condition (like permission).
مرتهن (murtahin): The mortgagee – the person who holds the pawn as security for a debt.
راهن (rahin): The pledgor – the person who gives the pawn as security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position, what is the status of a sale of a pawned item without the mortgagee's permission?
A) Void (batil)
B) Valid and effective
C) Valid but suspended (mawquf)
D) Voidable (fasid)

Key Takeaway
A pawned item can be sold, but the sale is suspended until the mortgagee permits or the debt is paid, due to the mortgagee's right of detention.
