Reconciling Imam Muhammad's Contradictory Statements on the Pawn Sale
Explains the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and reconciliation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the apparent contradictions in Imam Muhammad's statements regarding the sale of a pawn and identify the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad said both ‘void’ and ‘valid’; the school reconciles them: void without permission, valid with it.

This lesson delves into the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning the sale of a pawned item. Imam Muhammad's transmitted statements appear contradictory – sometimes calling the sale ‘fasid’ (void) and sometimes ‘ja’iz’ (valid). The later Hanafi masters harmonize these statements, and we must understand the reconciliation to correctly apply the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the apparent contradiction
In some transmissions, Muhammad says the sale of a pawn is fasid (void). In others, he says it is ja'iz (valid). These seem opposed.
2
Identify the reconciliation
The correct view is that the sale is ja'iz mawquf (valid but suspended). ‘Fasid’ is interpreted as the case where the mortgagee does not permit, and the judge will revoke it. ‘Ja'iz’ is the case where the mortgagee permits and delivers.
The passage says: 'His statement 'void' is interpreted as when the mortgagee does not permit... His statement 'valid' is interpreted as when the mortgagee permits and delivers.'
3
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds that the sale is effective (nafidh) regardless of the mortgagee's knowledge or permission. This is a distinct position within the school.
The passage mentions: 'According to Abu Yusuf, it is effective whether the mortgagee knows of the sale or not.'
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the suspended (mawquf) view, as it balances the pledgor's right to sell with the mortgagee's right of detention.
The passage states: 'The correct view is that it is valid but suspended.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتوقف بيع الرهن على إجازة مرتهنه أو قضاء دينه. اختلفت عبارة محمد رحمه الله تعالى في هذه المسألة؛ قال في موضع بيع المرهون فاسد، وفي موضع جائز، والصحيح أنه جائز موقوف، وقوله فاسد محمول على إذا لم يجز المرتهن فإن القاضي يفسد إذا خوصم إليه وطلب المشتري تسليمه، وقوله جائز بمعنى محمول على ما إذا أجاز وسلمه. وفي الجامع: باع الراهن الرهن فالبيع باطل؛ قيل معناه سيبطل، وعن أبي يوسف ينفذ سواء علم المرتهن بالبيع أو لا، وإنما يتوقف لأنه تعلق به حق المرتهن وفي بقائه إبطال حقه فلا ينفذ إلا بإجازته أو بقضاء الراهن الدين لزوال المعنى وهو تعلق حق المرتهن.
The sale of a pawn is suspended on the permission of its mortgagee or the payment of his debt. The expressions of Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) differ on this issue: in one place he said the sale of a pawn is void, and in another it is valid. The correct view is that it is valid but suspended. His statement 'void' is interpreted as when the mortgagee does not permit, for the judge would revoke it if the matter is brought to him and the buyer demands delivery. His statement 'valid' is interpreted as when the mortgagee permits and delivers. In al-Jami': if the pledgor sells the pawn, the sale is invalid; it is said its meaning is that it will become invalid. According to Abu Yusuf, it is effective whether the mortgagee knows of the sale or not. It is suspended only because the right of the mortgagee is attached to it, and its continuation would nullify his right, so it is not effective except with his permission or the pledgor's payment of the debt, because the reason (the attachment of the mortgagee's right) ceases.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a pledgor selling the pawned item. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that Imam Muhammad's statements appear contradictory, but the correct position is that the sale is valid but suspended (ja'iz mawquf). The sale does not become immediately effective because the mortgagee has a right to detain the pawn (haqq al-habs). Once the mortgagee permits or the debt is repaid, the sale becomes effective. Abu Yusuf's view that the sale is effective regardless is less relied upon. The suspension is due to the impediment of the mortgagee's right; once that impediment is removed, the sale proceeds.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): A contract that is valid in itself but its effect is suspended on a condition (like permission).
توفيق (tawfiq): Reconciliation of apparently conflicting texts by interpreting each in its proper context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It applies when the mortgagee permits the sale

Claim of Offspring from a Mortgaged Slave: Solvency and Sa'aya
Ruling on a pledgor claiming child from mortgaged slave woman with sa'aya obligations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a pledgor claims a child from a mortgaged slave woman, distinguishing between solvent and insolvent pledgor, and explain the sa'aya distribution.

Core Idea
A pledgor's claim of a child from a mortgaged slave triggers immediate payment if solvent, or shared sa'aya if insolvent.

When a mortgaged slave woman gives birth, the child becomes part of the pledge. But what happens if the pledgor claims the child as his own? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling, which hinges on the pledgor's solvency. It also introduces a nuanced qiyas reasoning for the child's obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the pledgor's solvency
Recognize that the ruling changes based on whether the pledgor is solvent or insolvent. Identify both branches from the text.
2
Apply the ruling for the solvent pledgor
The solvent pledgor must pay the debt immediately because his claim destroys the pledgee's right to hold the child.
3
Apply the ruling for the insolvent pledgor
Both mother and child must work (sa'aya) to pay half the debt each. The child is considered a principal debtor (asl) in the pledge.
4
Trace the qiyas for the child's status
The child becomes a principal because the right of detention (haqq al-habs) carried over from the mother at birth, and the pledgor's claim equates to a purchase.
The qiyas is khafi: it uses the shared illa of haqq al-habs.
5
Handle the exceptional case: mother dies before child completes sa'aya
If the mother dies, the child pays only the lesser of his value and half the debt. Nothing extra is added because the child is not a follower of the mother in sa'aya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا رهن أمة قيمتها ألف بألف فجاءت بولد يساوي ألفاً فادعاه الراهن وهو موسر ضمن المال لإتلاف حق المرتهن بالدعوى، وإن كان معسراً سعت الأمة في نصف المال والولد في نصفه لأن في حالة الإعسار لا يجب إلا السعاية، وكل واحد منهما صار أصلاً؛ الأم بالاستيلاد والولد بالإعتاق لأنه بالإعتاق صار مشترياً الولد فيصير الولد أصلاً في الرهن كالأم لأن الولد لما حدث سرى إليه ما كان في الأم من حق الحبس فصار مرهوناً كالأم، فإن لم يؤد الولد حتى ماتت الأم قبل أن يفرغ من السعاية يسعى في الأقل من قيمته ونصف الدين ولا يزاد عليه شيء بموت الأم لأن الولد حدث قبل وجود السعاية على الأم فلا يكون تبعاً لها في السعاية.
If he pawns a slave woman worth one thousand for one thousand, and she gives birth to a child worth one thousand, and the pledgor claims the child while he is solvent, he must pay the debt because he destroyed the pledgee's right by his claim. If he is insolvent, the slave woman works to pay half the debt and the child (works to pay) half, because in a state of insolvency only sa'aya (earning by labor) is required. Each of them becomes a principal (asl): the mother through istilad (bearing a child that becomes free by the master's claim) and the child through i'taq (emancipation by the pledgor's claim), because by claiming him he becomes a purchaser of the child. Thus the child becomes a principal in the pledge like the mother, because when the child came into existence, the right of detention (haqq al-habs) that was in the mother carried over to him, so he becomes mortgaged like the mother. If the child does not pay until the mother dies before completing the sa'aya, he (the child) works to pay the lesser of his value and half the debt, and nothing is added to it by the mother's death, because the child came into existence before the sa'aya was imposed on the mother, so he is not a follower of her in the sa'aya.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling concerning a scenario where a mortgaged slave woman (ama) gives birth after the mortgage. The pledgor (rahin) claims the child as his own. The ruling distinguishes based on the pledgor's financial status. If the pledgor is solvent (maysir), he must immediately pay off the debt because his claiming the child effectively destroys the pledgee's (murtahin) right to hold the child as part of the collateral. If the pledgor is insolvent (mu'sir), the debt is not immediately due; instead, both the mother and the child must work (sa'aya) to pay off the debt, each being responsible for half. The justification is that in insolvency, only sa'aya is required. The child is considered an original (asl) debtor through the pledgor's claim, which is treated as a purchase of the child by the pledgor, akin to emancipation. The right of detention (haqq al-habs) that applies to the mother also applies to the child from birth. A special case: if the mother dies before the child completes his half of the sa'aya, the child only pays the lesser of his value or half the debt; he is not burdened with the mother's remaining portion because the child was born before the mother's sa'aya was imposed, so he is not a follower in her obligation.

Key Terms
سعاية (sa'aya): Earning by labor to pay off a debt; here it refers to the obligation of the slave and child to work to pay the mortgage debt.
استيلاد (istilad): The act of a master impregnating his slave woman, resulting in the child being considered free and the mother becoming an umm walad.
إعتاق (i'taq): Emancipation of a slave; here used metaphorically for the pledgor's claim of the child, which is treated as a purchase (and thus emancipation from the mortgage).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mortgaged slave woman gives birth and the insolvent pledgor claims the child, who is responsible for the debt?
A) Only the mother must work to pay the entire debt.
B) The mother and child must each work to pay half the debt.
C) The pledgor must pay the debt immediately.
D) The child is free of any obligation.

Key Takeaway
The child of a mortgaged slave woman becomes a principal in the pledge, and upon the pledgor's claim, his obligation depends on the pledgor's solvency.

Kitaba and Tadbir of Mortgaged Slaves: The Principle of Avoiding Harm to the Pledgee
Rulings on kitaba and tadbir of a mortgaged slave and her offspring

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on kitaba and tadbir of a mortgaged slave, explain why tadbir does not constitute actual possession (qabd) when it harms the pledgee, and apply the principle of avoiding harm to determine the correct debt apportionment among multiple generations of slaves.

Core Idea
Tadbir is only a virtual qabd; it is disregarded when it prejudices the pledgee's right.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the interplay between mortgage (rahn) and manumission contracts (kitaba and tadbir). When a master makes a kitaba for a mortgaged slave, the pledgee can annul it because it would void the pledge. However, tadbir (postponed manumission) is treated differently: it is a valid act but does not automatically transfer possession to the pledgor in a way that reduces the pledgee's security. The passage presents detailed case studies and a dispute with 'Isa ibn Aban, ultimately relying on the maxim 'harm is removed' (al-darar yuzal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two manumission contracts
Kitaba (contract for freedom) and tadbir (freedom upon death) are the two acts discussed. Note the different effect on the pledge: kitaba can be rescinded, tadbir is valid but virtual.
The pledgee's right to rescind kitaba is absolute; for tadbir, the effect is limited.
2
Trace the debt apportionment across generations
Follow how the debt (sa'aya) extends from a slave to her children born after the mortgage. The passage provides several multi-generational examples; work through one to see how the debt is divided.
Debt is divided proportionally among slaves of equal value; if values differ, the ratio applies.
3
Locate the point of dispute with 'Isa ibn Aban
He argues that tadbir constitutes qabd (possession), which would change the debt division. Find his claim and the Hanafi response.
The dispute is about the nature of tadbir: real or virtual possession.
4
Understand the Hanafi response based on harm prevention
The text explains that tadbir is only a virtual qabd; it is not considered when it would harm the pledgee. This is the key legal principle.
The maxim 'al-darar yuzal' (harm must be removed) overrides the virtual possession.
5
Apply the principle to the given scenarios
Verify that the final ruling (e.g., lower daughter pays half, not two-thirds) follows from this principle.
The principle is consistently applied in all cases to protect the pledgee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا رهن أمة بألف وقيمتها خمسمائة فكاتبها المولى فللمرتهن فسخها لأن الكتابة تتضمن إبطال حق المرتهن لأن المكاتب لم يصلح رهناً لأنه لو أدى بدل الكتابة عتق ويبطل الرهن، وكذلك لو نفذت الكتابة يبطل الرهن لأنه لا يمكنه البيع والكتابة مما تحتمل الفسخ فتنفسخ فلو لم يكاتبها ولكن دبرها فسعت في قيمتها ثم ماتت عن بنت تساوي خمسمائة فعلى ولدها أن يسعى في خمسمائة لأنه يسري ما فيها من الدين إلى التي ولدتها أمتى ولدت فيصير مدبراً تبعاً للأصل، فإن سعت البنت في مائة ثم ولدت بنتاً ثم ماتت البنت الأولى وقيمة الأولى والسفلى سواء تسعى السفلى في الباقي كله لأنه يسري ما فيها إلى ولدها كما يجري من الجدة إلى الوسطى رهن أمتين قيمة كل واحد ألف فدبرها المولى ثم ماتت إحداهما سعت الباقية في نصف الدين ويضمن المولى نصفه لأنها ماتت بعدما خرجت من الرهن بالتدبير ولا يتحول شيء من دين الميتة إلى الباقية لأن الباقية لم تكن متولدة من الميتة والميتة في السعاية كانت محتملة على المولى، فإذا ماتت قبل استيفاء السعاية فقد تعذر استيفاء حقه من جهة المحتمل وهو الكفيل فيطالب من الأصيل، فإن ولدت هذه الباقية ثم ماتت يسعى الولد فيما على أمه وسواء كانت قيمة الأم أقل أو أكثر لأنها ولدت بمثل حالها مدبرة فيسري ما فيها إلى ولدها ولو كانت قبل التدبير ثم دبرهما جميعاً سعت في مائتين وخمسين إن كانت قيمتها مثل قيمة الأم لأن الولد قبل التدبير صار رهناً فانقسم ما في الأم من الدين عليهما نصفين على سبيل التوفيق إن ورد على الولد قبض الرهن بقي كذلك منقسماً، وإن لم يرد عليه قبض بطل الانقسام وظهر أن الدين كله كان بإزاء الأم، وهنا ورد على الراهن قبض على الولد لما ذكرنا لأن التدبير من المشتري قبل القبض يصير به قابضاً. رهن أمة بألف وقيمتها ألف فولدت ولداً يساوي ألفاً فماتت الأم ثم دبر البنت عليها السعاية في خمسمائة ورد على الميت قبض الراهن فإنه بالتدبير صار قابضاً للولد فظهر أن الدين كان منقسماً عليهما نصفين، فإن ولدت البنت بنتاً وماتت البنت الأولى سعت السفلى في خمسمائة وإن كانت قيمتها مائة لأن السفلى ولد المستسعاة فسرى ما في أمها إليها. ولدت الأمة المرهونة بنتاً ثم ولدت البنت بنتاً وقيمة كل واحدة ألف ثم دبرهن جميعاً ثم ماتت الأم والبنت الأولى فعلى السفلى السعاية في نصف الدين وعن عيسى بن أبان قال : ينبغي أن تسعى في ثلثي الدين لأنه قد كان قابضاً للوسطى بالتدبير لأن التدبير قبض وصار بإزاء كل واحدة منهن الدين كما لو رهنهن جميعاً ثم دبرهن وهو معسر وقد ماتت بنتان قبل السعاية تسعى الباقية في ثلثي الدين فكذا هذا والجواب عنه أن التدبير ليس بقبض حقيقة ولكن اعتبر قبضاً حكماً بحكم الإتلاف كالإعتاق وإنما يعتبر قبضاً حكماً متى لم يكن في اعتباره قبضاً ضرر على المرتهن، وهنا في اعتباره قبضاً ضرر بالمرتهن لأنه يؤدي إلى إبطال حقه بالسعاية لأنه لم يعتبر قبضاً كان للمرتهن أن يستسعي السفلى في نصف الدين، ومتى اعتبر قبضاً يستسعيها في جزء واحد من أحد عشر جزءاً من الدين فلا يعتبر قابضاً دفعاً للضرر عنه فصار كأن الوسطى ماتت قبل التدبير فيصير بإزاء السفلى نصف الدين بخلاف المسألة المتقدمة لأنا لو اعتبرنا التدبير قبضاً ينتفع به المرتهن ولا يتضرر به لأن السفلى تسعى في جميع ما وجب على الوسطى، ومتى لم يعتبر قبضاً تسعى في جزء من أحد عشر حزءاً من الدين، وكذلك لو دبر السفلى بعدما ماتت الأم والجدة لأنه لا يحتسب بالوسطى إذا ماتت قبل التدبير فكأنها لم تكن ولدت الجدة إلا ولداً واحداً ثم دبر الولد ولدت أمة الرهن ولداً يساوي ألفا ثم دبرها فعلى كل واحد منهما سعاية في خمسمائة لما عرف وإن ماتت البنت سعت الأم في الألف كلها. طعن عيسى وقال : بالتدبير يقرر الضمان فيه ولا يعود إلى الأم.
If he pawns a slave woman worth one thousand for one thousand, and her value is five hundred, and then the master makes a kitaba contract (for her freedom), the pledgee has the right to annul it because kitaba involves annulling the pledgee's right: the mukatab is not suitable as a pledge because if he pays the kitaba price he becomes free and the pledge is void. Similarly, if the kitaba is executed, the pledge becomes void because the slave can no longer be sold, and kitaba can be rescinded, so it is rescinded. If he does not make a kitaba but instead makes a tadbir (postponed manumission), then she works to pay her value. Then she dies, leaving a daughter worth five hundred: the daughter must work to pay five hundred because the debt that is on her extends to the one she gave birth to. She becomes a mudabbara following the original. If the daughter worked to pay one hundred, then gave birth to a daughter, then the first daughter died, and the value of the first and the lower one are equal: the lower one works to pay the remainder entirely because it extends to her child as it extends from the grandmother to the middle one. If he pawns two slave women each worth one thousand, and the master makes a tadbir for both, then one of them dies: the remaining one works to pay half the debt, and the master guarantees half because she died after leaving the pledge by tadbir. Nothing of the dead woman's debt transfers to the remaining one because the remaining one is not a descendant of the dead one. The dead woman's sa'aya was a guarantee upon the master (as a surety). So if she dies before the sa'aya is completed, the pledgee's right to collect from the surety becomes impossible, so he demands from the principal. If the remaining one then gives birth and dies, her child works to pay what was on his mother, regardless of whether the mother's value is less or more, because she gave birth in her state as a mudabbara, so what is in her carries over to her child. If they were before tadbir and then he made tadbir for both, the daughter works to pay two hundred and fifty if her value is like the mother's value, because before tadbir the child became a pledge, so the debt on the mother divided between them in halves, tentatively. If the pledgee's receipt came to the child, it remains divided; if receipt did not come to him, the division is void and it appears that the entire debt was against the mother. Here, receipt from the pledgor came to the child as we mentioned, because tadbir by the buyer before receipt makes him a qabid. He pawns a slave woman worth one thousand for one thousand, and she gives birth to a child worth one thousand, then the mother dies, then he makes tadbir of the daughter: upon her is sa'aya for five hundred, and receipt from the dead one came to the pledgor, because by tadbir he became a qabid of the child, so it appears that the debt was divided between them in halves. Then the daughter gives birth to a daughter and the first daughter dies: the lower one works to pay five hundred even if her value is one hundred, because the lower one is the child of the one who was working, so what was in her mother carried over to her. A slave woman who is mortgaged gives birth to a daughter, then the daughter gives birth to a daughter, each worth one thousand. Then he makes tadbir for all of them, then the mother and first daughter die: the lower one must work to pay half the debt. From 'Isa ibn Aban: he said that she should work to pay two-thirds of the debt because he had become a qabid for the middle one by tadbir, because tadbir is a qabd, and the debt is against each of them as if he pawned all of them then made tadbir while he was insolvent, and two daughters died before sa'aya: the remaining one works to pay two-thirds. Similarly here. The answer: tadbir is not a real qabd but is considered a virtual qabd due to destruction like emancipation. It is only considered a virtual qabd when it does not harm the pledgee. Here, considering it a qabd would harm the pledgee because it would lead to annulling his right in the sa'aya. If not considered a qabd, the pledgee can demand sa'aya from the lower one for half the debt; if considered a qabd, he can demand only one part out of eleven from the debt. So it is not considered a qabd to avoid harm, so it is as if the middle one died before tadbir, and the lower one is against half the debt. This is different from the earlier case because there, if we consider tadbir a qabd, the pledgee benefits and is not harmed, because the lower one works to pay all that was due on the middle one. If it is not considered a qabd, she works to pay one part out of eleven. Similarly, if he makes tadbir of the lower one after the mother and grandmother died, because the middle one is not counted if she died before tadbir, so it is as if the grandmother gave birth to only one child, then he made tadbir of that child. A mortgaged slave woman gives birth to a child worth one thousand, then makes tadbir of it: each one has sa'aya for five hundred as known. If the daughter dies, the mother works to pay the entire thousand. 'Isa objected and said: by tadbir the liability is established and does not return to the mother.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This lengthy passage deals with kitaba (contract of manumission) and tadbir (postponed manumission) of a mortgaged slave woman and the rights of the pledgee. If the pledgor makes a kitaba, the pledgee can rescind it because it would destroy his right to hold the slave as security. If instead the pledgor makes a tadbir, the slave must work to pay the debt (sa'aya). The debt extends to the slave's children born after the mortgage. The passage provides multiple case studies: a single slave with children, two slaves, and several generations, calculating how the debt is apportioned among them. It also includes a dispute with 'Isa ibn Aban, who argued that tadbir constitutes legal possession (qabd) by the pledgor, which would change the debt division. The Hanafi position, however, is that tadbir is only a virtual qabd and is not considered when it would harm the pledgee; thus in the given scenario, the lower daughter only works to pay half the debt, not two-thirds as 'Isa claimed. The passage emphasizes the principle of avoiding harm to the pledgee (raf' al-darar).

Key Terms
كتابة (kitaba): A contract between a master and slave where the slave pays a sum for freedom; here the pledgee can rescind it because it impairs the pledge.
تدبير (tadbir): A declaration by the master that a slave will become free upon the master's death; here it does not transfer possession to the pledgor for the purpose of dividing the debt.
قبض (qabd): Possession or receipt; here debated whether tadbir constitutes qabd for the pledgor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the text, if a mortgaged slave woman gives birth to a daughter, and the pledgor makes tadbir of all (mother, daughter, granddaughter), then mother and first daughter die, how much must the lower daughter work to pay?
A) One-third of the debt.
B) Two-thirds of the debt.
C) Half of the debt.
D) All of the debt.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir is a virtual possession that is disregarded when it harms the pledgee, ensuring the pledge remains effective.

Destruction of the Pawn: Rulings for Owner and Third Party
Explains the rulings when the pawn is destroyed by the owner or a third party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the pawn is destroyed by the owner or a third party, and apply the qiyas to determine the mortgagee's right to the substitute.

Core Idea
When a pawn is destroyed, its value becomes a new pawn — the mortgagee's right transfers to the substitute.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq explains the rulings when a pawn is destroyed by the pledgor or by a stranger. The author uses qiyas to analogize it to freeing a pawn, and establishes that the mortgagee, not the pledgor, is the proper claimant for compensation from the third party. The value taken becomes a new pawn in place of the original. A subtle problem about valuation and market decline is resolved by noting that consumption changes the substance, so the debt adjusts accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios and their basic rulings
Read the passage and note the difference in ruling when the pawn is destroyed by the owner (pledgor) versus a third party. Underline the key phrases: 'if he destroys it while he is wealthy and the debt is due, he pays the value immediately' and 'if a third party destroys it, the mortgagee holds him liable for its value and it becomes a pawn with him'.
The owner's destruction is likened to freeing the pawn; the third party's destruction gives the mortgagee the right to claim.
2
Analyze the qiyas: Why is the mortgagee the proper claimant?
Focus on the phrase 'because he has more right to the actual pawn while it exists, similarly in recovering what stands in its place.' Identify the asl (original pawn) and far' (substitute value), and the illa (the mortgagee's preferential right).
This is a clear qiyas jaliy: the right to the original extends to its substitute.
3
Understand the valuation dispute and its resolution
Examine the problematic statement from al-Hidayah about debt reduction when value declines after consumption. Then read the response from al-'Inayah: consumption changes the substance, so the pawn cannot revert to original value. Contrast with the case where the pawn remains intact and price declines—no debt reduction occurs.
The key distinction: consumption (itlaf) alters the 'ayn, making it impossible to return to its original state, unlike mere market fluctuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( واتلاف الرهن كإعتاقه يعني أنه إذا أتلفه وهو موسر والدين حال أدى القيمة في الحال، وإن كان مؤجلاً أدى القيمة وجعلت رهناً مكانه حتى يحل الدين. قال رحمه الله : (وإن أتلفه أجنبي فالمرتهن يضمنه قيمته وتكون رهناً عنده) يعني أن المرتهن هو الخصم في تضمينه قيمته فتكون رهناً عنده لأنه أحق بعين الرهن حال قيامه فكذا في استرداد ما قام مقامه، والواجب في هذا المستهلك قيمته يوم هلك باستهلاكه بخلاف ضمان المرتهن وقد الاستهلاك خمسمائة تقدم بيانه حتى لو كانت قيمته ألفاً الارتهان يوم ويوم غرم خمسمائة ولو وكانت رهناً وسقط من الدين خمسمائة لأن المعبر في ضمان المرتهن الرهن يوم قبضه. استهلك المرتهن الرهن والدين مؤجل ضمن قيمته لأنه أتلف مال الغير وكانت رهناً في يده حتى يحل الأجل، ولو حل الدين والمضمون من جنس حقه استوفى المرتهن دينه منه ويرد الفضل على الراهن إذا كان هناك فضل، وإن كان دينه أكثر وقد كانت قيمته يوم الرهن قدر الدين وقد رجعت قيمته إلى خمسمائة وقد كانت يوم القبض ألفاً ضمن بالاستهلاك خمسمائة وسقط من الدين خمسمائة ؛ كذا في الهداية قال الشارح وهو مشكل فإن النقصان بتراجع السعر إذا لم يكن مضموناً عليه ولا معتبراً فكيف يسقط من الدين خمسمائة؟ ومثل هذا الاستشكال نقله صاحب العناية وأجاب بأن العين قد تغيرت بالاستهلاك فصارت لا تحتمل العود إلى القيمة الأولى بتراجع السعر، ولو كانت باقية ترجع على ما كانت باقية عليه بخلاف ما إذا لم تتغير العين وهي باقية على حالها وقد تراجع السعر لأن العين التي قبضها بحالها فلا يرجع شيء من الدين بتراجع السعر ؛ كذا في العناية فأفاد أن ما في الخلاصة من قوله «وأما
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And destroying the pawn is like freeing it' meaning that if he destroys it while he is wealthy and the debt is due, he pays the value immediately; and if it is deferred, he pays the value and it is made a pawn in its place until the debt matures. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And if a third party destroys it, the mortgagee holds him liable for its value and it becomes a pawn with him' meaning that the mortgagee is the party to claim compensation for its value, so it becomes a pawn with him because he has more right to the actual pawn while it exists, similarly in recovering what stands in its place. The obligatory (value) in this destroyed item is its value on the day it was destroyed by consumption, contrary to the guarantee of the mortgagee, and the consumption (value) is five hundred (as previously explained). So even if its value was one thousand on the day of pledging and on the day of receipt he paid five hundred, and it was a pawn, and five hundred of the debt falls away, because the criterion in the guarantee of the mortgagee is the pawn on the day he received it. If the mortgagee consumed the pawn while the debt was deferred, he is liable for its value because he destroyed the property of another, and it was a pawn in his hand until the term matures. And if the debt matures and the guaranteed item is of the same kind as his right, the mortgagee collects his debt from it and returns the surplus to the pledgor if there is surplus. And if his debt is more, and its value on the day of pledge equaled the debt, and its value decreased to five hundred while it was one thousand on the day of receipt, he is liable by consumption for five hundred and five hundred of the debt falls away. Thus in al-Hidayah. The commentator said: This is problematic, for the decrease by market decline is neither guaranteed nor considered, so how does five hundred fall from the debt? The author of al-'Inayah transmitted such a problem and answered that the substance has changed by consumption so it is not susceptible to return to the first value by market decline; if it had remained, it would have returned to its former state, unlike when the substance has not changed and it remains in its condition and the price declines, because the substance he received is unchanged, so nothing of the debt falls due to price decline. Thus in al-'Inayah, so it indicates that what is in al-Khulasa from his saying 'As for...'
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses two scenarios of destroying a pawn. First, when the pawn is destroyed by the pledgor himself: the ruling is analogized to freeing a pawn (discussed earlier). If the pledgor is wealthy and the debt is due, he must pay the pawn's value immediately. If the debt is deferred, he pays the value and that value becomes a new pawn in place of the original until the debt matures. Second, when a third party destroys the pawn: the mortgagee (not the pledgor) is the proper claimant to demand compensation. The compensation amount becomes a new pawn held by the mortgagee. The reason given is that the mortgagee has a preferential right to the pawn itself while it exists; by analogy, he has the right to its substitute. The valuation for compensation is based on the day the pawn was destroyed (its market value at that time). The author then relates an issue from al-Hidayah: if the pawn's value was 1000 at the time of pledge but only 500 at the time of consumption, and the debt was equal to the initial value, the mortgagee is liable for 500 and 500 of the debt falls away. The commentator notes a problem: market decline after receipt is not normally considered in liability, so why should the debt reduce? The solution from al-'Inayah is that consumption changes the substance itself, so it cannot return to its original value even if market conditions improve. If the pawn had remained intact and its price declined, no debt would fall because the same object is still there. The passage underscores that the guarantee of the mortgagee is based on the pawn's value at receipt, but consumption alters the ruling due to the change in substance.

Key Terms
اتلاف (itlāf): Destruction or consumption of the pawn by the pledgor or a third party, including freeing or destroying.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to pay compensation for destroying the pawn; the mortgagee becomes liable if he consumes it, but here it refers to the third party's liability.
تراجع السعر (tarāju' al-si'r): Decline in market price after the pawn was received.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a third party destroys a pawn, who is entitled to claim compensation?
A) The pledgor (raahin)
B) The mortgagee (murtahin)
C) Both equally
D) The qadi (judge)

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's right to the pawn transfers to its substitute when the pawn is destroyed by a third party.

Master's Options for a Mortgaged Slave's Tort: Surrender or Ransom
Ruling with proof via detailed illustrative scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to a master when his mortgaged slave commits a tort (jinaayah) against a person or property, apply the distinction between injury to a human and injury to property, and explain the consequences in multi-tort scenarios such as the well-digging case.

Core Idea
The master may choose to surrender the slave or pay compensation; liability transfers accordingly.

This passage from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl, expounded in Al-Bahr al-Raiq, establishes a pivotal rule in Hanafi muamalat: when a mortgaged slave commits a tort causing monetary liability, the master is given a choice (takhyir) between surrendering the slave (daf') or paying the compensation (fida'). The rule distinguishes between injury to a human being (aadami) and injury to property (maal). The passage then applies this rule to a complex scenario of a slave digging a well on a road, leading to multiple successive torts, and also considers the case where the slave is freed before the incident. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its distinctions, and the reasoning behind the liabilities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the master's options
Locate the core ruling: for a tort requiring monetary compensation, the master may either surrender the slave (daf') or ransom him by paying the blood money (fida'). Note that this applies when the slave is still in the master's ownership (mortgaged).
The ruling is from Imam Muhammad in al-Asl, a foundational Hanafi text.
2
Distinguish between injury to a human and injury to property
For injury to a human (aadami), the options are surrender or pay the arsh. For injury to property, the options are sell the slave and pay the price to the owner, or ransom the slave by paying the compensation directly. Note the difference: in property injury, the slave's sale is involved, while in human injury, direct surrender is allowed.
This distinction affects the mechanism of transferring liability.
3
Analyze the well-digging scenario
Follow the commentator's illustration: a slave digs a well on the road. If an animal falls in and the master sells the slave to pay the compensation, then if another animal falls in, the second owner's claim is against the first owner (who received the price). If a person falls in after the sale, his blood is wasted (hadar). If the slave was surrendered in person for the first injury (a person), and then another person falls in, the master remains liable because the slave is still in the hands of the first victim.
The key is that the master's choice determines whether liability transfers or remains.
4
Consider the variant where the slave is freed after digging
If the slave is freed after digging the well but before anyone falls in, then when a person falls in and dies, the master must pay the slave's value (since the slave is now free and cannot be surrendered). If a second person falls in, they share that value. If the freed slave himself falls in, according to one narration, his blood is wasted.
The emancipation changes the nature of liability from surrender to payment of value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال محمد في الأصل : إذا جنى العبد على آدمي جناية موجبة للمال فمولاه بالخيار إن شاء دفعه بها، وإن شاء فداه بدفع أرشها . وفرق بين جنايته على آدمي وجنايته على المال ففي الجناية على الآدمي يخير المولى بين الدفع والفداء، وفي جنايته على مال الغير يخير المولى بين البيع ودفع الثمن وبين فدائه، ففي حفر البئر في الطريق مثلاً إذا وقع فيها دابة مثلاً فتلفت فباع المولى العبد ودفع ثمنه في الجناية لرب الدابة ثم تلفت فيها دابة أخرى يتبع رب الدابة الثانية رب الدابة الأولى لأن المولى لما باعه ودفع ثمنه فقد فعل ما الواجب عليه وخرج من العهدة، فلما وقع الآدمي ثانياً فقد هدر دمه لتعذر الطلب على المالك بعد خروجه من العهدة وثمنه قام مقام مخلص العبد للمشتري، وفي المسألة الثانية لما دفعه بعينه لولي الجناية الأولى ثم وقع في البئر إنسان آخر والعبد بعينه باق في ملك صاحب الجناية الأولى وقد تجدد عليه جناية بوقوع الثاني فيه وتلف بسبب حفره السابق وقد دفع بعينه للأول فيخاطب مالكه وفي الجناية الأولى بما هو الأصل من الدفع أو الفداء ويتجه قوله لأن الجنايتين استندتا إلى وقت الحفر إلى آخره هذا، وقد يجاب بأنا لا نسلم أنه لا يهدر دمه لما ذكرنا في المبسوط في جناية العبد في الحفر لو حفر عبد بئراً في الطريق فأعتق فأوقع فيه رجل فمات فعلى المولى قيمته الجنايته في ملكه ثم قال : فإن وقع فيها آخر اشتركا في القيمة لأنه بالإعتاق أتلف رقبة واحدة فعليه قيمة واحدة فهي بينهما، فإن وقع فيها العبد نفسه فوارثه يشارك الأول في ملك القيمة لأن العبد بعد العتق طهر في تلك الجناية وصار كغيره من الأجانب. وعن محمد أن دمه هدر والأصل أن العبد لو حفر بئراً في الطريق ثم أعتق ثم وقع فيها فمات فدمه هدر لأنه كجان على نفسه
Muhammad said in al-Asl: If the slave injures a person with a tort requiring monetary compensation, his master has the choice: if he wishes he surrenders him for it, and if he wishes he ransoms him by paying the blood money. And he distinguished between his injury to a person and his injury to property: for injury to a person, the master is given choice between surrender and ransom; for injury to the property of another, the master is given choice between selling and paying the price and between ransoming. So for example in digging a well on the road: if an animal falls in it and perishes, and the master sells the slave and pays its price for the injury to the owner of the animal, then another animal perishes in it, the owner of the second animal follows the owner of the first animal because when the master sold it and paid its price, he did what was obligatory upon him and exited liability. Then when the person falls secondarily, his blood is wasted (hadr) because claim is impossible on the owner after his exit from liability, and its price stood in place of the slave's deliverer for the buyer. In the second case, when he surrendered him in person to the guardian of the first injury, then another person falls into the well while the slave in person remains in the ownership of the owner of the first injury, and a new injury has occurred upon him due to the fall of the second and his perishing because of his prior digging, and he had been surrendered in person to the first, so his owner is addressed in the first injury with what is the principle of surrender or ransom, and his statement is appropriate because the two injuries are attributed to the time of digging... and it may be answered that we do not concede that his blood is wasted as we mentioned in al-Mabsut regarding the slave's injury in digging: if a slave dug a well on the road, then was freed, then a man fell in it and died, then upon the master is his value for his injury in his ownership. Then he said: if another falls in it, they share in the value because by the emancipation he destroyed one neck (slave), so upon him is one value, so it is between them. If the slave himself falls in it, then his heir shares with the first in the ownership of the value because the slave after emancipation became pure from that injury and became like other strangers. And from Muhammad that his blood is wasted, and the principle is that if a slave dug a well on the road then was freed then fell in it and died, his blood is wasted because he is like one who injures himself.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl, expanded upon by the commentator, lays out the master's options when a mortgaged slave commits a tort (jinaayah). The ruling distinguishes two categories: (1) injury to a human being (aadami) that necessitates monetary compensation (not qisas), and (2) injury to property (maal). For injury to a human, the master chooses between surrendering the slave (دفع) to the victim or paying the blood money (فداء). For injury to property, the master chooses between selling the slave and paying the value to the owner, or ransoming the slave (paying the damage). The passage then illustrates with a scenario where a slave digs a well on the road, causing multiple incidents. If an animal falls in and the master sells the slave to pay compensation, and then another animal falls in, the second owner's claim is against the first owner (who received the price) because the master has already fulfilled his duty. If a person falls in after the sale, his blood is wasted (لدمه هدر) because the master is no longer liable. However, if the slave was surrendered in person for the first injury (a person), and then another person falls in, the master is addressed again because the slave is still in the hands of the first guardian. The principle is that both injuries are attributed to the time of digging, so they are simultaneous. The passage then discusses a variation: if the slave is freed after digging but before anyone falls in, and then a person falls in, upon the master is the slave's value (because the slave is now free and cannot be surrendered). If another person falls in, they share that value. If the freed slave himself falls in, his heir shares with the first victim, but a narration from Muhammad says his blood is wasted.

Key Terms
دفع (daf'): Surrendering the slave to the victim or his guardian as compensation for the tort.
فداء (fida'): Ransoming the slave by paying the blood money or compensation from the master's own wealth.
هدر (hadar): Legally wasted; no claim for compensation is valid (blood money or otherwise).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A mortgaged slave injures a person's property (e.g., destroys a garment). What options does the master have according to Imam Muhammad?
A) Only surrender the slave.
B) Only pay the value from his own wealth.
C) Choose between selling the slave and paying the price, or ransoming the slave by paying the compensation.
D) Choose between surrendering the slave to the victim or paying the blood money.

Key Takeaway
The master of a mortgaged slave has a choice between surrendering the slave or paying compensation for the slave's tort, with distinct mechanisms for injury to a human versus property.

When a Mortgaged Slave's Tort Is Considered: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Critiquing the matn's absolute statement and explaining the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when a mortgaged slave's tort is hadr vs. mu'tabara, and explain the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A mortgaged slave's tort is hadr for financial claims but valid for qisas; the Sahibayn also consider it valid if it gives the pledgee ownership of the slave.

In this passage, the commentator critiques the absolute statement in Kanz al-Daqaiq that all torts of a mortgaged slave against the pledgor and pledgee are hadr. He refines the ruling: torts requiring qisas are always considered, while financial torts are hadr only when no benefit arises. However, the two disciples argue that a financial tort against the pledgee can be beneficial by allowing the pledgee to own the slave. We'll unpack the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its critique
The matn states all torts are hadr; the commentator argues this is too absolute. You must note the critique and the proposed refinement.
The commentator wanted the author to distinguish between types of tort.
2
Distinguish between qisas and financial claims
According to Abu Hanifa, torts requiring qisas are considered because they involve the slave's person, not just property. Identify the key difference: qisas vs. financial compensation.
The slave's person is not owned, so qisas is valid against the slave.
3
Apply Abu Hanifa's reasoning to financial claims
Financial claims are hadr because compensation would be تحصيل الحاصل (obtaining what is already had), as the slave's value is already claimed by the master and pledgee. Understand the logical impossibility argument.
تحصيل الحاصل is a key usul principle here.
4
Understand the Sahibayn's exception
They consider financial torts against the pledgee as mu'tabara because the pledgee may benefit by taking ownership of the slave. Compare their reasoning to Abu Hanifa's.
The pledgee might prefer owning the slave over the debt.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, a financial tort against the pledgee yields no compensation; under Sahibayn, the pledgee can claim the slave or its value. Apply this to a concrete scenario.
This difference affects the rights of the parties.

قال رحمه الله : (وجناية الرهن عليهما وعلى مالهما (هدر ولا يخفى أن هذا الإطلاق غير ظاهر. ولو قال المؤلف وجنايته على الرهن الموجبة للمال وعلى ماله هدر وعلى المرتهن فيما دون النفس أو في ماله هدر كان أولى لأن الجناية على الراهن الموجبة للقصاص معتبرة في النفس والأطراف فيما توجبه وعلى المرتهن في النفس الموجبة للقصاص معتبرة ومحل كونها هدراً في حق المرتهن حيث لا فضل في قيمته عند الإمام . قال الشارح: أطلق الجواب والمراد جناية لا توجب القصاص وإن كانت توجبه معتبرة حتى يجب عليه القصاص، أما المرتهن فظاهر لأنه أجنبي عنه وكذا المولى لأنه كالأجنبي عنه في حق الدم إذا لم يدخل في ملكه لا من حيث المالية ألا ترى أن إقرار المولى عليه بالجناية الموجبة للقصاص باطل وإقرار العبد بها جائز والإقرار بالمال على عكسه، فإذا لم يكن في ملكه من ذلك الوجه صار أجنبياً عنه بخلاف ما المال لأن ماليته ملك المولى ويستحق المرتهن فلا فائدة في اعتبارها إذ يوجب تحصيل الحاصل محال بخلاف جناية المغصوب على المغصوب منه حيث تعتبر عند أبي حنيفة لأن الملك عند أداء الضمان يثبت للغاصب مستنداً حتى يكون الكفن على الغاصب فكانت كجنايته على غير ملكه فاعتبرت وهذا الحكم فيها فيما إذا كانت جناية الرهن موجبة للدين على العبد لا دفع الرقبة بأن كانت على غير الآدمي في النفس خطأ أو فيما دونها فكذلك عند أبي حنيفة . وقالا : إن كانت جنايته على الراهن فكذلك، وإن كانت على المرتهن فمعتبرة لأن في اعتبارها فائدة تملك رقبة العبد والمرتهن غير مالك حقيقة فكانت جناية المرتهن عليه جناية على غير المالك غير أنها سقطت لعدم الفائدة في جناية لا توجب دفع العبد لما ذكرنا، وهذه أفادت ملك رقبة العبد وإن كان دينه يسقط بذلك لأنه قد يختار ملك رقبة العبد، وربما يكون بقاء الدين أنفع له فيختار أيهما شاء، ثم إذا اختار أخذه ووافقه الراهن على ذلك بطل الرهن بسقوط الدين بهلاكه لأنه دفعه بالجناية يوجب هلاكه على الراهن فيسقط به الدين، ولهذا لو
He (the author) said: 'And the injury of the mortgaged slave against them (the pledgor and pledgee) and against their property is wasted (hadr).' And it is not hidden that this absolute statement is not apparent. Had the author said: 'His injury against the pledgor that necessitates property [compensation] and against his property is wasted, and against the pledgee regarding what is less than life or his property is wasted' would have been better because the injury against the pledgor that necessitates qisas is considered regarding life and limbs with what it entails, and against the pledgee regarding life that necessitates qisas is considered. The occasion for its being hadr with respect to the pledgee is where there is no surplus in his value according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]. The commentator said: He gave an absolute answer, and what is meant is injury that does not necessitate qisas; if it necessitates qisas, it is considered so that qisas becomes obligatory upon him. As for the pledgee, it is apparent because he is a stranger to him, and likewise the master because he is like a stranger to him in the matter of blood if it does not enter into his ownership (i.e., the slave's) from the perspective of property. Do you not see that the master's confession of a tort requiring qisas is invalid, while the slave's confession of it is valid, and confession of property is the opposite? So if it is not in his ownership from that aspect, he becomes a stranger to him, unlike property because his property is owned by the master and the pledgee has a claim, so there is no benefit in considering it as it would entail an impossibility (obtaining what is already obtained). Contrary to the tort of a usurped (slave) against the usurper according to Abu Hanifa, because ownership upon payment of the guarantee is established for the usurper retrospectively so that the shroud is upon the usurper, thus it is like his injury against non-his ownership, so it is considered. And this ruling for it is when the injury of the mortgaged slave necessitates debt upon the slave, not surrender of the neck, such as against a non-human in life (death by mistake) or what is less than that, so likewise according to Abu Hanifa. And they (the two disciples) said: If his injury is against the pledgor, then likewise; and if against the pledgee, then it is considered because in considering it there is a benefit: ownership of the slave's neck. And the pledgee is not a true owner, so the injury of the pledgee against him is an injury against a non-owner, except that it fell due to lack of benefit in an injury that does not necessitate surrender of the slave as we mentioned. And this (injury against pledgee) brings the benefit of ownership of the slave's neck, even if his debt falls by that, because he may choose ownership of the slave's neck, and perhaps the survival of the debt is more beneficial to him, so he chooses whichever he wishes. Then if he chooses to take him and the pledgor agrees to that, the mortgage becomes void by the fall of the debt due to its destruction because his surrender by the injury necessitates his destruction upon the pledgor, so the debt falls by it. And therefore if...
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage begins with a critique by the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq of the statement in the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) that the injury of the mortgaged slave against the pledgor (raahin) and pledgee (murtahin) and their property is hadr (legally wasted, i.e., no liability). The commentator argues that this absolute statement is not accurate. He proposes a more precise formulation: the injury against the pledgor that necessitates only monetary compensation is hadr, but if it necessitates qisas (retaliation) for life or limbs, it is considered valid and qisas becomes obligatory. Similarly, injury against the pledgee that is less than life (e.g., wound) or against his property is hadr, but injury causing death is considered. The reason is that the master (mawla) and pledgee are considered strangers concerning blood claims because the slave's life is not owned by them (only the usufruct or value is in mortgage). Thus, qisas can be claimed against the slave himself, not against the master. The commentator then explains that according to Abu Hanifa, if the injury is only a financial claim (e.g., animal killed by the slave), there is no benefit in considering it because the slave's value already belongs to the master and the pledgee has a claim on it, so compensation would result in a contradiction (تحصيل الحاصل). However, if the injury results in the surrender of the slave (دفع رقبة), as in cases of intentional killing or wounding, there is a benefit because the victim can take the slave in compensation. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree with Abu Hanifa for injury to the pledgor, but they differ for injury to the pledgee: they consider it valid because it allows the pledgee to own the slave's neck (i.e., the slave's entire value), even if it extinguishes the debt. The pledgee may prefer ownership of the slave over the debt. Thus, the injury is not wasted. The passage ends with the consequence: if the pledgee chooses to take the slave with the pledgor's agreement, the mortgage is void because the debt is extinguished by the destruction of the slave (i.e., the slave is given as compensation).

Key Terms
هدر (hadar): Legally wasted; no liability or claim arises from the act.
معتبرة (mu'tabara): Considered valid; the tort gives rise to legal claims (either qisas or compensation).
تحصيل الحاصل (tahseel al-haasil): Obtaining what is already obtained; a logical impossibility used as a proof that considering the tort would be redundant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the refined ruling in the commentary, which type of tort of a mortgaged slave against the pledgor is NOT hadr?
A) A tort that requires financial compensation only.
B) A tort that is less than life (e.g., wound).
C) A tort that necessitates qisas (e.g., killing).
D) All torts are hadr regardless.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on a mortgaged slave's tort depends on whether it involves qisas or financial compensation, with Abu Hanifa restricting consideration to qisas cases, and the Sahibayn extending it to financial torts against the pledgee due to the benefit of ownership.

The General Rule of Injury by the Pledge and Its Qualifications
Explaining the general rule and its qualifications, including the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that injury by the pledge is of no consequence (hadar) and identify its exceptions, including when qisas is obligatory and the distinction between injury to the pledgor vs. mortgagee.

Core Idea
The pledge's injury is disregarded unless it warrants qisas or benefits the mortgagee's right.

The passage begins with the matn statement that any injury caused by the pledged item to the pledgor, mortgagee, or their property is of no consequence. However, the commentator immediately refines this absolute statement, noting that injuries warranting retaliation (qisas) are considered. He also distinguishes between injury to the pledgor and the mortgagee, and introduces the key intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding injury upon the mortgagee. This lesson unpacks the general rule and its qualifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule from the matn
Read the matn statement: 'وجناية الرهن عليهما وعلى مالهما هدر'. This is the default ruling: no liability arises from the pledge's injury upon the pledgor, mortgagee, or their property.
The word 'هدر' means 'of no consequence' – no compensation or claim.
2
Recognize the commentator's qualification
The commentator notes this absolute statement is 'not apparent' because it fails to exclude injuries that necessitate qisas (retaliation). Such injuries are considered and must be enforced.
Qisas applies to intentional killing or wounding; the pledge's owner is liable to qisas or diyah.
3
Distinguish injury to pledgor vs. mortgagee
Injury to the pledgor is hadar (no liability) except when qisas is due. Injury to the mortgagee is also hadar according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn hold it is considered if it provides benefit (possibility of ownership).
The 'benefit' is the mortgagee's chance to take ownership of the slave instead of the debt.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on injury to mortgagee
Compare Abu Hanifa's view (no consideration because no benefit/ impossible purification) with the Sahibayn's view (consideration because the mortgagee may choose ownership). Note the qiyas with the usurped slave case.
The dispute revolves around whether the mortgagee gains any tangible benefit from considering the injury.
5
Apply the rule to a practical scenario
Given a scenario: a pledged slave damages the mortgagee's property or injures him. Determine if the mortgagee can claim compensation or take the slave. According to Abu Hanifa, no; according to Sahibayn, yes with pledgor's consent.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is Abu Hanifa's view.

كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره
وعلى مالهما هدر ولو رهن عبداً يساوي ألفاً بألف ورجعت قيمته إلى مائة فقتله رجل فمات فعلى المولى قيمته الجنايته في ملكه ثم قال : فإن وقع فيها آخر اشتركا في القيمة لأنه بالإعتاق أتلف رقبة واحدة فعليه قيمة واحدة فهي بينهما، فإن وقع فيها العبد نفسه فوارثه يشارك الأول في ملك القيمة لأن العبد بعد العتق طهر في تلك الجناية وصار كغيره من الأجانب. وعن محمد أن دمه هدر والأصل أن العبد لو حفر بئراً في الطريق ثم أعتق ثم وقع فيها فمات فدمه هدر لأنه كجان على نفسه وظاهر الرواية أن على المولى قيمته لورثته لما ذكرنا أنه لما عتق طهر من الجناية عبدان حفرا بئراً في الطريق فوقع فيها عبد الرهن فدفعا ثم وقع أحدهما فيها فمات بطل نصف الدين وهدر دمه لأنهما قاما مقام العبد الأول وأخذا حكم الأول، ولو وقع العبد الأول في البئر وذهب نصفه بأن ذهبت عينه أو شلت يده وسقط نصف الدين فكذا هذا .
به
قال رحمه الله : (وجناية الرهن عليهما وعلى مالهما (هدر ولا يخفى أن هذا الإطلاق غير ظاهر. ولو قال المؤلف وجنايته على الرهن الموجبة للمال وعلى ماله هدر وعلى المرتهن فيما دون النفس أو في ماله هدر كان أولى لأن الجناية على الراهن الموجبة للقصاص معتبرة في النفس والأطراف فيما توجبه وعلى المرتهن في النفس الموجبة للقصاص معتبرة ومحل كونها هدراً في حق المرتهن حيث لا فضل في قيمته عند الإمام . قال الشارح: أطلق الجواب والمراد جناية لا توجب القصاص وإن كانت توجبه معتبرة حتى يجب عليه القصاص، أما المرتهن فظاهر لأنه أجنبي عنه وكذا المولى لأنه كالأجنبي عنه في حق الدم إذا لم يدخل في ملكه لا من حيث المالية ألا ترى أن إقرار المولى عليه بالجناية الموجبة للقصاص باطل وإقرار العبد بها جائز والإقرار بالمال على عكسه، فإذا لم يكن في ملكه من ذلك الوجه صار أجنبياً عنه بخلاف ما المال لأن ماليته ملك المولى ويستحق المرتهن فلا فائدة في اعتبارها إذ يوجب تحصيل الحاصل محال بخلاف جناية المغصوب على المغصوب منه حيث تعتبر عند أبي حنيفة لأن الملك عند أداء الضمان يثبت للغاصب مستنداً حتى يكون الكفن على الغاصب فكانت كجنايته على غير ملكه فاعتبرت وهذا الحكم فيها فيما إذا كانت جناية الرهن موجبة للدين على العبد لا دفع الرقبة بأن كانت على غير الآدمي في النفس خطأ أو فيما دونها فكذلك عند أبي حنيفة . وقالا : إن كانت جنايته على الراهن فكذلك، وإن كانت على المرتهن فمعتبرة لأن في اعتبارها فائدة تملك رقبة العبد والمرتهن غير مالك حقيقة فكانت جناية المرتهن عليه جناية على غير المالك غير أنها سقطت لعدم الفائدة في جناية لا توجب دفع العبد لما ذكرنا، وهذه أفادت ملك رقبة العبد وإن كان دينه يسقط بذلك لأنه قد يختار ملك رقبة العبد، وربما يكون بقاء الدين أنفع له فيختار أيهما شاء، ثم إذا اختار أخذه ووافقه الراهن على ذلك بطل الرهن بسقوط الدين بهلاكه لأنه دفعه بالجناية يوجب هلاكه على الراهن فيسقط به الدين، ولهذا لو
جنى على الأجنبي فدفع بها سقط الدين، وإن لم يدفع بالجناية فهو رهن على حاله. ولأبي حنيفة أن هذه الجناية لو اعتبرناها للمرتهن كان عليه التطهير من الجناية لأنها حصلت في ضمانه فلا تفيد وجوب الضمان مع وجوب التخليص عليه وهذا الاختلاف نظير الاختلاف في العبد المغصوب فإن جنايته على الغاصب لا تعتبر عنده وعندهما تعتبر. وما ذكرا من الفائدة غير ظاهر لأن أخذ العبد بالجناية لا يكون إلا باختيار المالك. وفي رواية عن أبي حنيفة إذا كانت قيمة الرهن أكثر من الدين فإن كانت جنايته على المرتهن معتبرة بحسابها لأن الزائد أمانة فصار كجناية العبد المودع . قيد بقوله «عليهما» لأن جنايته على أولادهما معتبرة فلو جنى الرهن على ابن الراهن أو على ابن المرتهن فهي معتبرة في الصحيح حتى يدفع بها أو يفيد، وإن كانت على المال فيباع كما إذا جنى على الأجنبي إذ هو أجنبي كسائر الأملاك. هذا ولم يتعرض المؤلف لبقية الجناية التي تكون هدر أو الجناية بعض الرهن على بعض قال في المبسوط : أصله أن جناية المشغول على المشغول هدر لكن يسقط الدين في المجني بقدره وجناية المشغول على الفارغ والفارغ على الفارغ وجناية الفارغ على المشغول معتبرة وينتقل ما في المشغول من الدين إلى الفارغ فيصير رهناً مكانه لأن الجناية إنما تعتبر لحق المرتهن في المجني عليه لا لحق الراهن لأن كلاهما ملكه واعتبار الجناية لحق المرتهن لا يفيد إلا في جناية الفارغ على المشغول لأنها إنما تعتبر ليشتغل الجاني بما كان من المجني عليه وهو الحبس، وهذا ثابت قبل الجناية فإن الجاني كان محبوساً بالدين الذي كان المجني عليه محبوساً به، ولهذا جناية الفارغ على الفارغ هدر لأنه لا شغل فيها بحق الحبس. وإذا لم يفد اعتبارها صار كأنه فات بآفة سماوية فإن جناية الفارغ على المشغول تفيد لأن الدين تحول إليه من المجني عليه فقام مقامه .
ثم المسائل على فصول : أحدها في الجناية على الرهن والثاني في جناية ولد الرهن . والثالث في جناية الرهن المستعار. وإذا ارتهن دابتين فأتلفت إحداهما الأخرى ذهب من الدين بحسابها بخلاف ما لو كان الرهن عبدين فقتل أحدهما الآخر يتحول بين المقتول إلى القاتل لأن جناية العجماء جبار لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام جرح العجماء جبار» فكان قتل إحداهما الأخرى بمنزلة موتها حتف أنفها. وأما جناية الرقيق على الرقيق فمعتبرة حتى يجب القصاص أو يجب الدفع أو الفداء فقام القاتل مقام المقتول فيتحول دين المقتول إلى القاتل، ثم بأي قدر يتحول إليه سيأتي ارتهن عبدين فلا يخلو إما إن ارتهنهما في صفقة واحدة أو في صفقتين، فإن ارتهنهما في صفقة بألف وقيمة كل واحد منهما ألف فقتل أحدهما صاحبه فالباقي رهن بتسعمائة وخمسين لأن كل واحد منهما نصفه مشغول ونصفه فارغ فالنصف الفارغ . المقتول تلف بجناية الفارغ على المشغول وبجناية الفارع على الفارغ وذلك كله هدر، والنصف المشغول تلف بجناية المشغول على المشغول وذلك هدر فصار كأنه رهن بسبعمائة من العبد
Book of Pledge: Chapter on Disposal of the Pledge, Injury upon It, and Its Injury upon Others. And upon their property it is of no consequence. If one pledges a slave worth one thousand for one thousand, and its value returns to one hundred, then a man kills him and he dies, then the owner owes his value for the injury upon his property. Then he said: If another falls into it, they share the value because he destroyed one neck by emancipation, so one value is upon him, and it is between them. If the slave himself falls into it, his heir shares with the first in ownership of the value because the slave after emancipation becomes free of that injury and becomes like other outsiders. From Muhammad that his blood is of no consequence. The principle is that if a slave digs a well in the road, then is freed, then falls into it and dies, his blood is of no consequence because he is like one injuring himself. The apparent narration is that the owner owes his value to his heirs due to what we mentioned: that when he was freed, he became free of the injury. Two slaves dug a well in the road, then the pledged slave fell into it, so they paid, then one of them fell into it and died; half of the debt is voided and his blood is of no consequence because they stood in the place of the first slave and took the ruling of the first. If the first slave falls into the well and half of him is lost, such as his eye goes or his hand is paralyzed, and half of the debt is dropped, then it is similar. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And the injury of the pledge upon them and upon their property is of no consequence). It is not hidden that this absolute statement is not apparent. If the author had said 'And its injury upon the pledgor that necessitates wealth is of no consequence upon his property, and upon the mortgagee in what is less than the self or upon his property is of no consequence,' it would be more appropriate, because the injury upon the pledgor that necessitates retaliation is considered in the self and limbs in what it necessitates, and upon the mortgagee in the self that necessitates retaliation is considered. The place of its being of no consequence regarding the mortgagee is when there is no surplus in its value according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentator said: He gave an absolute answer and what is meant is injury that does not necessitate retaliation; if it necessitates retaliation, it is considered, so retaliation is obligatory upon him. As for the mortgagee, it is apparent because he is a stranger to him, and similarly the owner, because he is like a stranger to him regarding blood as long as he has not come into his ownership, not from the aspect of financial value. Do you not see that the owner's acknowledgement of injury that necessitates retaliation is invalid, while the slave's acknowledgement of it is valid; acknowledgement of financial matters is the opposite. So when he is not in his ownership from that perspective, he becomes a stranger to him, unlike financial matters because his financial value is owned by the owner and the mortgagee has a claim, so there is no benefit in considering it, as it would necessitate an impossibility. This is unlike the injury of a usurped item upon the one from whom it was usurped, which is considered according to Abu Hanifa, because ownership upon payment of compensation is established for the usurper retroactively, such that the shroud is upon the usurper, so it is like his injury upon non-ownership and thus considered. This ruling in it is when the injury of the pledge necessitates a debt upon the slave, not surrender of the neck, such as when it is upon a non-human in the self by mistake, or in what is less than that. So similarly according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If his injury is upon the pledgor, then similarly (not considered); but if it is upon the mortgagee, then it is considered because in considering it there is benefit: ownership of the slave's neck. And the mortgagee is not truly an owner, so the mortgagee's injury upon him is an injury upon a non-owner, but it is dropped due to lack of benefit in an injury that does not necessitate surrender of the slave due to what we mentioned. This injury benefits ownership of the slave's neck, even if his debt drops because of it, because he may choose ownership of the slave's neck, and perhaps the continuation of the debt is more beneficial to him, so he chooses whichever he wishes. Then if he chooses to take him and the pledgor agrees, the pledge becomes void with the drop of the debt due to its destruction, because surrendering him due to injury necessitates his destruction upon the pledgor, so the debt drops with it. Therefore, if he injures a stranger and surrenders by it, the debt drops; if he does not surrender by the injury, then he remains a pledge as before. According to Abu Hanifa, if we consider this injury for the mortgagee, it would be upon him to purify from the injury because it occurred in his guarantee, so it does not benefit the obligation of compensation along with the obligation of release. This difference is similar to the difference in the usurped slave: his injury upon the usurper is not considered according to him (Abu Hanifa), but is considered according to the two. And what they mentioned of benefit is not apparent, because taking the slave by injury is only by the choice of the owner. In a narration from Abu Hanifa, if the value of the pledge is more than the debt, then his injury upon the mortgagee is considered in proportion because the surplus is a trust, so it becomes like the injury of a deposited slave. He restricted with his saying 'upon them' because his injury upon their children is considered. So if the pledge injures the son of the pledgor or the son of the mortgagee, it is considered according to the correct view, so he surrenders by it or benefits. And if it is upon property, it is sold as when he injures a stranger, because he is a stranger like other properties. This is so, and the author did not address the rest of the injury that is of no consequence, or the injury of one part of the pledge upon another. It is stated in al-Mabsut: The principle is that injury of the encumbered upon the encumbered is of no consequence, but the debt drops from the injured to its extent. Injury of the encumbered upon the unencumbered, and the unencumbered upon the unencumbered, and injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered are considered, and what is in the encumbered from debt is transferred to the unencumbered, which becomes a pledge in its place, because injury is considered for the right of the mortgagee upon the injured, not for the right of the pledgor, because both are his property. Consideration of injury for the right of the mortgagee only benefits in injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered, because it is considered so that the injurer becomes occupied with what was upon the injured, which is detention. This was established before the injury: the injurer was detained by the debt with which the injured was detained. Therefore, injury of the unencumbered upon the unencumbered is of no consequence because there is no occupation regarding the right of detention. And if its consideration does not benefit, it is as if it was lost by a heavenly calamity. Injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered benefits because the debt is transferred from the injured to him, so he stands in his place. Then the issues are in sections: first, concerning injury upon the pledge; second, concerning injury of the offspring of the pledge; third, concerning injury of the borrowed pledge. If one takes as pledge two riding animals and one destroys the other, an amount of the debt goes in proportion, unlike if the pledge were two slaves and one kills the other: the debt is transferred from the killed to the killer, because injury of a dumb animal is of no effect due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The injury of a dumb animal is of no effect.' So the killing of one by the other is like its death by natural causes. As for injury of slaves upon slaves, it is considered, even if it necessitates retaliation or surrender or ransom, so the killer stands in the place of the killed, so the debt of the killed is transferred to the killer. Then by what amount it is transferred will come. If one pledges two slaves, either he pledges them in a single transaction or in two transactions. If he pledges them in a single transaction for one thousand and each one's value is one thousand, and one kills the other, the remaining one is a pledge for nine hundred and fifty, because each one: half is encumbered and half is unencumbered. The unencumbered half of the killed is lost by injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered and by injury of the unencumbered upon the unencumbered, and all that is of no consequence. The encumbered half is lost by injury of the encumbered upon the encumbered, and that is of no consequence. So it is as if it were a pledge for seven hundred from the slave.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the ruling on injury caused by a pledged item (al-rahn). The commentator begins by quoting the matn: 'وجناية الرهن عليهما وعلى مالهما هدر' meaning that any injury caused by the pledged property to the pledgor (rahin) or mortgagee (murtahin) or their property is of no consequence (hadar) — i.e., no liability arises. However, the commentator immediately notes that this absolute statement is not fully apparent, because there are exceptions: if the injury causes harm that warrants retaliation (qisas), such as killing or severing limbs, then it is considered and qisas becomes obligatory. Also, there is a distinction between injury to the pledgor vs. mortgagee, and between injuries that necessitate only financial compensation vs. those that necessitate surrender of the slave. The passage then explains the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: injury by the pledge upon the mortgagee is not considered because it would provide no benefit (since the mortgagee already has a right in the pledge). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they argue that if the injury is upon the mortgagee, it can be beneficial because the mortgagee might choose to take ownership of the slave instead of the debt. The commentator also gives examples: a slave who digs a well, then is freed, then falls into it — his blood is wasted because he is like a self-injurer. Another example: two slaves dig a well, a pledged slave falls in, they pay, then one of the diggers falls in — half the debt is voided. The passage then discusses the principle from al-Mabsut: injury of the encumbered (mashghul) upon the encumbered is of no consequence (hadar), but some debt drops. Injury of the unencumbered (farigh) upon the encumbered is considered and debt transfers. The text also covers cases of two pledged animals vs. two pledged slaves: for animals, the destruction is like natural death; for slaves, the debt is transferred to the killer. Finally, an example of two slaves pledged in one transaction: each has half encumbered and half unencumbered, leading to a specific calculation of the remaining debt. The teacher should note that this passage is a detailed expansion of the general rule, emphasizing that the 'consideration' of injury depends on whether it benefits the mortgagee's right.

Key Terms
جناية (jināyah): In this context, injury or damage caused by the pledged item (slave) to persons or property.
هدر (hadar): Of no consequence; no liability or compensation is due.
قصاص (qisās): Retaliation, specifically in cases of intentional killing or wounding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position regarding injury caused by the pledge upon the mortgagee?
A) It is always considered because the mortgagee may choose to take the slave.
B) It is of no consequence (hadar) because no tangible benefit accrues.
C) It is considered only if the debt is less than the slave's value.
D) It is considered only if the injury is unintentional.

Key Takeaway
The general rule that injury by the pledge is hadar is subject to exceptions for qisas and is disputed regarding injury to the mortgagee, with the mufta bihi being Abu Hanifa's view that it is also hadar.

Detailed Principles: Injury of Encumbered vs. Unencumbered and Case Studies
Detailed principles from al-Mabsut on injury among pledges and case studies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principles from al-Mabsut regarding injury of encumbered (mashghul) and unencumbered (farigh) parts of a pledge and calculate debt transfer in cases of injury among multiple pledges.

Core Idea
Injury among encumbered parts is hadar but drops debt proportionally; injury of unencumbered to encumbered transfers debt to the injurer.

After establishing the general rule and the dispute, the passage shifts to a more detailed exposition borrowed from al-Mabsut. It lays out a principle: injury of the encumbered upon the encumbered is of no consequence (hadar), but the debt drops from the victim to the extent of the injury. Injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered is considered, and the debt transfers to the injurer, who becomes a pledge in its place. The text then applies these principles to several case studies: a well dug by slaves, two pledged animals versus two pledged slaves, and a detailed calculation of debt transfer when two slaves are pledged in one transaction.

Guided Path
1
Understand the key terms: mashghul (encumbered) and farigh (unencumbered)
Mashghul refers to a share of the pledge that is 'occupied' by debt (i.e., the portion that secures the loan). Farigh is the portion that is free of debt (e.g., surplus value).
If a slave is worth 1000 and the debt is 500, half is mashghul, half is farigh.
2
Learn the four categories of injury between pledges
Identify four scenarios: (1) mashghul on mashghul – injury is hadar, but debt drops proportionally from victim; (2) mashghul on farigh – injury is considered, debt transfers from victim to injurer; (3) farigh on farigh – injury is hadar (no benefit); (4) farigh on mashghul – injury is considered, debt transfers to injurer.
Only scenarios where benefit accrues to the mortgagee (debt transfer) are considered.
3
Apply to the well example
Two slaves dig a well; a pledged slave falls in and dies. According to the principle, the two slaves (as unencumbered? Actually they are not pledged) paid compensation. Then one of them falls into the same well and dies: half the debt is voided and his blood is hadar because he stood in place of the first slave.
This demonstrates how the principle works when the 'encumbered' status changes.
4
Distinguish animals from slaves
For animals (dabbah), injury of one upon another is like natural death (hadar due to hadith 'al-jarah jabar'). For slaves, injury is considered because they are liable for qisas, diyah, or surrender.
This distinction is based on the nature of the item: animals are not subject to qisas.
5
Calculate debt transfer in the two-slave pledge example
Given two slaves pledged in one transaction, each worth 1000, debt 1000. One kills the other. Each slave: half encumbered (500) and half unencumbered (500). The victim's unencumbered half is lost due to injury by the killer's unencumbered half (hadar) and his encumbered half by killer's encumbered half (hadar). So the killer's remaining value after surrender? The text says: remaining pledge is for 950? Actually the text says remaining is for 950? The passage states: 'فالباقي رهن بتسعمائة وخمسين' and later 'فصار كأنه رهن بسبعمائة من العبد' – there is inconsistency in the OCR. We rely on the principle: the killer stands in place of the victim for the debt portion.
The exact calculation is complex; focus on the underlying principle of proportional transfer.
