كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره
وعلى مالهما هدر ولو رهن عبداً يساوي ألفاً بألف ورجعت قيمته إلى مائة فقتله رجل فمات فعلى المولى قيمته الجنايته في ملكه ثم قال : فإن وقع فيها آخر اشتركا في القيمة لأنه بالإعتاق أتلف رقبة واحدة فعليه قيمة واحدة فهي بينهما، فإن وقع فيها العبد نفسه فوارثه يشارك الأول في ملك القيمة لأن العبد بعد العتق طهر في تلك الجناية وصار كغيره من الأجانب. وعن محمد أن دمه هدر والأصل أن العبد لو حفر بئراً في الطريق ثم أعتق ثم وقع فيها فمات فدمه هدر لأنه كجان على نفسه وظاهر الرواية أن على المولى قيمته لورثته لما ذكرنا أنه لما عتق طهر من الجناية عبدان حفرا بئراً في الطريق فوقع فيها عبد الرهن فدفعا ثم وقع أحدهما فيها فمات بطل نصف الدين وهدر دمه لأنهما قاما مقام العبد الأول وأخذا حكم الأول، ولو وقع العبد الأول في البئر وذهب نصفه بأن ذهبت عينه أو شلت يده وسقط نصف الدين فكذا هذا .
به
قال رحمه الله : (وجناية الرهن عليهما وعلى مالهما (هدر ولا يخفى أن هذا الإطلاق غير ظاهر. ولو قال المؤلف وجنايته على الرهن الموجبة للمال وعلى ماله هدر وعلى المرتهن فيما دون النفس أو في ماله هدر كان أولى لأن الجناية على الراهن الموجبة للقصاص معتبرة في النفس والأطراف فيما توجبه وعلى المرتهن في النفس الموجبة للقصاص معتبرة ومحل كونها هدراً في حق المرتهن حيث لا فضل في قيمته عند الإمام . قال الشارح: أطلق الجواب والمراد جناية لا توجب القصاص وإن كانت توجبه معتبرة حتى يجب عليه القصاص، أما المرتهن فظاهر لأنه أجنبي عنه وكذا المولى لأنه كالأجنبي عنه في حق الدم إذا لم يدخل في ملكه لا من حيث المالية ألا ترى أن إقرار المولى عليه بالجناية الموجبة للقصاص باطل وإقرار العبد بها جائز والإقرار بالمال على عكسه، فإذا لم يكن في ملكه من ذلك الوجه صار أجنبياً عنه بخلاف ما المال لأن ماليته ملك المولى ويستحق المرتهن فلا فائدة في اعتبارها إذ يوجب تحصيل الحاصل محال بخلاف جناية المغصوب على المغصوب منه حيث تعتبر عند أبي حنيفة لأن الملك عند أداء الضمان يثبت للغاصب مستنداً حتى يكون الكفن على الغاصب فكانت كجنايته على غير ملكه فاعتبرت وهذا الحكم فيها فيما إذا كانت جناية الرهن موجبة للدين على العبد لا دفع الرقبة بأن كانت على غير الآدمي في النفس خطأ أو فيما دونها فكذلك عند أبي حنيفة . وقالا : إن كانت جنايته على الراهن فكذلك، وإن كانت على المرتهن فمعتبرة لأن في اعتبارها فائدة تملك رقبة العبد والمرتهن غير مالك حقيقة فكانت جناية المرتهن عليه جناية على غير المالك غير أنها سقطت لعدم الفائدة في جناية لا توجب دفع العبد لما ذكرنا، وهذه أفادت ملك رقبة العبد وإن كان دينه يسقط بذلك لأنه قد يختار ملك رقبة العبد، وربما يكون بقاء الدين أنفع له فيختار أيهما شاء، ثم إذا اختار أخذه ووافقه الراهن على ذلك بطل الرهن بسقوط الدين بهلاكه لأنه دفعه بالجناية يوجب هلاكه على الراهن فيسقط به الدين، ولهذا لو
جنى على الأجنبي فدفع بها سقط الدين، وإن لم يدفع بالجناية فهو رهن على حاله. ولأبي حنيفة أن هذه الجناية لو اعتبرناها للمرتهن كان عليه التطهير من الجناية لأنها حصلت في ضمانه فلا تفيد وجوب الضمان مع وجوب التخليص عليه وهذا الاختلاف نظير الاختلاف في العبد المغصوب فإن جنايته على الغاصب لا تعتبر عنده وعندهما تعتبر. وما ذكرا من الفائدة غير ظاهر لأن أخذ العبد بالجناية لا يكون إلا باختيار المالك. وفي رواية عن أبي حنيفة إذا كانت قيمة الرهن أكثر من الدين فإن كانت جنايته على المرتهن معتبرة بحسابها لأن الزائد أمانة فصار كجناية العبد المودع . قيد بقوله «عليهما» لأن جنايته على أولادهما معتبرة فلو جنى الرهن على ابن الراهن أو على ابن المرتهن فهي معتبرة في الصحيح حتى يدفع بها أو يفيد، وإن كانت على المال فيباع كما إذا جنى على الأجنبي إذ هو أجنبي كسائر الأملاك. هذا ولم يتعرض المؤلف لبقية الجناية التي تكون هدر أو الجناية بعض الرهن على بعض قال في المبسوط : أصله أن جناية المشغول على المشغول هدر لكن يسقط الدين في المجني بقدره وجناية المشغول على الفارغ والفارغ على الفارغ وجناية الفارغ على المشغول معتبرة وينتقل ما في المشغول من الدين إلى الفارغ فيصير رهناً مكانه لأن الجناية إنما تعتبر لحق المرتهن في المجني عليه لا لحق الراهن لأن كلاهما ملكه واعتبار الجناية لحق المرتهن لا يفيد إلا في جناية الفارغ على المشغول لأنها إنما تعتبر ليشتغل الجاني بما كان من المجني عليه وهو الحبس، وهذا ثابت قبل الجناية فإن الجاني كان محبوساً بالدين الذي كان المجني عليه محبوساً به، ولهذا جناية الفارغ على الفارغ هدر لأنه لا شغل فيها بحق الحبس. وإذا لم يفد اعتبارها صار كأنه فات بآفة سماوية فإن جناية الفارغ على المشغول تفيد لأن الدين تحول إليه من المجني عليه فقام مقامه .
ثم المسائل على فصول : أحدها في الجناية على الرهن والثاني في جناية ولد الرهن . والثالث في جناية الرهن المستعار. وإذا ارتهن دابتين فأتلفت إحداهما الأخرى ذهب من الدين بحسابها بخلاف ما لو كان الرهن عبدين فقتل أحدهما الآخر يتحول بين المقتول إلى القاتل لأن جناية العجماء جبار لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام جرح العجماء جبار» فكان قتل إحداهما الأخرى بمنزلة موتها حتف أنفها. وأما جناية الرقيق على الرقيق فمعتبرة حتى يجب القصاص أو يجب الدفع أو الفداء فقام القاتل مقام المقتول فيتحول دين المقتول إلى القاتل، ثم بأي قدر يتحول إليه سيأتي ارتهن عبدين فلا يخلو إما إن ارتهنهما في صفقة واحدة أو في صفقتين، فإن ارتهنهما في صفقة بألف وقيمة كل واحد منهما ألف فقتل أحدهما صاحبه فالباقي رهن بتسعمائة وخمسين لأن كل واحد منهما نصفه مشغول ونصفه فارغ فالنصف الفارغ . المقتول تلف بجناية الفارغ على المشغول وبجناية الفارع على الفارغ وذلك كله هدر، والنصف المشغول تلف بجناية المشغول على المشغول وذلك هدر فصار كأنه رهن بسبعمائة من العبد
Book of Pledge: Chapter on Disposal of the Pledge, Injury upon It, and Its Injury upon Others. And upon their property it is of no consequence. If one pledges a slave worth one thousand for one thousand, and its value returns to one hundred, then a man kills him and he dies, then the owner owes his value for the injury upon his property. Then he said: If another falls into it, they share the value because he destroyed one neck by emancipation, so one value is upon him, and it is between them. If the slave himself falls into it, his heir shares with the first in ownership of the value because the slave after emancipation becomes free of that injury and becomes like other outsiders. From Muhammad that his blood is of no consequence. The principle is that if a slave digs a well in the road, then is freed, then falls into it and dies, his blood is of no consequence because he is like one injuring himself. The apparent narration is that the owner owes his value to his heirs due to what we mentioned: that when he was freed, he became free of the injury. Two slaves dug a well in the road, then the pledged slave fell into it, so they paid, then one of them fell into it and died; half of the debt is voided and his blood is of no consequence because they stood in the place of the first slave and took the ruling of the first. If the first slave falls into the well and half of him is lost, such as his eye goes or his hand is paralyzed, and half of the debt is dropped, then it is similar. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): (And the injury of the pledge upon them and upon their property is of no consequence). It is not hidden that this absolute statement is not apparent. If the author had said 'And its injury upon the pledgor that necessitates wealth is of no consequence upon his property, and upon the mortgagee in what is less than the self or upon his property is of no consequence,' it would be more appropriate, because the injury upon the pledgor that necessitates retaliation is considered in the self and limbs in what it necessitates, and upon the mortgagee in the self that necessitates retaliation is considered. The place of its being of no consequence regarding the mortgagee is when there is no surplus in its value according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentator said: He gave an absolute answer and what is meant is injury that does not necessitate retaliation; if it necessitates retaliation, it is considered, so retaliation is obligatory upon him. As for the mortgagee, it is apparent because he is a stranger to him, and similarly the owner, because he is like a stranger to him regarding blood as long as he has not come into his ownership, not from the aspect of financial value. Do you not see that the owner's acknowledgement of injury that necessitates retaliation is invalid, while the slave's acknowledgement of it is valid; acknowledgement of financial matters is the opposite. So when he is not in his ownership from that perspective, he becomes a stranger to him, unlike financial matters because his financial value is owned by the owner and the mortgagee has a claim, so there is no benefit in considering it, as it would necessitate an impossibility. This is unlike the injury of a usurped item upon the one from whom it was usurped, which is considered according to Abu Hanifa, because ownership upon payment of compensation is established for the usurper retroactively, such that the shroud is upon the usurper, so it is like his injury upon non-ownership and thus considered. This ruling in it is when the injury of the pledge necessitates a debt upon the slave, not surrender of the neck, such as when it is upon a non-human in the self by mistake, or in what is less than that. So similarly according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If his injury is upon the pledgor, then similarly (not considered); but if it is upon the mortgagee, then it is considered because in considering it there is benefit: ownership of the slave's neck. And the mortgagee is not truly an owner, so the mortgagee's injury upon him is an injury upon a non-owner, but it is dropped due to lack of benefit in an injury that does not necessitate surrender of the slave due to what we mentioned. This injury benefits ownership of the slave's neck, even if his debt drops because of it, because he may choose ownership of the slave's neck, and perhaps the continuation of the debt is more beneficial to him, so he chooses whichever he wishes. Then if he chooses to take him and the pledgor agrees, the pledge becomes void with the drop of the debt due to its destruction, because surrendering him due to injury necessitates his destruction upon the pledgor, so the debt drops with it. Therefore, if he injures a stranger and surrenders by it, the debt drops; if he does not surrender by the injury, then he remains a pledge as before. According to Abu Hanifa, if we consider this injury for the mortgagee, it would be upon him to purify from the injury because it occurred in his guarantee, so it does not benefit the obligation of compensation along with the obligation of release. This difference is similar to the difference in the usurped slave: his injury upon the usurper is not considered according to him (Abu Hanifa), but is considered according to the two. And what they mentioned of benefit is not apparent, because taking the slave by injury is only by the choice of the owner. In a narration from Abu Hanifa, if the value of the pledge is more than the debt, then his injury upon the mortgagee is considered in proportion because the surplus is a trust, so it becomes like the injury of a deposited slave. He restricted with his saying 'upon them' because his injury upon their children is considered. So if the pledge injures the son of the pledgor or the son of the mortgagee, it is considered according to the correct view, so he surrenders by it or benefits. And if it is upon property, it is sold as when he injures a stranger, because he is a stranger like other properties. This is so, and the author did not address the rest of the injury that is of no consequence, or the injury of one part of the pledge upon another. It is stated in al-Mabsut: The principle is that injury of the encumbered upon the encumbered is of no consequence, but the debt drops from the injured to its extent. Injury of the encumbered upon the unencumbered, and the unencumbered upon the unencumbered, and injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered are considered, and what is in the encumbered from debt is transferred to the unencumbered, which becomes a pledge in its place, because injury is considered for the right of the mortgagee upon the injured, not for the right of the pledgor, because both are his property. Consideration of injury for the right of the mortgagee only benefits in injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered, because it is considered so that the injurer becomes occupied with what was upon the injured, which is detention. This was established before the injury: the injurer was detained by the debt with which the injured was detained. Therefore, injury of the unencumbered upon the unencumbered is of no consequence because there is no occupation regarding the right of detention. And if its consideration does not benefit, it is as if it was lost by a heavenly calamity. Injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered benefits because the debt is transferred from the injured to him, so he stands in his place. Then the issues are in sections: first, concerning injury upon the pledge; second, concerning injury of the offspring of the pledge; third, concerning injury of the borrowed pledge. If one takes as pledge two riding animals and one destroys the other, an amount of the debt goes in proportion, unlike if the pledge were two slaves and one kills the other: the debt is transferred from the killed to the killer, because injury of a dumb animal is of no effect due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The injury of a dumb animal is of no effect.' So the killing of one by the other is like its death by natural causes. As for injury of slaves upon slaves, it is considered, even if it necessitates retaliation or surrender or ransom, so the killer stands in the place of the killed, so the debt of the killed is transferred to the killer. Then by what amount it is transferred will come. If one pledges two slaves, either he pledges them in a single transaction or in two transactions. If he pledges them in a single transaction for one thousand and each one's value is one thousand, and one kills the other, the remaining one is a pledge for nine hundred and fifty, because each one: half is encumbered and half is unencumbered. The unencumbered half of the killed is lost by injury of the unencumbered upon the encumbered and by injury of the unencumbered upon the unencumbered, and all that is of no consequence. The encumbered half is lost by injury of the encumbered upon the encumbered, and that is of no consequence. So it is as if it were a pledge for seven hundred from the slave.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the ruling on injury caused by a pledged item (al-rahn). The commentator begins by quoting the matn: 'وجناية الرهن عليهما وعلى مالهما هدر' meaning that any injury caused by the pledged property to the pledgor (rahin) or mortgagee (murtahin) or their property is of no consequence (hadar) — i.e., no liability arises. However, the commentator immediately notes that this absolute statement is not fully apparent, because there are exceptions: if the injury causes harm that warrants retaliation (qisas), such as killing or severing limbs, then it is considered and qisas becomes obligatory. Also, there is a distinction between injury to the pledgor vs. mortgagee, and between injuries that necessitate only financial compensation vs. those that necessitate surrender of the slave. The passage then explains the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: injury by the pledge upon the mortgagee is not considered because it would provide no benefit (since the mortgagee already has a right in the pledge). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they argue that if the injury is upon the mortgagee, it can be beneficial because the mortgagee might choose to take ownership of the slave instead of the debt. The commentator also gives examples: a slave who digs a well, then is freed, then falls into it — his blood is wasted because he is like a self-injurer. Another example: two slaves dig a well, a pledged slave falls in, they pay, then one of the diggers falls in — half the debt is voided. The passage then discusses the principle from al-Mabsut: injury of the encumbered (mashghul) upon the encumbered is of no consequence (hadar), but some debt drops. Injury of the unencumbered (farigh) upon the encumbered is considered and debt transfers. The text also covers cases of two pledged animals vs. two pledged slaves: for animals, the destruction is like natural death; for slaves, the debt is transferred to the killer. Finally, an example of two slaves pledged in one transaction: each has half encumbered and half unencumbered, leading to a specific calculation of the remaining debt. The teacher should note that this passage is a detailed expansion of the general rule, emphasizing that the 'consideration' of injury depends on whether it benefits the mortgagee's right.

Key Terms
مشغول (mashghūl): Encumbered; a share of the pledge that is occupied by the debt.
فارغ (fārigh): Unencumbered; a share of the pledge that is free from debt obligation.
جبار (jubbār): Of no effect; used in the hadith 'جرح العجماء جبار' meaning injury by a dumb animal is not compensable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the debt when a pledged animal destroys another pledged animal?
A) The debt is fully transferred to the killer animal.
B) The debt is reduced proportionally from the total.
C) The debt remains unchanged because the injury is considered.
D) The entire debt is cancelled.

Key Takeaway
Injury among pledges is assessed based on benefit to the mortgagee; only injury from unencumbered to encumbered transfers debt, while other combinations result in proportional loss or no effect.

Options When One Mortgaged Slave Kills Another (Separate Contracts)
Ruling with proof (qiyas) on options for injury between separately mortgaged slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to the mortgagor and mortgagee when one of two separately mortgaged slaves kills the other, and apply the qiyas to injury of a third party's slave.

Core Idea
When two slaves are mortgaged separately, each is vacant relative to the other, so the choice mirrors injury to a stranger's slave.

This passage explains the rulings when a mortgaged slave kills or injures another mortgaged slave, but where each slave is pledged under a separate contract. The key principle is that the debts are independent, so the legal options are analogous to injury to a third party. The parties may either exchange the killer for the slain (cancelling the debt on the slain) or ransom the killer by paying its value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the two slaves are mortgaged separately (صفقة على حدة). This means each slave's debt is independent; they are 'vacant' (فارغ) relative to each other.
If they were mortgaged together in one contract, the ruling would differ.
2
Determine if there is surplus value
Check whether the value of each slave exceeds the debt for which it is pledged. If there is no surplus, the debt on the slain drops because handing over the killer provides no benefit.
If surplus exists, the parties have a choice.
3
Apply the choice between exchange and ransom
When surplus exists, the mortgagor and mortgagee may either (a) exchange the killer for the slain, cancelling the debt on the slain, or (b) ransom the killer by paying its value (the value of the slain).
In ransom, each party pays half of the value, and that amount becomes a new pledge.
4
Recognize the qiyas to injury of a third party's slave
The ruling is analogized (qiyas jali) to a case where a mortgaged slave injures a slave belonging to a stranger. The same choice between surrender and ransom applies.
This is stated explicitly: 'فصار كما لو جنى أحدهما على عبد لأجنبي'.
5
Extend to partial injury (eye gouging)
Partial destruction (e.g., gouging an eye) is treated like total destruction by way of qiyas: the same choice of surrender or ransom, with the ransom being the full arsh (blood money) of the lost part.
The text says 'يعتبر بإتلاف الكل'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أرباع خمسمائة، وأما إذا ارتهن عبدين كل واحد بخمسمائة بصفقة على حدة فقتل أحدهما صاحبه، فإن لم يكن فيهما فضل عن الدين روي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه يسقط ما في المجني عليه لأنه لا فائدة في الدفع للمرتهن وهدرت الجناية فإن كان فيهما فضل يخير الراهن والمرتهن إن شاء جعلا القاتل مكان المقتول وبطل ما في المقتول من الدين، وإن شاء أفديا القاتل بقيمة المقتول وغرم كل واحد خمسمائة فكانت القيمة رهناً مكان المقتول. والقاتل رهن بحاله لأن المقتول كله تلف بجناية الفارغ لأن الصفقة متى تفرقت فالحق المتعلق بأحدهما لا يتعلق بالآخر فكان كل واحد منهما فارغاً عن الآخر، ولهذا لو قضى دين أحدهما كان له أن يفتكه وجناية المشغول على الفارغ معتبرة فصار كما لو جنى أحدهما على عبد لأجنبي يخير الراهن والمرتهن بين الدفع والفداء فكذا هذا وإن اختار الفداء فكذا هذا. وإن اختار الفداء غرم كل واحد خمسمائة لأن نصف القاتل مضمون على المرتهن وعبده أمانة عنده فكان الفداء عليهما اعتباراً للبعض بالكل، وإن كان فقأ أحدهما عين الآخر فقيل لهما ادفعاه أو افدياه بأرش عليه الآخر لأن إتلاف البعض يعتبر بإتلاف الكل، وفي إتلاف الكل يخير فكذا في إتلاف البعض، فإن دفعه بطل ما فيه من الدين، وإن فدياه كان الفداء عليهما نصفين رهناً مع المفقوءة عينه. ولو قال المرتهن لا أفدي وادع الرهن على حاله له ذلك والمفقوءة عينه ذهب نصف باقية لأن هذه الجناية إنما تعتبر لحق المرتهن لا لحق الراهن لأنه لو طلب الجناية ودفع الجاني سقط نصف الدين ولو ترك الجناية يسقط الدين فكان ربع في طلب الجناية ضرر بالمرتهن، فإذا رضي بإبطال حقه فله ذلك ويسقط اعتبار الجناية، ولو قال الراهن افديه وقال المرتهن لا أفديه للراهن أن يفديه بأرش الجناية كلها لأنه محتاج إلى الفداء ليخلص عبد الرهن عند الجناية، فإن فداه يكون له نصف ذلك عما على المرتهن في العبد الجاني ويبطل في حقه من العبد الجاني نصفه لأن الرهن مضطر إلى الفداء يحيي ملكه والإنسان فيما يحيي ملكه لا يكون متبرعاً فيكون له حق الرجوع عليه وللمرتهن عليه مثله فيلتقيان قصاصاً فيصير مؤدياً دين القاتل فيخرج القاتل من الرهن وإن أبى الراهن الفداء وقال المرتهن أفدي وفدى يكون متطوعاً فيه إذا كان الراهن حاضراً لأن بقدر المضمون أدى عن نفسه وبقدر الأمانة أدى عن الراهن وهو غير مضطر فيه لأنه غير محيي ملكه فيكون متبرعاً. وإن كان الراهن غائباً كان على الراهن نصف الفداء ديناً، قيل هذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، وعندهما يكون متبرعاً كان الراهن حاضراً أو غائباً لما يأتي.
Quarter of five hundred. And if he takes two slaves in pawn, each for five hundred, in a separate contract, and one kills the other, then if there is no surplus over the debt, it is related from Abu Hanifa that the debt on the slain one drops because there is no benefit in handing over (the killer) to the mortgagee, and the injury is disregarded. If there is surplus, the mortgagor and mortgagee have a choice: if they wish, they may place the killer in the position of the slain and the debt on the slain is cancelled; if they wish, they may ransom the killer for the value of the slain, and each pays five hundred, so the value becomes a pledge in place of the slain. The killer remains a pledge as before because the slain is entirely lost due to the injury of the 'vacant' one. When the bargain is separate, the right attached to one does not attach to the other, so each is vacant with respect to the other. Hence, if the debt of one is paid off, he may redeem it. The injury of the 'encumbered' one upon the 'vacant' one is considered, so it becomes as if one injured a slave belonging to a stranger: the mortgagor and mortgagee are given the choice between surrender and ransom. Similarly here if they choose ransom. And if they choose ransom, each pays five hundred because half of the killer is guaranteed by the mortgagee, and his slave is a trust with him, so the ransom is upon both, considering part as whole. If one gouges out the eye of the other, they are told: either surrender him or ransom him with the full arsh because partial destruction is considered like total destruction. In total destruction they have a choice, similarly in partial destruction. If they surrender him, the debt on him is cancelled; if they ransom him, the ransom falls on both equally, and it becomes a pledge along with the one whose eye is gouged. If the mortgagee says, 'I will not ransom, leave the pledge as it is,' he may do so, and the one whose eye is gouged loses half (the debt) remains, because this injury is only considered for the right of the mortgagee, not the mortgagor. If he claims the injury and surrenders the injurer, half the debt falls; if he abandons the claim, half the debt falls, so demanding injury would harm the mortgagee. If he consents to forfeit his right, he may do so, and the consideration of the injury falls. If the mortgagor says, 'I will ransom it,' and the mortgagee says, 'I will not ransom,' the mortgagor may ransom it with the full arsh because he needs redemption to free the pledged slave from injury. If he ransoms it, he has half of that against the mortgagee for his share in the injuring slave, and in his own right half of the injuring slave is cancelled because the mortgagor is compelled to ransom to revive his property, and a person reviving his property is not a volunteer, so he has a right of recourse. The mortgagee has a similar claim against him, so they cancel out (by way of qisas), making him pay the debt of the killer, so the killer exits from the pledge. If the mortgagor refuses ransom and the mortgagee says, 'I will ransom,' and he ransoms, he is a volunteer if the mortgagor is present because he pays for himself to the extent of his guarantee, and pays for the mortgagor to the extent of the trust, and he is not compelled because he does not revive his property, so he is a volunteer. If the mortgagor is absent, half the ransom is a debt upon the mortgagor. It is said this is according to Abu Hanifa; according to the two companions, he is a volunteer whether the mortgagor is present or absent, as will come.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding injury between two mortgaged slaves where each is pledged for a separate debt. The author presents the ruling of Abu Hanifa as related, with detailed options for the parties. The key principle is that when the bargain is distinct (صَفْقَة على حِدَة), each slave is considered 'vacant' (فارغ) relative to the other, so the debt does not transfer. The ruling uses analogy (qiyas) to the case of injury to a third party's slave. The passage also covers partial injury (gouging an eye), and the scenarios where one party refuses ransom. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute mentioned: according to Abu Hanifa, if the mortgagee ransoms in the absence of the mortgagor, half the ransom is a debt; according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the mortgagee is a volunteer in both cases.

Key Terms
صفقة على حدة (safqah 'ala hidah): A separate purchase contract for each slave
فارغ (fārigh): A slave not encumbered by the debt of the other

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if two separately mortgaged slaves have no surplus over their debts and one kills the other, what happens?
A) The killer is handed over to the mortgagee of the slain.
B) The debt on the slain is cancelled and the injury is disregarded.
C) The killer is sold and the proceeds are divided.
D) The mortgagor must pay the value of the slain.

Key Takeaway
When two slaves are mortgaged separately, each is considered vacant relative to the other, and the parties may choose to exchange or ransom upon injury, analogously to injury of a third party's slave.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Mortgagee's Ransom in Absence of Mortgagor
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mortgagee's right to reimbursement when ransoming in mortgagor's absence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding whether the mortgagee is entitled to reimbursement when ransoming a killer slave in the mortgagor's absence, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When the mortgagee ransoms in the mortgagor's absence, Abu Hanifa sees half as a debt; the Sahibayn see the mortgagee as a volunteer.

This section of the passage addresses a scenario where one party (mortgagor or mortgagee) refuses to ransom, and the other ransoms alone. The key intra-Hanafi dispute arises when the mortgagee ransoms while the mortgagor is absent: is the mortgagee a volunteer or entitled to half the ransom from the mortgagor? The text presents the views of Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: one party refuses ransom
The text considers two situations: (a) mortgagee refuses, mortgagor ransoms; (b) mortgagor refuses, mortgagee ransoms. Focus on (b).
The dispute concerns situation (b) when the mortgagor is absent.
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa: if the mortgagee ransoms in the mortgagor's absence, half the ransom is a debt on the mortgagor. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the mortgagee is a volunteer, whether the mortgagor is present or absent.
The text says 'قيل هذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يكون متبرعاً'.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that the mortgagee is reviving his own property (the killer slave is his security), so he is not a volunteer. The Sahibayn argue that the mortgagee is reviving the mortgagor's property (the killer slave belongs to the mortgagor), so he is a volunteer.
The difference hinges on whether the benefit of revival is considered for the mortgagee's own right or the mortgagor's.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
If the mortgagee ransoms in absence, according to Abu Hanifa he can claim half the ransom from the mortgagor; according to the Sahibayn, he cannot.
This affects the mortgagee's willingness to ransom when the mortgagor is unavailable.
5
Note the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi practice follows the Sahibayn: the mortgagee is a volunteer in all cases.
The text does not explicitly choose, but later works adopt the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

This passage is a ruling from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding injury between two mortgaged slaves where each is pledged for a separate debt. Key Terms
فارغ (fārigh): A slave not encumbered by the debt of the other
مشغول (mashghūl): A slave encumbered by his own debt (i.e., the one for which he is pledged)
متبرع (mutabarri'): Volunteer, one who acts without expectation of reimbursement

According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the ruling when a mortgagee ransoms a killer slave in the mortgagor's absence?
A) Half the ransom is a debt on the mortgagor.

When the mortgagee ransoms in the mortgagor's absence, the mufta bihi (Sahibayn) view holds that the mortgagee is a volunteer and cannot claim reimbursement from the mortgagor.

Three Dimensions of a Pawned Slave Injury Case
Analyzing three legal dimensions of a complex injury case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings in a case of two pawned slaves injuring each other and explain how the debt allocation shifts between the borrower, mortgagee, and owners.

Core Idea
Pawned slaves' injuries shift debt and create claims between three pairs of parties.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a complex case involving two borrowed slaves who are pawned for a debt and then injure each other's eyes. The Hanafi jurist breaks down the legal implications into three distinct dimensions: between the borrower and the creditor (mortgagee), between the borrower and the slave owners, and between the two owners themselves. Understanding this case trains the student in proportional allocation and the interaction of pawn law with torts.

Guided Path
1
Dimension 1: Borrower vs Mortgagee
Determines how the debt secured by each slave changes after the injuries. The debt allocation shifts because the free portion of the injured slave’s value is lost and must be compensated.
Focus on the initial assumption: each slave is half free and half pawned because total value=2000, debt=1000.
2
Dimension 2: Borrower vs Owners
The borrower (who is the pawner) must compensate the owners for the free portion of the eyes destroyed, as the injury on the pawned portion is wasted (hadar).
The compensation amounts are derived from the blood money of an eye (500 dirhams for each eye).
3
Dimension 3: Owners vs Owners
The two owners must adjust their claims by exchanging shares of the slaves or payments to settle the net differences from the compensation received from the borrower.
The final result is that each slave is fully redeemed without further claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا استعار من رجلين عبدين قيمة كل واحد ألف فرهنهما بألف ففقأ أحدهما عين الآخر ثم المفقوءة عينه فقأ عين الفاقئ فهنا أحكام ثلاثة حكم بين المستعير والمرتهن، وحكم فيما بين المستعير والمعيرين وحكم فيما بين المعيرين. أما الحكم فيما بين المستعير والمرتهن فنقول: إن كل عبد نصفه فارغ ونصفه مشغول فلما فقأ عين الأكبر الأصغر فقد أتلف نصفه لأن العين من الآدمي نصفه فالجناية على النصف الفارغ وعلى النصف المشغول هدر لما بينا فسقط ما بإزائه من الدين وذلك مائة وخمسة وعشرون والجناية على نصف النصف المشغول معتبرة لأنه تلف بجناية الفارغ على المشغول فيتحول ما بإزائه من الدين إلى القاتل وذلك مائة وعشرون فبقي الأصغر رهناً بمائتين وخمسين فصار الأكبر رهناً بستمائة وخمسة وعشرين، ثم لما فقأ الأصغر عين الأكبر فقد أتلف نصف الأكبر وبإزاء نصفه ثلاثمائة واثني عشر ونصف فسقط نصف ذلك وذلك مائة وستة وخمسون وربع ويتحول نصف الآخر وذلك الأصغر فبقي الأكبر رهناً بثلاثمائة واثني عشر ونصف وصار الأصغر رهناً بأربعمائة وستة وربع فيكون جملة ذلك سبعمائة وثمانية عشر وثلاثة أرباع وسقط مائتان واحد وثمانون وربع . الحكم فيما بين المعير والمستعير فالمستعير يفتك العبد بسبعمائة وثمانية عشر درهماً وثلاثة أرباع درهم وعليه أيضاً لولي العبد المفقوءة عينه أولاً مائة وخمسة وعشرون ولولي العبد المفقوءة عينه آخراً مائة وستة وخمسون وربع لأن كل واحد من الموليين صار قاضياً دينه من عبده هذا القدر. وأمال الحكم فيما بين المعيرين وهو أن يقال لمولى العبد الأكبر ادفع ثلاثة أرباع عبدك إلى الثاني وافده بثلاثة أرباع أرش الفاقئ الآخر لأنه وصل إليه ربع أرش العين من جهة المستعير لأنه وصل إليه من جهة المستعير مائة وخمسة وعشرون وذلك ربع أرش العين لأن أرش العين الواحدة خمسمائة كانت قيمة العبد ألفاً ولم يصل إليه ثلاثة أرباع أرض العين، فإن فدى يقال المولى الأصغر ادفع من عبدك ثلاثة أخماسه وثلاثة أثمان خمسه ونصف ثمن خمسة أو افده بمثل ذلك من أرش العين لأنه وصل إلى مولى الأكبر من جهة المستعير مائة وستة وخمسون أرش العين وأربعة أثمان أخماسه ونصف ثمن خمس، فإذا دفع أو فدى وربع فقد برئ من حي فظهر كل عبدين جناتين وعشر ولا يرجع واحد على صاحبه بشيء.
And if he borrowed from two men two slaves, each worth a thousand, and pawned them both for a thousand, and one poked out the eye of the other, then the one whose eye was poked out poked out the eye of the poker, then here are three rulings: a ruling between the borrower and the mortgagee, a ruling between the borrower and the two lenders, and a ruling between the two lenders. As for the ruling between the borrower and the mortgagee, we say: each slave is half free and half occupied. When the larger poked out the eye of the smaller, he has destroyed half of him because the eye of a human is half of him. So the injury is on the free half and on the occupied half is wasted as we have shown, so what corresponds to it of the debt falls, which is one hundred and twenty-five. And the injury on half of the occupied half is considered because it was destroyed by the injury of the free on the occupied, so what corresponds to it of the debt transfers to the killer, which is one hundred and twenty. So the smaller remains as pawn for two hundred and fifty, and the larger becomes pawn for six hundred and twenty-five. Then when the smaller poked out the eye of the larger, he has destroyed half of the larger, and against half of him is three hundred and twelve and a half, so half of that falls, which is one hundred and fifty-six and a quarter, and the other half transfers to the smaller. So the larger remains as pawn for three hundred and twelve and a half, and the smaller becomes pawn for four hundred and six and a quarter. So the total is seven hundred and eighteen and three-quarters, and two hundred and eighty-one and a quarter falls. The ruling between the lender and the borrower: the borrower ransoms the slave for seven hundred and eighteen dirhams and three-quarters of a dirham, and he also owes the guardian of the slave whose eye was poked out first one hundred and twenty-five, and the guardian of the slave whose eye was poked out last one hundred and fifty-six and a quarter, because each of the two guardians has been paid his debt from his slave by this amount. As for the ruling between the two lenders, it is said to the guardian of the larger slave: pay three-quarters of your slave to the second and ransom him with three-quarters of the blood money of the other poker, because a quarter of the blood money of the eye reached him from the borrower, for one hundred and twenty-five reached him from the borrower, which is a quarter of the blood money of the eye, because the blood money of one eye is five hundred, the value of the slave was a thousand, and he did not receive three-quarters of the blood money of the eye. If he ransoms, it is said to the smaller guardian: pay three-fifths and three-eighths of a fifth and half of an eighth of a fifth of your slave, or ransom him with the same from the blood money of the eye, because to the guardian of the larger from the borrower reached one hundred and fifty-six plus four-eighths of a fifth and half of an eighth of a fifth of the blood money of the eye. So if he pays or ransoms and a quarter, he becomes free from liability. So it appears that each of the two slaves is ransomed completely, and neither has any claim against the other.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal ruling (hukm) from the commentary on a scenario involving two borrowed slaves (musta'ir) from two different owners (mu'ir), who are then pawned together for a debt. The case involves reciprocal eye-poking injuries. The author presents three dimensions of the ruling: (1) between the borrower (who is the mortgagee) and the creditor (mortgagee? Actually the borrower is the mortgagor? Let's clarify: The scenario: a person borrows two slaves from two different owners, then pawns them to a creditor for a debt of 1000 dirhams. So the borrower is the pawner (rahin) and the creditor is the mortgagee (murtahin). The borrower is also the المستعير (borrower of the slaves). So there are three parties: the borrower (pawner), the creditor (mortgagee), and the two owners (mu'ir). The creditor holds the slaves as pawn. Now the first slave (larger) pokes out the eye of the second (smaller). Then the second retaliates and pokes out the first's eye. Each slave is half free (فارغ) and half pawned (مشغول) because the debt is 1000 and total value is 2000, so each slave secures half the debt (500). When an eye is destroyed, half of that slave is lost (eye is half the human). The injury on the free half is compensable, but on the pawned half is هدر (wasted) because it is under pawn. The compensation for the eye (blood money) is 500 (half the value of the slave). The calculation adjusts the debt distribution among the slaves and the killer. The commentary walks through the fractions step by step. This is a typical Hanafi exercise in proportional allocation, similar to faraid but for debt and injury.

Key Terms
فارغ (fārigh): Free portion of a pawned slave not secured by debt.
مشغول (mashghūl): Occupied portion of a pawned slave that secures the debt.
هدر (hadar): Null, wasted; here means that the injury on the pawned portion does not give right to compensation because it is already encumbered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario of two borrowed pawned slaves poking each other's eyes, how many legal dimensions (rulings) are considered?
A) Two: between borrower and mortgagee, and between the two owners.
B) Three: between borrower and mortgagee, between borrower and owners, and between the two owners.
C) Four: including the killer and the judge.
D) One: only the final compensation amount.

Key Takeaway
A pawned slave injury case produces three distinct rulings affecting debtor, creditor, and owners, with debt allocation shifting based on the free and pawned portions.

Market Price Decrease of a Pawn: No Reduction of Debt
Commentary on pawn value fluctuation rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that a market price decrease of a pawn does not reduce the secured debt, and distinguish this from a physical defect using the proof provided in the commentary.

Core Idea
Market price decrease of a pawn does not reduce the debt; only physical defects do.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi pawn (rahn) law: when the value of a pawned item drops due to market fluctuations, the debt remains intact. We will explore the reasoning (dalil) behind this ruling, contrast it with an opposing view from Zufar, and see how it applies to related scenarios like sale at a loss and increase in value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Read the matn case: a pawned slave worth 1000 is pawned for 1000, its market price drops to 100, then a third party kills it by mistake and pays 100 diya. The mortgagee takes the 100 and has no claim against the pawner.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The debt remains fully secured despite the price drop. The mortgagee recovers only the actual value received (100) and cannot claim the shortfall from the pawner.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The commentator argues that market price decrease (nuqsan al-sir) is due to slackening public demand, not a defect in the pawn itself. This is not considered in sales (buyer has no option) nor in usurpation (guarantor not liable for price drop). Therefore, it does not affect secured rights.
4
Contrast with Zufar's view
Zufar analogizes price decrease to physical defect (nuqsan al-ayn) because both reduce monetary value. The Hanafi response: physical defect diminishes the pawn itself; price decrease is external and thus not a basis for reducing liability.
5
Apply to related cases
If the mortgagee sells the pawn at the lower price by the pawner's order, he takes the sale price and can recover the remaining debt from the pawner. For increase in value, any loss is attributed to the increase (the dependent) first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الله : (ولو رهن عبداً يساوي ألفاً بألف ورجعت قيمته إلى مائة فقتله رجل خطأ وغرم مائة وحل الأجل فالمرتهن يقبض المائة قضاء لحقه ولا يرجع على الراهن بشيء) ولو باعه بمائة بأمره قبض المائة قضاء حقه ورجع بتسعمائة فإن قتله عبد وغرم رجع قیمته من أصله أن النقصان من حيث السعر لا يوجب سقوط الدين عندنا وقد قدمنا ما فيه من التفصيل خلافاً لزفر، وهو يقول إن المالية قد انتقصت فأشبه انتقاص العين. ولنا أن نقصان السعر عبارة عن فتور رغبات الناس وذلك غير معتبر في المبيع حتى إذا حصل في المبيع قبل القبض لا يثبت للمشتري الخيار، ولو حصل في الغصب لا يوجب على الغاصب ضمان ما نقص بالسعر عند رد العين المغصوبة بخلاف نقصان العين على ما تقدم. وإذا قتله يوم الإتلاف لأن القيمة تعتبر يوم الإتلاف لأن المولى استحقه بسبب المالية بحق المرتهن يتعلق بالمالية فكذا فيما قام مقامه . ثم لا يرجع على الراهن بشيء لأن يد الراهن يد استيفاء من الابتداء أو نقول : لا يمكن أن يجعل مستوياً للألف بمائة لأنه يؤدي إلى الربا فيصير مستوفياً المائة وبقي تسعمائة في العين، فإذا هلكت يصير مستوفياً لتسعمائة بالهلاك بخلاف ما إذا كان من غير قتل أحد لأنه يصير مستوفياً للكل بالعبد ولا يؤدي إلى الربا بالاختلاف الجنس بخلاف المسألة الأولى لأنا لو جلعناه مستوفياً للألف بمائة يؤدي إلى الربا فجعلناه مستوفياً تسعمائة بالعبد الهالك وهو المقتول والمائة بالمائة . قال رحمه الله : (ولو باعه بمائة بأمره قبض المائة قضاء من حقه ورجع بتسعمائة) أي لو باع المرتهن العبد الذي يساوي ألفاً بمائة بأمر الراهن وكان رهناً بألف قبض المرتهن تلك المائة التي هي الثمن قضاء لحقه على الراهن بتسعمائة لأنه لما باعه بإذن الراهن صار كأنه الرهن استرده وباعه بنفسه، ولو كان كذلك بطل الرهن وبقي الدين إلا بقدر ما استوفاه فكذا هنا هذا فيما إذا نقصت قيمته بتغيير السعر فجنى عليه وأما إذا زاد ثلث قيمته بتغيير السعر فجنى عليه أو مات بالسراية أو جنى المرهونة ولدها أو أعور المرهون أو زال عوره فجنى عليه فنذكر ذلك تتميماً للفائدة . قال في المبسوط : عبد مرهون صارت قيمته ألفين فصار كما لو غصبه غاصب يضمن ألفين فكذا هذا، فإن أدى ألفاً وتوى ألف كان المرتهن أولى بها لأن القيمة الأصلية كانت ألفاً . زادت ألفاً أخرى فكانت هذه الألف الزائدة تبعاً للألف الأصلية حيث وجدت بسبب وجودها، فإذا ورد الهلاك يصرف إلى التابع لا إلى الأصل وإلى التابع جميعاً لأن فيه إلحاق التابع بالأصل ولا يجوز ذلك، ولا يمكن صرفه إلى الأصل دون التابع لأنه لا يمكن إيفاء التابع دون الأصل، ولأن فيه ترجيح التابع على الأصل وذلك ممتنع فصرفنا الهلاك إلى التابع ضرورة تحقيقاً للتبعية كما في المضاربة يصرف الهلاك إلى الربح وإن كانت قيمته في الأصل ألفين فما يخرج من قيمته بين الراهن والمرتهن نصفين وما توى بينهما لأن كل واحد منهما أصل بنفسه، فما توى يتوى على الحقين، وما يخرج يخرج على الحقين. عبد مرهون بألف وقيمته ألف فقتله عبدان فدفعا به فهما جميعاً رهن بألف لأنهما قاما مقام الأول فيكون حكمهما كالأول فتكون جناية أحدهما إلى صاحبه كجناية الأول على نفسه وذلك هدر وغير
He (the author of Kanz) said: (And if he pawns a slave worth a thousand for a thousand, and its value returns to a hundred, then a man kills it by mistake and pays a hundred, and the term matures, then the mortgagee takes the hundred as payment for his right and does not claim anything from the pawner.) And if he sells it for a hundred by his order, he takes the hundred as payment for his right and recovers nine hundred. For if a slave kills it and pays its price, the origin is that decrease in price does not necessitate reduction of debt according to us, and we have already presented the detail of that, contrary to Zufar. He says that the monetary value has decreased, so it resembles decrease in the physical substance. Our evidence is that decrease in price is an expression of slackening of people's desires, and that is not considered in sales; even if it occurs in a sold item before delivery, the buyer does not have the option, and if it occurs in a usurped item, it does not obligate the usurper to guarantee the decrease in price when returning the usurped item, unlike decrease in the physical substance as previously mentioned. And if he kills it on the day of destruction, because value is considered on the day of destruction, because the owner is entitled to it due to monetary value; the right of the mortgagee attaches to monetary value, so likewise for what stands in its place. Then he does not claim anything from the pawner because the pawner's hand is a hand of recovery from the beginning, or we say: it is not possible to consider him as having recovered the thousand by the hundred, because it leads to riba. So he is considered to have recovered the hundred, and nine hundred remain in the slave. So if the slave perishes, he is considered to have recovered the nine hundred by the perishing, unlike the case where there is no killing, because then he is considered to have recovered everything by the slave, and it does not lead to riba due to difference in kind, unlike the first case. Because if we considered him to have recovered the thousand by the hundred, it would lead to riba, so we considered him to have recovered nine hundred by the dead slave (the murdered one) and the hundred by the hundred. He (Ibn Nujaym) said: (And if he sells it for a hundred by his order, he takes the hundred as payment from his right and recovers nine hundred), meaning if the mortgagee sells the slave worth a thousand for a hundred by order of the pawner, and it was pawned for a thousand, the mortgagee takes that hundred which is the price as payment for his right, and he has recourse against the pawner for nine hundred, because when he sold it with the permission of the pawner, it is as if the pawner redeemed it and sold it himself, and if that were the case, the pawn would be void and the debt remains except for what he recovered. So likewise here. This applies when its value decreased by change in price and then an injury occurred. But if its value increased by a third of its value by change in price and then an injury occurred, or it died due to spontaneous effect, or the pawned female gave birth, or the pawned slave became one-eyed, or its one-eyed condition disappeared, and then an injury occurred, we will mention that to complete the benefit. He said in al-Mabsut: A pawned slave whose value became two thousand, so it is as if a usurper usurped it and is liable for two thousand; likewise here. If he pays a thousand and a thousand is lost, the mortgagee has priority to it because the original value was a thousand. Another thousand increased, so this increased thousand is a dependent of the original thousand because it originated due to its existence. So when loss occurs, it is attributed to the dependent, not to the original, nor to both together, because that would attach the dependent to the original and that is not permissible. It cannot be attributed to the original alone without the dependent because the dependent cannot be fulfilled without the original, and because that would prefer the dependent over the original, which is impossible. So we attribute the loss to the dependent by necessity to realize dependency, as in mudaraba where loss is attributed to profit. And if its value in origin is two thousand, then what comes out of its value is divided between the pawner and mortgagee equally, and what is lost is lost between them, because each of them is a principal in itself. So what is lost is lost on both rights, and what comes out comes out on both rights. A slave pawned for a thousand, value a thousand, then two slaves killed it and are paid for it, so they both are pawn for a thousand because they stand in place of the first, so their ruling is like the first; so the injury of one against the other is like the injury of the first against himself, and that is null and void.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It deals with several rulings when the value of a pawned slave changes. First, the matn gives a case: the pawned slave's value drops from 1000 to 100 due to market decline, then a stranger kills him by mistake and pays 100 diya. The mortgagee takes that 100 as payment for the debt and has no claim against the pawner for the remaining 900 because the decrease was in price, not physical defect. The commentator then extends: if the mortgagee sells the slave by order of the pawner for 100, he takes the 100 and can recover 900 from the pawner. The principle is established: decrease in market price (نقصان السعر) does not reduce the debt, unlike physical defect (نقصان العين). This is the Hanafi position, opposing Zufar who analogized price drop to physical defect. The proof (dalil) is that price fluctuation is due to changing demand, which is not considered in sales or guarantees. Then the commentator discusses increase in value: if the pawn's value rises to 2000, the increase is a trust in the mortgagee's hand, and any loss is attributed to the increase first. Finally, a case where two slaves kill a pawned slave: they both become pawn for the original debt, and injuries between them are null.

Key Terms
سعر (si‘r): Market price; fluctuation due to demand/supply.
هلاك (halāk): Destruction or loss of the pawn.
تابع (tābi‘): Accessory; the increased value of the pawn that depends on the original.
أصل (aṣl): Principal; the original value of the pawn or the original debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pawned slave's market value drops from 1000 to 100 (no injury), and then a third party kills the slave and pays 100 diya, what does the mortgagee receive?
A) The 100 diya as full payment and no claim against the pawner.
B) The 100 diya plus the pawner must pay the remaining 900.
C) The mortgagee can take the 100 diya and also demand the original 1000 from the pawner.
D) The pawn is void and the mortgagee gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
A decrease in the market price of a pawn does not reduce the secured debt; only physical defects affect the rights of the parties.

When a Pledged Item Changes State – Grape Juice to Wine to Vinegar
Detailed ruling and commentary on transformation of pledged items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pledged item that changes from grape juice to wine to vinegar, and distinguish whether value or quantity determines the remaining debt.

Core Idea
A pledge remains valid if the substance stays; loss of value does not reduce debt, only loss of quantity does.

This lesson examines the first major ruling in the passage: if a Muslim pledges grape juice worth ten for ten, and it becomes wine and then vinegar, the pledge remains valid for ten. The key principle is that the item's substance persists, and the consideration is quantity (weight or volume), not market value. This ruling uses qiyas to the principle that wine is a valid subject of sale in continuation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its conditions
The act is a pledge (rahn) of grape juice by a Muslim pledgor to a Muslim pledgee for a debt of ten. Note that the item transforms twice: grape juice → wine → vinegar.
The religious status of the parties affects later rulings.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The pledge remains valid for the original debt amount (ten), provided the quantity (volume/weight) has not decreased.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof is based on the principle: 'What is a valid subject of sale in continuation is a valid subject of pledge in continuation.' Wine, though not a valid subject for initial sale to Muslims, can be sold after it becomes wine, so it is valid for pledge in continuation.
This is a qiyas (analogy) between pledge and sale.
4
Distinguish value vs quantity
The text makes a critical distinction: the pledge is about the substance (quantity measured by weight/volume), not its market value. If the quantity decreases, the debt reduces proportionally; if only value changes, the debt remains unchanged.
This is a consensus (ijma) among the Hanafi companions.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
If 5 liters of grape juice are pledged for 50 dirhams and after transformation only 4.5 liters remain due to evaporation, the debt reduces to 45 dirhams.
The same applies if the market value fluctuates independently.

كتاب الرهن باب التصرف في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره فصل رهن عصيراً قيمته عشرة بعشرة فتخمر ثم تخلل وهو يساوي عشرة فهو رهن بعشرة وللآخر أن يردوه لأنه إيثار لبعض الغرماء بالإيفاء الحكمي فأشبهه الإيثار بالإيفاء الحقيقي، والجامع ما في كل واحد منهما من إبطال حق غيره من الغرماء ألا ترى أن الميت بنفسه لا يملك ذلك بمرض موته فكذا من قام مقامه . وإن قضى دينهم قبل أن يردوه جاز لزوال المانع ووصول حقهم، ولو لم يكن للميت غريم آخر جاز الرهن اعتباراً بالإيفاء الحقيقي وبيع في يباع فيه قبل الرهن فكذا بعده، وإذا ارتهن الوصي بدين للميت على رجل جاز لأنه استيفاء فيملكه وله أن يبيعه والله أعلم. دينه لأنه تخلف عن فصل هذا الفصل بمنزلة المتفرقة المذكورة في أواخر الكتب فلذا أخره استدراكاً لما فاته فيما سبق . قال رحمه الله : رهن عصيراً قيمته عشرة بعشرة فتخمر ثم تخلل وهو يساوي عشرة فهو رهن بعشرة) يعني إذا رهن عند مسلم عصيراً إلى آخرها قالوا ما كان محلاً للبيع بقاء يكون محلاً للرهن بقاء كما أن ما يكون محلاً للبيع ابتداء يكون محلاً للرهن ابتداء والخمر محل للبيع بقاء وإن لم يكن محلاً له ابتداء ، أقول : لقائل أن يقول لو كان مدار مسألتنا المذكورة على هذا القدر من التعليل لما ظهر فائدة قوله ثم صار خلاً في وضع مسألة بل كان يكفي أن يقال ومن رهن عصيراً بعشرة فتخمر فهو رهن بعشرة لكفاية التعليل المذكور بعينه في إثبات هذا المعنى العام فتأمل . قال صاحب العناية : ولقائل أن يقول ما يرجع إلى المحل فالابتداء والبقاء فيه سواء فما بال هذا ذلك الأصل؟ وقال : ويمكن أن يجاب عنه بأنه كذلك فيما يكون المحل باقياً وههنا يتبدل المحل حكماً بتبدل الوصف فكذلك تخلف عن ذلك الأصل ا هـ . . أقول : قوله : «ثم تخلل وهي تساوي عشرة» يشير إلى أن المعتبر فيه في الزيادة والنقصان القيمة وليس كذلك بل المعتبر القدر لأن العصير والخل من المقدرات لأنه إما مكيل أو موزون وفيها نقصان القيمة لا يوجب سقوط شيء من ذلك الدين كما مر في انكسار القلب، وإنما يوجب الخيار على ما ذكرنا لأن الغاية فيه مجرد الوصف وفوات كل شيء من الوصف في المكيل والموزون لا يوجب سقوط شيء من الدين بإجماع بين أصحابنا فيكون الحكم فيه أنه إن نقص شيء من القدر سقط بقدره شيء من الدين وإلا فلا. وأشار بقوله ثم تخلل إلى أن المرهون عنده مسلم والراهن فلو كان ذمياً قال في المبسوط : رهن ذمي من ذمي خمراً فصارت خلاً لا ينقص من قيمته بقدره ويبقى رهناً لأن بالتغيير من وصف المرارة إلى الحموضة نقصت المالية عندهم ومقومها مع بقاء العين بحالها وبتبدل الصفة لا يبطل الرهن كما لو كان الرهن قلباً فانكسر وبقي الوزن على حاله، ثم عندهما يتخير الراهن إن شاء افتكه بجميع الدين ،وأخذه، وإن شاء ضمنه خمراً مثل خمره فيصير البحر الرائق ٣٣٥/٨ ٥١٤ كتاب الرهن باب التصر في الرهن والجناية عليه وجنايته على غيره الخل سبب يضمن من ملكاً للمرتهن . .. وعند محمد رحمه الله تعالى إن شاء افتكه بجميع الدين وإن شاء جعله بالدين كما في مسئلة القلب إذا انكسر كما مر بيانه وقيدنا بقولنا رهن مسلم عصيراً» لأن رهن الكافر الخمر عند مسلم أو رهن المسلم الخمر عند كافر باطل قال : ارتهن المسلم من كافر خمراً فصار خلاً في الرهن باطل ويكون الخل أمانة في يده للراهن وهو بالخيار إن شاء أخذه قضاء دينه، وإن شاء يدع الخل بدينه إن كانت قيمة الخل يوم الرهن كالدين لأن المسلم يجوز أن يضمن الخمر بالرهن لأنه ضمان والمضمون متى نصب في يد الضمين يخير من له الضمان كما لو غصب المسلم خمراً من ذمي فصارت خلاً في يده يخير الذمي لأن الخمر عند أهل الذمة يصلح لمنافع ما لا يصلح له الخل ولا وجه فصار الخمر كالهالك من وجه، وليس له المرتهن خمراً مثل خمره لأن المسلم منهي عن تمليك الخمر ولا وجه أن يترك الخل عليه ويضمن النقصان لأنه يؤدي إلى الربا ولا وجه أن يأخذ الخل ويضمن الدين كله لأنه يتضرر به فقلنا بأنه يجعله بالدين ليدفع الضرر عنه وليس فيه ضرر على المرتهن فكذا هذا، فإذا وجبت قيمة الخمر للراهن على المرتهن فله عليه مثل ذلك فيلتقيان قصاصاً. ولو ارتهن الكافر خمراً من مسلم لا يجوز ويكون أمانة في يد المرتهن لأن الخمر لا يصير مضموناً على الكافر المسلم وإن قبضها بجهة الضمان كما في الغصب والإتلاف. ارتهن مسلم من مسلم عصيراً فصار خمراً فللمرتهن تخليلها وتكون رهناً، ويبطل من الدين بحساب ما نقص يعني من الكيل والوزن بقذف الزبد لأن . التخليل إحياء حق المرتهن وإصلاح الفاسد فله ذلك، وفي إبقاء العقد بعد التخمير فائدة لجواز التخليل فيبقى كالعصير إذا تخمر قبل القبض يبقى البيع فكذا هذا ، والدين يسقط بانتقاص الرهن لأنه احتبس عنده بعض الرهن ولا ينقص بانتقاص القيمة كما إذا تغير السعر وقيدنا بذكر العصير في المسلم قال وإن كان الراهن كافراً يأخذ الخمر والدين عليه وليس للمرتهن أن يخلها، فإن خللها ضمن قيمتها يوم خلل ورجع بدينه بخلاف ما لو كان الراهن مسلماً فخللها لم يضمن. والفرق أن هناك لا ضرر على الراهن في إبقاء عقد الرهن إلى ما بعد التخمير بل له فيه منفعة لأن ماله يصير متقوماً بالتخليل ولم يصر المرتهن متلفاً لماله بل إضرار بالراهن لأن لأهل رغائب في الخمر ما ليس مثلها في العصير وهو لم يرضى بكون الخمر رهناً، فلو بقينا عقد الرهن بعد تغيير ملكه في حقه يؤدي إلى الضرر به لأن الخمر بالعصير جنسان مختلفان في حق أهل الذمة وهو لم يعقد الرهن على الخمر وإنما عقد على العصير فلا يبقى العقد فيكون للراهن أخذ الخمر من المرتهن، فإن خللها يضمن قيمتها لأنه أتلف الخمر بالتخليل على الذمي لما بينا والله أعلم. رهن ذمي من ذمي جلد ميتة فدبغه المرتهن لم يكن رهناً وأخذه الراهن وأعطاه أجرة الدباغة إن كان له قيمة لأن جلد الميتة ليس بمال عند أحد فلم ينعقد العقد لفوات المحل فلا . جائزاً بحدوث المحلية من بعد كما لو رهن من مسلم خمراً فصارت خلا فإذا دبغه بشيء له قيمة بقي أثره في الجلد فيكون له على صاحب الجلد قيمة ما زاد الدباغ فيه كمن صبغ ثوب انسان الذمة يعود
Chapter of Pledge: Section on Disposition of the Pledge and Crime Upon It and Its Crime Upon Others. A section. He pledged grape juice worth ten for ten, then it became wine, then it became vinegar and it is worth ten, so it is a pledge for ten. And for the other [creditors] to reject it because it is preferring some creditors by a notional fulfillment, so it resembles preference by actual fulfillment. The commonality is the nullification of the right of other creditors. Do you not see that the deceased himself does not own that in his death illness, so likewise the one who stands in his place. If he pays their debt before they reject it, it is permissible because the impediment is removed and their right is fulfilled. If the deceased had no other creditor, the pledge is permissible by analogy to actual fulfillment. And it is sold as it was sold before the pledge, so likewise after. And if the executor pledges for a debt due to the deceased against a man, it is permissible because it is recovery, so he owns it and may sell it, and Allah knows best. His debt because it fails to follow the section. This section is like the scattered [rulings] mentioned at the ends of books, so he delayed it to make up for what he missed earlier. He (the author) said: 'He pledged grape juice worth ten for ten, then it became wine, then it became vinegar and it is worth ten, so it is a pledge for ten' meaning if he pledges grape juice with a Muslim up to its end. They said: what is a valid subject of sale in continuation is a valid subject of pledge in continuation, just as what is a valid subject of sale initially is a valid subject of pledge initially. Wine is a valid subject of sale in continuation even if not initially. I say: one could say if the basis of our mentioned issue were this limited reasoning, there would be no benefit in his saying 'then it became vinegar' in posing the issue; rather it would suffice to say 'and whoever pledges grape juice for ten then it becomes wine, it is a pledge for ten' because the mentioned reasoning would suffice to establish this general meaning. So reflect. The author of al-`Inaya said: one could say what relates to the subject, initial and continuation are the same, so why [differentiate from] that principle? And he said: it can be answered that it is so when the subject remains, and here the subject changes legally by change of description, so it fails to follow that principle. End. I say: his saying 'then it became vinegar and it is worth ten' indicates that what is considered in increase and decrease is value, but it is not so; rather what is considered is quantity because grape juice and vinegar are measured items, being either by weight or measure. In them, decrease in value does not necessitate reduction of any of that debt, as previously in the case of a broken heart; rather it necessitates an option as we mentioned, because the purpose is merely description, and loss of any description in measured items does not necessitate reduction of anything from the debt by consensus of our companions. So the ruling is that if something of the quantity is lost, an equivalent of the debt is reduced, otherwise not. And he indicated by his saying 'then it became vinegar' that the pledgee is a Muslim and the pledgor. If the pledgor were a dhimmi, it is said in al-Mabsut: a dhimmi pledged wine from a dhimmi, then it became vinegar – it does not decrease from its value proportionally and remains a pledge because by change from the description of bitterness to sourness, the monetary value decreased in their estimation, but the substance remains as is, and by change of description the pledge is not invalidated, as if the pledge were a heart that broke while the weight remained. Then according to them, the pledgor has the choice: if he wishes, he may redeem it with the full debt and take it, and if he wishes, he may guarantee wine like his wine, so it becomes... The vinegar becomes the cause for guarantee from the ownership of the pledgee. And according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him): if he wishes, he may redeem it with the full debt, and if he wishes, he may make it against the debt as in the case of the heart that broke as previously explained. And we restricted by our saying 'a Muslim pledged grape juice' because the pledge of wine by a kafir to a Muslim or the pledge of wine by a Muslim to a kafir is invalid. He said: a Muslim took wine as pledge from a kafir, then it became vinegar in the pledge – the pledge is invalid, and the vinegar is a trust in his hand for the pledgor, and he has the choice: if he wishes, he may take it as payment of his debt, and if he wishes, he may leave the vinegar for his debt if the value of the vinegar on the day of pledge equals the debt, because a Muslim is permitted to guarantee wine by pledge since it is a guarantee, and when the guaranteed thing is placed in the hand of the guarantor, the one entitled to the guarantee has the choice, just as if a Muslim seized wine from a dhimmi and it became vinegar in his hand – the dhimmi has the choice because wine for the dhimmis is suitable for benefits for which vinegar is not suitable, and there is no way, so wine became like destroyed in one sense. And he does not have wine like his wine because the Muslim is forbidden from making wine property, and there is no way to leave the vinegar on it and guarantee the decrease because it leads to usury, and there is no way to take the vinegar and guarantee the full debt because it harms him. So we said he makes it against the debt to remove harm from him, and there is no harm on the pledgee, so likewise this. So when the value of the wine becomes due to the pledgor on the pledgee, he has similar against him, so they offset. If the kafir took wine as pledge from a Muslim, it is invalid, and it is a trust in the hand of the pledgee because wine does not become guaranteed against the Muslim kafir even if he takes it by the way of guarantee, as in usurpation and destruction. A Muslim pledged grape juice from a Muslim, then it became wine – the pledgee may turn it into vinegar, and it remains a pledge, and the debt is reduced by the amount of what decreased in terms of measure/weight by throwing out the foam because turning into vinegar is reviving the right of the pledgee and repairing what is corrupt, so he has that right. And there is benefit in keeping the contract after fermentation for the permissibility of turning into vinegar, so it remains like grape juice that fermented before taking possession – the sale remains, so likewise this. The debt is reduced by the decrease of the pledge because some of the pledge is detained with him, and it does not decrease by decrease of value as when the price changes. And we restricted by mentioning grape juice in the Muslim. He said: if the pledgor is a kafir, he takes the wine and the debt remains upon him, and the pledgee may not turn it into vinegar. If he turns it into vinegar, he guarantees its value on the day he turned it and returns to his debt, unlike if the pledgor were Muslim and he turned it into vinegar – he does not guarantee. The difference is that there is no harm on the pledgor in keeping the pledge contract after fermentation; rather he has benefit because his property becomes valuable by turning into vinegar, and the pledgee did not become a destroyer of his property, but harm to the pledgor because the people have desires in wine that are not like in grape juice, and he did not consent to the wine being a pledge. If we kept the pledge contract after changing his property in his right, it leads to harm to him because wine and grape juice are two different types in the right of the dhimmis, and he did not contract the pledge on wine, but on grape juice, so the contract does not remain. So the pledgor may take the wine from the pledgee. If he turns it into vinegar, he guarantees its value because he destroyed the wine by turning to vinegar upon the dhimmi as we explained, and Allah knows best. A dhimmi pledged a dead animal skin from a dhimmi, then the pledgee tanned it – it is not a pledge, and the pledgor takes it and gives him the wage of tanning if it has value, because the skin of a dead animal is not property for anyone, so the contract did not conclude due to lack of subject. It does not become valid by subsequent acquisition of subject, as if he pledged wine from a Muslim and it became vinegar. So if he tanned it with something of value, its effect remains in the skin, so he has upon the owner of the skin the value of what the tanning increased, like one who dyed the garment of a person.. the dhimma returns.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the rulings regarding changes in the state of a pledged item and cross-religious pledges. It begins with the main ruling: if grape juice worth ten is pledged for ten, then becomes wine, then vinegar, it remains a pledge for ten. The commentator explains that the key is whether the item is a valid subject of sale in continuation; wine is valid for sale after fermentation. A subtle point is raised: the consideration for increase/decrease is quantity (measure/weight), not value, because grape juice and vinegar are measured items. The passage then discusses several scenarios: (1) a dhimmi pledging wine to a dhimmi – if it becomes vinegar, the pledge remains, but the pledgor has options; (2) a Muslim taking wine as pledge from a kafir – the pledge is invalid, and the vinegar is a trust; (3) a kafir taking wine from a Muslim – invalid; (4) a Muslim pledging grape juice to a Muslim – if it becomes wine, the pledgee may turn it to vinegar, and the debt reduces by the quantity loss; (5) a dhimmi pledging a dead animal skin – the pledge is invalid even if tanned, but the tanner gets compensation. Throughout, the commentator uses qiyas and istihsan, distinguishing between cases based on the religious status of the parties and the nature of the items.

Key Terms
عصير (asir): Grape juice, a valuable property subject to pledge.
خمر (khamr): Wine; an alcoholic beverage made from grape juice, considered non-property (ghayr mutaqawwim) for Muslims but property for dhimmis.
خل (khal): Vinegar, produced from wine; becomes a valuable property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim pledges grape juice worth ten and it becomes wine then vinegar worth ten, what is the status of the pledge?
A) The pledge becomes void because wine is not a valid subject.
B) The pledge remains valid for the full ten.
C) The pledge remains valid but the debt reduces to the vinegar's market value.
D) The pledge becomes a trust in the pledgee's hands.

Key Takeaway
A pledge remains valid upon change of description if the substance remains; debt is reduced only by loss of quantity, not value.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Dhimmi Pledge of Wine and Its Transformation – Options and Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on options for dhimmi pledged wine that becomes vinegar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a dhimmi pledging wine to a dhimmi that becomes vinegar, and identify the options available to the pledgor and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
When a dhimmi pledges wine that becomes vinegar, the pledge remains valid; the pledgor may either redeem it or claim compensation, with disagreement among the imams.

This lesson shifts to the scenario of a dhimmi pledging wine to another dhimmi. The wine becomes vinegar, reducing its value in the estimation of dhimmis (who value wine more than vinegar). The Hanafi school rules that the pledge remains valid because the substance remains, but the pledgor is given a choice to either redeem the pledge with the full debt or demand compensation. There is a known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the exact options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and subject
Both pledgor and pledgee are dhimmis; the subject is wine (khamr) which is property (mal) for them. The wine turns into vinegar.
Dhimmis own wine, and it is a valid property for them.
2
State the ruling on validity
The pledge remains valid because the substance (al-ayn) remains; only the description changed. This is analogous to a broken heart (qalb munakassir) where the weight remains.
Value decrease does not affect validity.
3
Identify the pledgor's options at the two disciples (عندهما)
According to Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's initial view (عندهما), the pledgor has two choices: redeem the pledge by paying the full debt and take the vinegar, or demand wine similar to the pledged wine (i.e., compensation in kind).
This is based on the analogy to a broken heart.
4
Identify Muhammad's separate view
Muhammad al-Shaybani has a third view: the pledgor may also choose to make the vinegar itself the satisfaction of the debt (i.e., keep it as full payment).
This differs from the two disciples' view.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf)
The difference lies in whether the pledgor can force the pledgee to accept vinegar as full payment for the debt, or only as a redemption subject to additional compensation.
The text does not explicitly give tarjih, but the common view follows the two disciples.

حقهم، ولو لم يكن للميت غريم آخر جاز الرهن اعتباراً بالإيفاء الحقيقي وبيع في يباع فيه قبل الرهن فكذا بعده، وإذا ارتهن الوصي بدين للميت على رجل جاز لأنه استيفاء فيملكه وله أن يبيعه والله أعلم. دينه لأنه تخلف عن فصل هذا الفصل بمنزلة المتفرقة المذكورة في أواخر الكتب فلذا أخره استدراكاً لما فاته فيما سبق . قال رحمه الله : رهن عصيراً قيمته عشرة بعشرة فتخمر ثم تخلل وهو يساوي عشرة فهو رهن بعشرة) يعني إذا رهن عند مسلم عصيراً إلى آخرها قالوا ما كان محلاً للبيع بقاء يكون محلاً للرهن بقاء كما أن ما يكون محلاً للبيع ابتداء يكون محلاً للرهن ابتداء والخمر محل للبيع بقاء وإن لم يكن محلاً له ابتداء ، أقول :
